Hudud — Fixed Penalties
beginner
6 min
The Definition and Structure of Hadd Punishments
Introduces the Book of Hadd, defining hadd and its conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define hadd technically, distinguish it from ta'zir and qisas, and identify its rukn, sharṭ, sabab, and ḥikmah.

Core Idea
Hadd is a fixed punishment from Allah; its rukn is execution by the ruler, and it requires a sane, healthy offender.

This passage opens the Book of Hadd in Kanz al-Daqa'iq, providing the linguistic and technical definition of hadd. It then proceeds to outline the structural components of hadd: its rukn, sharṭ, sabab, and ḥikmah. Understanding these categories is essential for correctly applying hadd punishments and distinguishing them from other penal categories like ta'zir and qisas.

Guided Path
1
Define hadd linguistically and technically
Identify the linguistic meaning (prevention) and the technical meaning (fixed punishment from Allah). Note how the technical meaning builds on the linguistic.
The term 'hadd' is used in Quran like 'hudud Allah'.
2
Distinguish hadd from ta'zir and qisas
Compare the three: hadd is fixed (muqaddara) by Allah; ta'zir is unfixed, delegated to judge; qisas is a right of the victim, not a fixed punishment from Allah alone.
The text explicitly uses 'muqaddara Allah' to exclude qisas.
3
Identify the rukn, sharṭ, sabab, and ḥikmah of hadd
Rukn: implementation by Imam or his deputy. Sharṭ: offender must be of sound mind and body. Sabab: committing a major sin like zina, qadhf, or shurb al-khamr. Ḥikmah: deterrence.
These are the four terms used in Hanafi fiqh for any legal ruling.
4
Apply the conditions to determine when hadd is postponed
If the offender is insane, intoxicated, sick, or weak-bodied, hadd is postponed until recovery. This shows the sharṭ in action.
This is a practical consequence of the condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحدود: [وهو جمع حد وهو المنع لغة ومنه سمي البواب حداداً لمنعه الناس عن الدخول والخروج. (رمز الحقائق: ۳۷۷/۱)] ... الحد: عقوبة مقدرة الله تعالى، ... والزنا أي في الشرع أي معينة ومقدرة أي الموجب للحد ... وقيد بقوله: 'مقدرة' احترازا عن التعزير فإنه عقوبة غير مقدرة شرعاً، وتقديره مفوض إلى رأي الحاكم، وقيد بقوله: 'مقدرة الله تعالى' احترازاً عن القصاص، فإنه شرع لشفاء الصدور، وهو حق العباد، والتقديرات على أربعة أنواع منها: ما هو لمنع الزيادة والنقصان وهو الحدود، ومنها ما ليس بمنع الزيادة والنقصان ... وركن الحد إقامة الإمام أو نائبه وشرطه كون من يقام عليه من أهل الاعتبار سليم البدن فلا يقام على مجنون، وسكران ولا على مريض وضعيف الخلقة إلا بعد الصحة، وسببه ارتکاب كبيرة من زنا أو قذف أو شرب خمر وحكمته: انزجار من يقام عليه. ... والزنا: وطء الرجل في قبل خال عن ملك وشبهته.
Book of Hadd: [It is the plural of 'hadd' which linguistically means prevention; from this the gatekeeper is called 'haddad' because he prevents people from entering and exiting. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/377)] ... Hadd: A punishment determined by Allah Almighty. ... And zina in the Sharia: a specific and determined [punishment]... and the restriction by his statement 'determined' (muqaddara) excludes ta'zir, for it is a punishment not determined by Sharia; its determination is delegated to the judge's opinion. The restriction by 'determined by Allah Almighty' excludes qisas, for it is prescribed to heal the hearts and is a right of the servants. The determinations are of four types: among them is what prevents increase and decrease, which is hudud; among them is what does not prevent increase and decrease... The rukn of hadd is implementation by the Imam or his deputy; its condition is that the person on whom it is carried out is of sound mind and body, so it is not carried out on a lunatic, an intoxicated person, nor on a sick person or weak-bodied except after recovery; its cause is committing a major sin like zina, qadhf, or drinking wine; its wisdom is deterrence of the person on whom it is carried out. ... And zina: the man's penetration of the front passage devoid of ownership and its doubt.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Hadd with a linguistic and technical definition. 'Hadd' linguistically means prevention, and technically it is a fixed punishment prescribed by Allah, distinguished from ta'zir (discretionary punishment) and qisas (retaliation). The text then explains the structure of hadd using the terms rukn (pillar), sharṭ (condition), sabab (cause), and ḥikmah (wisdom). The rukn is the execution by the imam or his deputy. The shart is that the offender must be of sound mind and body; thus hadd is not applied to a lunatic, drunkard, sick person, or weak-bodied person until they recover. The sabab is committing a grave sin like zina, qadhf (false accusation of zina), or shurb al-khamr (drinking wine). The hikmah is deterrence. Then the text defines zina specifically as the man's penetration of the front private part (vulva) of a woman who is not his wife or slave, and without any doubt regarding ownership (shubhah). This excludes bestiality, homosexuality, and acts with minors. The definition also requires penetration beyond the circumcised area, as mixing (mukhalata) occurs with that. The passage also mentions that hadd punishes major sins (kaba'ir), but the Qur'an and sunnah specify the three mentioned.

Key Terms
الحد (al-ḥadd): A fixed punishment (muqaddarah) from Allah, distinct from ta'zir and qisas.
التعزير (al-taʿzīr): Discretionary punishment not fixed by Sharia, determined by the judge.
القصاص (al-qisās): Retaliation (eye for an eye), a right of the victim/guardians, not a fixed hadd.
الركن (al-rukn): The essential component of the hadd: its execution by the ruler.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the rukn (pillar) of hadd?
A) The offender's confession
B) The judge's verdict
C) Implementation by the Imam or his deputy
D) The crime committed

Key Takeaway
Hadd is defined by its fixed nature (muqaddara) and its structural components: rukn (execution), sharṭ (sanity/health), sabab (major sin), and ḥikmah (deterrence).

Definition of Hadd and Zina
Defines hadd and zina with conditions and types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of hadd and zina, identify the conditions that exclude an act from being zina, and explain why liwat is not considered zina in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Zina is only vaginal intercourse free from ownership and doubt; liwat and other acts are separate crimes with different rulings.

This lesson opens the Book of Hudud with the foundational definitions of hadd and zina. Understanding these precise definitions is critical because they determine when the fixed punishment (hadd) applies. The Hanafi school rigorously distinguishes zina from other unlawful sexual acts, each with its own legal consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its linguistic root
The word 'hadd' linguistically means prevention; hence a doorkeeper is called 'haddad'. Recognize that the legal meaning builds on this concept of prevention.
This linguistic foundation helps understand the purpose of hudud: to prevent crimes.
2
Distinguish hadd from ta'zir and qisas
Hadd is a fixed punishment determined by Allah; ta'zir is discretionary and left to the judge; qisas is retaliation as a right of the victim. Note the key qualifiers in the text: 'muqaddara' (determined) excludes ta'zir, and 'muqaddara Allah ta'ala' excludes qisas.
This distinction is essential for classifying punishments and their evidentiary requirements.
3
Analyze the elements of hadd: pillar, condition, cause, wisdom
The pillar (rukn) is establishment by the Imam or his deputy. The condition (shart) is that the person must be mukallaf and sound of body. The cause (sabab) is committing a major sin like zina, qadhf, or drinking wine. The wisdom (hikma) is deterrence.
These elements are not all part of the definition but explain when and why hadd is applied.
4
Break down the definition of zina
Zina is defined as 'intercourse in the front, free from ownership and doubt of ownership'. Analyze each part: 'front' excludes liwat (anal intercourse); 'intercourse' excludes the act of a minor or one compelled; 'free from ownership' excludes lawful intercourse with wife or slave; 'free from doubt' excludes cases with contractual irregularities or apparent ownership.
Pay attention to the exceptions: intercourse with a corpse, animal, or prepubescent girl not desired also excluded.
5
Understand the requirement for penetration
The hadd requires that the glans (circumcision site) fully enters the vagina; anything less is only touching and does not trigger the full rulings of intercourse, including ghusl, expiation, etc.
This is a key Hanafi condition for establishing zina.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحدود
الحد: عقوبة مقدرة الله تعالى، والزنا أي في الشرع أي معينة ومقدرة أي الموجب للحد
كتاب الحدود: [وهو جمع حد وهو المنع لغة ومنه سمي البواب حداداً لمنعه الناس عن الدخول والخروج. (رمز الحقائق: ۳۷۷/۱)] المناسبة بين الكتابين: الأيمان والحدود أن الحدود سبب للامتناع كما أن الأيمان سبب له إن كان الحلف على نفي الفعل، والحدود عقوبات بعضها حق الله خالصاً كحد الزنا والخمر، وبعضها مشوب بحق العباد كحد القذف، فابتدأ بالأول وقدم الأقوى منهما. (فتح)
غد،
الحد إلخ: الفرق بين العقاب والعقوبة أن ما يلحق الإنسان من الألم في الجناية إن كان في الآخرة يقال له: العقاب، وإن كان في الدنيا يقال له العقوبة، وركن الحد إقامة الإمام أو نائبه وشرطه كون من يقام عليه من أهل الاعتبار سليم البدن فلا يقام على مجنون، وسكران ولا على مريض وضعيف الخلقة إلا بعد الصحة، وسببه ارتکاب كبيرة من زنا أو قذف أو شرب خمر وحكمته: انزجار من يقام عليه. وقيد بقوله: "مقدرة" احترازا عن التعزير فإنه عقوبة غير مقدرة شرعاً، وتقديره مفوض إلى رأي الحاكم، وقيد بقوله: "مقدرة الله تعالى" احترازاً عن القصاص، فإنه شرع لشفاء الصدور، وهو حق العباد، والتقديرات على أربعة أنواع منها: ما هو لمنع الزيادة والنقصان وهو الحدود، ومنها ما ليس بمنع الزيادة والنقصان كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا تَدْرِي نَفْسٌ مَاذَا تَكْسِبُ غَدًا﴾ (لقمان: ٣٤)، فإنها لا تعلم ماذا تكسب في هذا اليوم في الزمان الثاني، ولا في بعد ومنها: ما هو لمنع الزيادة دون النقصان، وهو خيار الشرط عند الإمام، ومنها ما هو لمنع النقصان دون الزيادة كمدة السفر. (مستخلص فتح عقوبة : هي الألم الذي يلحق الإنسان مستحقاً على الجناية. (ف) الله متعلق بمحذوف أي تجب حقاً الله تعالى (عيني) والزنا إلخ الزنا بالقصر في لغة أهل الحجاز التي جاء بها القرآن قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَلا تَقْرَبُوا الزِّنَى﴾ (الإسراء: ۳۲)، فيكتب بالياء، وبالمد في لغة أهل نجد فيكتب بالألف وإنما بدأ بالكلام عليه؛ لكثرته مع ثبوت حده بالقطعي، وقيد بقوله: "وطء" في "قبل احترازاً . عن اللواطة، والمراد وطء الرجل ليخرج فعل الصبي، وقوله: "خال عن ملك" احتراز عن وطء المنكوحة والمملوكة، فإنه ليس بزنا، وكذا احتراز عن وطء امرأته الحائض أو أمته الحائض، وقوله: "وشبهته" أي خال عن شبهة ملك النكاح فيما إذا تزوج رجل امرأة بغير شهود أو أمة بغير إذن مولاها، وخال عن شبهة ملك اليمين فيما إذا وطئ الرجل جارية ابنه أو جارية مكاتبه أو عبده المأذون المديون، فلا يتعلق بوطء المجنون والصبي والمكره ووطء غير المشتهاة كالصغيرة التي لم تبلغ حد التشهي والميتة والبهائم، وإنما قيد بالخلو عن الملك؛ لأن الوطء فيه مباح وأما اشتراط عدم الشبهة؛ فلقوله عليه: "ادرءوا الحدود بالشبهات ما استطعتم" ولابد في الوطء من مجاوزة الختان؛ لأن المخالطة تتحقق بذلك، وما دونه ملامسة لا تتعلق بها أحكام الوطء من الغسل وكفارة الصوم وفساد الحج وثبوت الرجعة وغيرها. (مستخلص، فتح)
الحد
The Book of Hudud. Hadd: a punishment determined by Allah the Exalted, and zina in the Sacred Law i.e. specific and determined, i.e. that which necessitates the hadd. The Book of Hudud: [It is the plural of hadd, which linguistically means prevention; hence the doorkeeper is called haddad because he prevents people from entering and exiting. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 377/1)] The connection between the two books: oaths and hudud, that hudud are a cause of abstention just as oaths are a cause of it if the oath is upon denial of an action, and hudud are punishments, some of which are purely the right of Allah like the hadd of zina and wine, and some are mixed with the right of servants like the hadd of qadhf. So he began with the first and presented the stronger of the two. (Fath). Hadd etc.: The difference between 'iqab and 'uqubah is that the pain that befalls a person due to a crime—if in the Hereafter it is called 'iqab, and if in this world it is called 'uqubah. The pillar of hadd is its establishment by the Imam or his deputy. Its condition is that the person upon whom it is established must be accountable and sound of body, so it is not established upon a madman, an intoxicated person, a sick person, or one of weak constitution except after recovery. Its cause is committing a major sin of zina, qadhf, or drinking wine. Its wisdom is deterrence of the person upon whom it is established. He restricted with his saying 'determined' to exclude ta'zir, for it is a punishment not determined by the Sacred Law, and its determination is delegated to the judge's opinion. He restricted with 'determined by Allah the Exalted' to exclude qisas, for it is legislated to soothe the hearts and it is the right of servants. Determinations are of four types: that which prevents increase and decrease—these are the hudud; that which does not prevent increase or decrease—as Allah said: 'And no soul knows what it will earn tomorrow' (Luqman:34), for it does not know what it will earn on this day in the second time, nor later; that which prevents increase but not decrease—which is the option of condition according to Imam [Abu Hanifa]; and that which prevents decrease but not increase—like the duration of travel. (Mustakhlas Fath: 'Uqubah is the pain that befalls a person justly due to the crime. (F) 'Allah' is attached to an omitted word, i.e., it is obligatory as a right of Allah the Exalted (Ayni). And zina etc.: Zina is shortened in the language of the Hijaz, with which the Quran came. Allah said: 'And do not approach zina' (al-Isra':32), so it is written with ya', and with elongation in the language of Najd, written with alif. He began speaking about it because of its frequency and that its hadd is established by definitive evidence. He restricted with 'intercourse' in 'front' to exclude liwat. The meaning is the intercourse of a man to exclude the act of a boy. His saying 'free from ownership' excludes intercourse with a married woman or a female slave, for that is not zina. Similarly, it excludes intercourse with his menstruating wife or his menstruating slave woman. His saying 'and its doubt' i.e., free from doubt of ownership of marriage in the case where a man marries a woman without witnesses or a slave woman without the permission of her master, and free from doubt of ownership of right hand in the case where a man has intercourse with his son's slave girl, or his mukatib's slave girl, or his indebted authorized slave. So it does not apply to intercourse by a madman, a boy, one compelled, intercourse with one who is not desired like a young girl who has not reached the age of desire, a corpse, or animals. He restricted with 'free from ownership' because intercourse therein is permissible. As for stipulating absence of doubt, due to his عليه saying: 'Ward off the hudud with doubts as much as you can.' It is necessary in intercourse to exceed the circumcision site because mixing is realized by that; anything less is mere touching to which the rulings of intercourse do not attach regarding ghusl, expiation of fasting, invalidation of hajj, establishment of ruj'a, and others. (Mustakhlas, Fath). Hadd.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage is a definition and expansion on the opening of the Book of Hudud. It defines hadd as a fixed punishment determined by Allah, distinguishing it from ta'zir (discretionary punishment) and qisas (retaliation). The author explains the linguistic meaning of hadd as 'prevention' and notes the connection between the book of oaths and hudud. The passage then details the pillar, condition, cause, and wisdom of hadd. It clarifies that hadd is only for major sins like zina, qadhf, and drinking wine. The definition of zina is then given: it is sexual intercourse in the front (vaginal) that is free from ownership and doubt of ownership. The commentator expands on each part: 'front' excludes sodomy; 'intercourse' excludes the act of a minor; 'free from ownership' excludes lawful intercourse with one's wife or slave; 'free from doubt' excludes cases with a contractual defect or apparent ownership. The necessity of penetration beyond the circumcision site is emphasized because full mixing is required. This follows the Hanafi position that hadd is established only when there is clear unlawful intercourse without any mitigating factor.

Key Terms
الحد (al-hadd): A fixed punishment determined by Allah for specific crimes like zina, qadhf, and drinking wine.
التعزير (al-ta'zir): A discretionary punishment not fixed by Shari'a, left to the judge's opinion.
الزنا (al-zina): Unlawful sexual intercourse (vaginal) by a mukallaf person, free from ownership and doubt of ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is excluded from the definition of zina according to the passage?
A) Intercourse with a wife without witnesses to the marriage
B) Intercourse with a female slave owned by the man
C) Intercourse with a corpse
D) Intercourse with a woman in her menses

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of zina is precise: only vaginal intercourse free from ownership and doubt qualifies; all other unlawful sexual acts are separate offenses.

Proof of Zina by Four Witnesses
Explains the requirement of four witnesses for zina, the necessary wording, and the judge's fivefold questioning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for proving zina and apply them to evaluate the validity of witness testimony.

Core Idea
Zina is proven only by four male witnesses using the word 'zina' in one session; otherwise the accusers are punished.

The Hanafi school imposes strict evidentiary requirements for the crime of zina, reflecting the Quranic emphasis on concealment and certainty. This lesson examines the conditions under which testimony is accepted, the specific word required, and the judge's fivefold interrogation. Understanding these rules is essential to avoid wrongful punishment and to uphold the hadd system.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal act and its proof requirement
Determine what act is being proven (zina) and what the general proof mechanism is: testimony of four male witnesses using the word 'zina'.
The act of zina is defined as full vaginal penetration (al-mil fi al-mikhalah).
2
Locate the textual evidence
Identify the Quranic verses (an-Nisa:15, an-Nur:4) and the hadith of Ma'iz that establish the requirement.
The imperative 'istashhidu' and the negation 'lam ya'tu' set the number and condition.
3
Understand the specific conditions
List the conditions: four males, word 'zina', unity of session, witnesses must be 'adl, and the judge's fivefold questioning.
Why the word 'zina'? It directly indicates the forbidden act; 'intercourse' is ambiguous.
4
Examine the judge's interrogation
Review the five questions: mahiyya (essence), kayfiyya (manner), makan (place), zaman (time), mar'iyya (woman). Each eliminates a potential doubt that would avert hadd.
The Prophet interrogated Ma'iz in this manner; it is a procedural safeguard.
5
Note the inter-madhhab difference
Contrast the Hanafi requirement of unity of session with the Shafi'i position allowing separate testimony.
The practical consequence: separate testimony leads to qadhf penalty for the witnesses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويثبت بشهادة أربعة بالزنا، لا بالوطء أي ملك يمين ونكاح أي خال عن شبهة الملك والجماع، فيسألهم الإمام عن ماهيّته وكيفيته ومكانه وزمانه والمزنية، فإن بينوه،
أو القاضي بعد شهادتهم
وطء: أي وطء المكلف الطالع الناطق ولو ذمياً في دارنا. (ط) عيني) ويثبت بشهادة أربعة: أي يثبت الزنا عند الحاكم بشهادة أربعة رجال يشهدون بلفظ الزنا؛ لأنه هو الدال على الفعل الحرام، ولا يشهدون بالوطء والجماع؛ لأنهما لا يدلان على الحرام، ولأن فيهما احتمال، فلعله وطئها فيما دون الفرج أو جامعها كذلك، واشتراط الأربعة بالنص، وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿فَاسْتَشْهِدُوا عَلَيْهِنَّ أَرْبَعَةً مِنْكُمْ ﴾ (النساء:١٥)، وبقوله تعالى: ﴿ثُمَّ لَمْ يَأْتُوا بِأَرْبَعَةِ شُهَدَاءَ (النور:٤)، وبقوله عليا للذي قذف زوجته: "ايت بأربعة شهداء يشهدون على صدق مقالتك" ولأن في اشتراط الأربعة يتحقق معنى الستر، وهو مندوب إليه، فلا يثبت بعلم القاضي، ولا بشهادة أقل العدد من المذكور، ولا بشهادة النساء واتحاد المجلس شرط لصحة الشهادة بالزنا عندنا، حتى لو شهدوا متفرقين واحداً بعد واحد لا تقبل شهادتهم، ويحدون حد القذف خلافاً للشافعي. (مستخلص، مسكين، عيني) لا بالوطء: أي لا يثبت بلفظ الوطء والجماع؛ لأنهما لا يدلان على ذلك. (ط) فيسألهم الإمام: أي إذا شهد الشهود يسألهم الإمام عن خمسة أشياء: الأول: عن ماهية الزنا، والمراد منه السؤال عن ذاته أي حقيقته الشرعية، وهي إدخال الفرج في الفرج كما أشار إليه المصنف بقوله : "الزنا وطء في قبل، والغرض من هذا السؤال أن من الناس من يزعم أن كل وطء حرام فهو، زنا، وليس كذلك، فإن مماسة الفرجين ،حرام، ولا يجب الحد بغير الإيلاج، وكذا الوطء في الفخذ وغيره فلهذا الاحتمال يسأله عن الزنا ما هو . الثاني: يسأل عن كيفيته بأن يقول: كيف زنى إكراها أو طوعاً؛ لأنه إذا كان بإكراه لا يجب الحد، والثالث: يسأل عن مكان الزنا بأن يقول: أين زنى؛ لاحتمال أن يكون في دار الحرب أو في عسكر أهل البغي، فلا يجب الحد، والرابع: يسأل عن زمانه بأن يقول متى زنى؛ لاحتمال تقادم عهد الزنا، أو في حال الصبا أو الجنون، فلا يجب الحد والخامس يسأل عن المزنية بأن يقول : من زنى؛ لاحتمال أنه زنى بجارية ابنه، أو بمن له فيها ملك أو شبهة لا يقف عليها الشهود، فلا يجب عليه الحد، ووجه السؤال عن هذه الأشياء الخمسة؛ لأن النبي عليا استفسر ماعزاً على هذا التفصيل. (مستخلص، فتح) فإن بينوه: [ أي إن بين الشهود الزنا بعد سؤال الحاكم على الوجه المذكور. (عيني)] القياس يقتضي جمع الضمير لعودها إلى الوجوه التي دفع السؤال عنها من الماهية ،ومعطوفاتها، لكنه أفرد الضمير ليرجع إلى المذكور، وذكر بكلمة "إن" وهي تذكر في أمر غير كائن؛ لأنه قل ما يثبت الزنا بالبينة، وقوله: "كالميل في المكحلة" الميل الخشبة التي يكحل بها الكحل، والمكحلة بضمتين يعني الميم والحاء وعاء الكحل، وقوله: "عدلوا سراً وجهراً" والتعديل سراً: أن يبعث القاضي ورقة فيها أسماء الشهود وأسماء محلتهم على وجه يتميز كل منهم لمن يعرفهم، =
And it is established by testimony of four [witnesses] with [the word] 'zina', not by [the word] 'intercourse' i.e., [saying] 'ownership of right hand' and 'marriage', i.e., free from doubt of ownership and intercourse. So the Imam asks them about its quiddity, its manner, its place, its time, and the woman with whom zina was committed. If they explain it, or the judge after their testimony. 'Intercourse': i.e., intercourse of the mukallaf adult speaking male, even if a dhimmi in our abode. (T, Ayni). 'And it is established by testimony of four': i.e., zina is established before the judge by testimony of four men who testify using the word 'zina', because it is what indicates the forbidden act. They do not testify using the word 'intercourse' and 'copulation' because they do not indicate the forbidden [nature], and because they involve probability, perhaps he had intercourse with her below the private part or copulated thus. And the stipulation of four is by the text, which is His saying: 'And call to witness from among you four witnesses' (an-Nisa:15), and His saying: 'Then they did not produce four witnesses' (an-Nur:4), and his statement to the one who accused his wife: 'Bring four witnesses who testify to the truth of your statement.' And because in stipulating four the meaning of concealment is realized, and it is recommended. So it is not established by the judge's knowledge, nor by testimony of less than the mentioned number, nor by testimony of women. And the unity of the session is a condition for the validity of testimony in zina according to us, such that if they testify separately one after another their testimony is not accepted, and they are punished with the hadd of qadhf, contrary to al-Shafi'i. (Mustakhlas, Miskin, Ayni). 'Not by intercourse': i.e., it is not established by the word 'intercourse' and 'copulation' because they do not indicate that. (T). 'So the Imam asks them': i.e., when the witnesses testify, the Imam asks them about five things: first, about the quiddity of zina, meaning the question about its essence i.e., its legal reality, which is inserting the male organ into the female private part, as the author indicated by his saying: 'Zina is intercourse in the front.' The purpose of this question is that some people claim that every unlawful intercourse is zina, but it is not so. For mere touching of the private parts is forbidden, but hadd is not obligatory without insertion. Similarly, intercourse on the thigh or elsewhere. For this possibility he asks about what zina is. Second, he asks about its manner, saying: How did he commit zina? Under compulsion or voluntarily? Because if under compulsion, hadd is not obligatory. Third, he asks about the place of zina, saying: Where did he commit zina? Because of the possibility that it occurred in a war territory or in the camp of rebellious people, so hadd is not obligatory. Fourth, he asks about its time, saying: When did he commit zina? Because of the possibility that the time of zina is long past, or that it occurred during childhood or insanity, so hadd is not obligatory. Fifth, he asks about the woman with whom zina was committed, saying: With whom did he commit zina? Because of the possibility that he committed zina with his son's slave girl, or with one in whom he has ownership or doubt, which the witnesses are not aware of, so hadd is not obligatory upon him. The reason for questioning about these five things is that the Prophet عليه interrogated Ma'iz in this detail. (Mustakhlas, Fath). 'If they explain it': [i.e., if the witnesses explain the zina after the judge's questioning in the mentioned manner. (Ayni)] The rule of analogy requires the pronoun to be plural to refer to the matters about which the question was raised, i.e., the quiddity and its conjunctions. But he used the singular pronoun to refer back to the mentioned [zina]. He used the word 'in' which is used for a matter that is non-existent because rarely is zina established by evidence. And his saying: 'like the kohl stick in the kohl container' – al-mil is the stick used to apply kohl, and al-mikhalah (with damm on the mim and ha') is the container of kohl. And his saying: 'they established integrity secretly and publicly' – and the secret establishment of integrity is that the judge sends a paper containing the names of the witnesses and the names of their locality in a way that each of them is distinguished to those who know them, =
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage expands on the ruling that zina is proven only by the testimony of four male witnesses who explicitly use the word 'zina'. The author explains that the witnesses must testify with the word 'zina' because it directly indicates the forbidden act, unlike 'intercourse' or 'copulation' which are ambiguous. The requirement of four witnesses is derived from the Quran (al-Nisa:15, al-Nur:4) and the hadith of the Prophet. The passage also details that the judge must question the witnesses about five specific aspects: the essence of zina (to confirm it is vaginal penetration), its manner (voluntary or coerced), its place (dar al-harb or dar al-Islam), its time (prescription, childhood, insanity), and the identity of the woman (to rule out ownership or doubt). This questioning follows the precedent of the Prophet's interrogation of Ma'iz. The commentary emphasizes that unity of the session is a condition for accepting testimony; if witnesses testify separately, they are not accepted and instead punished for qadhf. The analogy of the kohl stick and container illustrates the degree of penetration required. The final part mentions the procedure for verifying the witnesses' integrity (tazkiyah) both secretly and publicly.

Key Terms
الشهادة (al-shahada): Testimony given in court, specifically for zina it must be by four men using the word 'zina'.
الميل في المكحلة (al-mil fi al-mikhalah): Analogy for the degree of penetration required for hadd: like a kohl stick entering its container; full insertion.
التعديل (al-ta'dil): The process of establishing the integrity ('adalah) of witnesses, done secretly and publicly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Their testimony is accepted if they all agree
B) Their testimony is rejected and they are punished for qadhf
C) The judge asks them to repeat together
D) Only two witnesses are needed if they are reliable

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires four male witnesses testifying in unity using the word 'zina' for the hadd of zina to be established, with detailed judicial interrogation to eliminate all doubts.

Proving Zina: Four Witnesses and the Judge's Inquiry
Explains how zina is proven by four witnesses and the judge's questioning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid testimony in a zina case and explain the purpose of the judge's five questions.

Core Idea
Zina is proven only by four male witnesses in one sitting; the judge must inquire into every detail to avoid executing the hadd.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq details the rigorous procedure for proving zina. The Hanafi school imposes strict conditions on the testimony to protect against wrongful punishment. The judge is not merely a passive receiver of testimony; he actively interrogates the witnesses on five specifics to ensure the case meets the legal definition of zina.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal definition of zina
Determine that zina is only penis-in-vagina intercourse, free from ownership or semblance. This definition excludes other sexual acts from hadd.
The witnesses must understand this definition; the judge tests their knowledge.
2
Determine the witness requirements
Four male witnesses, using the word 'zina', testifying together in one sitting. Note the dispute with Shafi'i on separate testimony.
If they say 'intercourse' (wat'), it is insufficient; likewise, if they testify separately, it is rejected.
3
Outline the judge's five questions
Ask about essence (haliyyah), force/volition, place, time, and woman. Each question addresses a potential defense (dar' al-hadd).
The questions follow the precedent of the Prophet ﷺ with Ma'iz.
4
Understand the tazkiyah process
Probity must be verified secretly (by written inquiry) and openly (by confrontation). The judge cannot rely on his own knowledge.
This ensures maximum caution before executing the hadd.
5
Apply the principle of caution (ihtiyat)
The entire procedure is designed to avoid implementing the hadd unless absolutely certain. Any doubt (shubha) averts the punishment.
The Hanafi school is particularly strict in hudud to safeguard against error.

Source Text

كتاب الحدود

شرائط الحد وأحكامها

وطء في قبل خال عن ملك وشبهته، ويثبت بشهادة أربعة بالزنا، لا بالوطء أي ملك يمين ونكاح أي خال عن شبهة الملك والجماع، فيسألهم الإمام عن ماهيّته وكيفيته ومكانه وزمانه والمزنية، فإن بينوه،
أو القاضي بعد شهادتهم
وطء: أي وطء المكلف الطالع الناطق ولو ذمياً في دارنا. (ط) عيني) ويثبت بشهادة أربعة: أي يثبت الزنا عند الحاكم بشهادة أربعة رجال يشهدون بلفظ الزنا؛ لأنه هو الدال على الفعل الحرام، ولا يشهدون بالوطء والجماع؛ لأنهما لا يدلان على الحرام، ولأن فيهما احتمال، فلعله وطئها فيما دون الفرج أو جامعها كذلك، واشتراط الأربعة بالنص، وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿فَاسْتَشْهِدُوا عَلَيْهِنَّ أَرْبَعَةً مِنْكُمْ ﴾ (النساء:١٥)، وبقوله تعالى: ﴿ثُمَّ لَمْ يَأْتُوا بِأَرْبَعَةِ شُهَدَاءَ (النور:٤)، وبقوله عليا للذي قذف زوجته: "ايت بأربعة شهداء يشهدون على صدق مقالتك" ولأن في اشتراط الأربعة يتحقق معنى الستر، وهو مندوب إليه، فلا يثبت بعلم القاضي، ولا بشهادة أقل العدد من المذكور، ولا بشهادة النساء واتحاد المجلس شرط لصحة الشهادة بالزنا عندنا، حتى لو شهدوا متفرقين واحداً بعد واحد لا تقبل شهادتهم، ويحدون حد القذف خلافاً للشافعي. (مستخلص، مسكين، عيني) لا بالوطء: أي لا يثبت بلفظ الوطء والجماع؛ لأنهما لا يدلان على ذلك. (ط) فيسألهم الإمام: أي إذا شهد الشهود يسألهم الإمام عن خمسة أشياء: الأول: عن ماهية الزنا، والمراد منه السؤال عن ذاته أي حقيقته الشرعية، وهي إدخال الفرج في الفرج كما أشار إليه المصنف بقوله : "الزنا وطء في قبل، والغرض من هذا السؤال أن من الناس من يزعم أن كل وطء حرام فهو ،زنا، وليس كذلك، فإن مماسة الفرجين ،حرام، ولا يجب الحد بغير الإيلاج، وكذا الوطء في الفخذ وغيره فلهذا الاحتمال يسأله عن الزنا ما هو . الثاني: يسأل عن كيفيته بأن يقول: كيف زنى إكراها أو طوعاً؛ لأنه إذا كان بإكراه لا يجب الحد، والثالث: يسأل عن مكان الزنا بأن يقول: أين زنى؛ لاحتمال أن يكون في دار الحرب أو في عسكر أهل البغي، فلا يجب الحد، والرابع: يسأل عن زمانه بأن يقول متى زنى؛ لاحتمال تقادم عهد الزنا، أو في حال الصبا أو الجنون، فلا يجب الحد والخامس يسأل عن المزنية بأن يقول : من زنى؛ لاحتمال أنه زنى بجارية ابنه، أو بمن له فيها ملك أو شبهة لا يقف عليها الشهود، فلا يجب عليه الحد، ووجه السؤال عن هذه الأشياء الخمسة؛ لأن النبي عليا استفسر ماعزاً على هذا التفصيل. (مستخلص، فتح) فإن بينوه: [ أي إن بين الشهود الزنا بعد سؤال الحاكم على الوجه المذكور. (عيني)] القياس يقتضي جمع الضمير لعودتها إلى الوجوه التي دفع السؤال عنها من الماهية ،ومعطوفاتها، لكنه أفرد الضمير ليرجع إلى المذكور، وذكر بكلمة "إن" وهي تذكر في أمر غير كائن؛ لأنه قل ما يثبت الزنا بالبينة، وقوله: "كالميل في المكحلة" الميل الخشبة التي يكحل بها الكحل، والمكحلة بضمتين يعني الميم والحاء وعاء الكحل، وقوله: "عدلوا سراً وجهراً" والتعديل سراً: أن يبعث القاضي ورقة فيها أسماء الشهود وأسماء محلتهم على وجه يتميز كل منهم لمن يعرفهم، = وقالوا: رأيناه وطئها كالميل في المكحلة، وعدلوا سراً وجهراً حكم به، فيكتب تحت اسمه هو عدل مقبول الشهادة وحاصل التعديل علانية: أن يجمع القاضي بين المزكي والشاهد، فيقول: هذا هو الذي زكيته. والحاصل: أن القاضي لا يكتفي بظاهر العدالة، ولا يقضي بعلمه، بخلاف سائر الحقوق احتيالاً للدرء، وقوله: "حكم به" جزاء الشرط أي فإن بينوا وقالوا حكم الحاكم بموجب الزنا بشهادتهم وأقام الحد على المشهود عليه؛ لظهور الحق، ويجوز حبسه إلى أن يسأل عن الشهود لا أخذ الكفيل؛ لأنه نوع احتياط، فلا يشرع فيما يبتني على الدرء. (مستخلص، فتح، عيني) وعدلوا: على صيغة المجهول أي الشهود
Book of Hudud. Conditions of the hadd and its rulings. Intercourse in the front, free of ownership and its semblance, and it is established by the testimony of four (witnesses) with the word 'zina', not with the word 'intercourse' (wat') – i.e., (they must testify to) intercourse (wat') in the front, free of ownership and its semblance and marriage – so the imam (or judge) asks them about its essence, its manner, its place, its time, and the woman with whom zina was committed; if they clarify it... (The commentary then explains that the witnesses must be four men, testifying with the word 'zina', that it is proven by four witnesses based on Quranic verses and hadith, that the witnesses must be in one sitting, that the judge asks about five matters: essence of zina, whether it was by force or choice, the place, the time, and the woman, and that if they testify as described and are declared upright (tazkiyah) both secretly and openly, the judge rules accordingly. The analogy of the kohl stick in the kohl container is mentioned, and the judge does not rely on his own knowledge but requires this procedure to protect against punishment.)
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq on the conditions for establishing the hadd punishment for zina. The author first defines zina as intercourse in the front (vagina) that is not based on valid ownership (like a slave-girl) or a semblance of ownership (like a doubtful marriage), and that it is free from any ownership right or its semblance. The ruling is that zina is proven by the testimony of four male witnesses who explicitly use the word 'zina' (not 'intercourse' or 'copulation') because those terms are ambiguous and could refer to lawful acts. The witnesses must testify together in one sitting; if they testify separately, their testimony is rejected and they are punished for qadhf (false accusation). The judge then interrogates them about five specifics: (1) the legal reality of zina (insertion of the glans into the vagina), (2) whether it was by force or voluntary, (3) the location (to ensure it was in dar al-Islam or not in a rebellious army camp), (4) the time (to rule out childhood, insanity, or prescription), and (5) the identity of the woman (to exclude cases of ownership or doubt unknown to the witnesses). This detailed questioning follows the precedent of the Prophet ﷺ with Ma'iz. The passage also requires tazkiyah (attestation of the witnesses' probity) both secretly (by sending a confidential letter to their hometown) and openly (by having the one who recommended them affirm it in front of the judge). The judge does not rely on his own knowledge nor on the apparent probity of the witnesses, out of caution (ihtiyatan li'l-dar') to avoid implementing the hadd. Once the conditions are met and the judge rules, the hadd is carried out.

Key Terms
الزنا (al-zina): The legal definition: intercourse (wat') in the front (qubul) that is free from valid ownership or its semblance; requires insertion of the glans.
البينة (al-bayyinah): Proof by four male witnesses testifying explicitly with the word 'zina' in one sitting; the judge must question them and verify their integrity.
التعديل (al-ta'dil): Attestation of the witnesses' probity, done both secretly (by sending a written inquiry) and openly (by confronting the recommender with the witness).
السؤال (al-su'al): The judge's obligatory questioning of witnesses about five specifics: essence, manner, place, time, and woman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many witnesses are required to prove zina in Hanafi fiqh, and what specific word must they use in their testimony?
A) Two witnesses, using the word 'intercourse' (wat').
B) Four witnesses, using the word 'zina' (al-zina).
C) Four witnesses, using the word 'adultery' (al-fahishah).
D) Three witnesses, using the word 'fornication' (al-firash).

Key Takeaway
The strict conditions for proving zina reflect the principle of dar' (averting punishment) and the caution in hudud; the judge must ensure absolute certainty before implementing the hadd.

Proving Zina by Confession: Four Confessions in Separate Sittings
Requirement of four confessions in separate sittings with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi requirement of four confessions in separate sittings for proving zina and explain the dalil from the hadith of Ma'iz.

Core Idea
Four separate confessions are required for the hadd of zina, each followed by the judge's rebuff.

When a person confesses to zina, the Hanafi school imposes a strict procedure to protect the accused through the principle of dar' (averting punishment). Unlike testimony, where four witnesses are needed, confession also requires repetition—four times in four separate sittings—each time the judge rebuffs the confessor. This lesson examines the ruling, its proof from the Prophetic practice, and the difference with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is confessing to zina before a judge. The ruling is that the hadd penalty is established only after the confession is repeated four times in separate sittings.
This is wajib, not fard, because the evidence is a single hadith (ahad).
2
State the Hanafi position and its rationale
The Hanafi school requires four confessions, analogizing to the four witnesses for testimony, both as a precaution to avoid punishment (ihtiyalan li'l-dar'). Each confession must be in a separate sitting, and the judge must rebuff the confessor each time.
The rationale: just as the number of witnesses was increased to four to prevent hasty punishment, the number of confessions is increased likewise.
3
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is the hadith of Ma'iz: the Prophet (ﷺ) delayed the hadd until Ma'iz had confessed four times in four separate sittings, and he rebuffed him each time.
The hadith is ahad (thubut zanni) but its meaning is clear (dalala qati).
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof proves the ruling)
The Prophet's delay indicates that if one confession sufficed, he would not have delayed. The rebuffing after each confession shows that the confessions must be in separate sittings.
Also, the Prophet rebuffed Ma'iz until he hid behind the walls of Madinah, demonstrating the practice.
5
Compare with the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that one confession suffices because repetition does not add clarity. The Hanafi response relies on the explicit practice of the Prophet.
Malik agrees with the Hanafi position; the Shafi'i ruling is based on qiyas with other rights.

وبإقراره أربعاً : عطف على قوله : "بشهادة أربعة" أي ويثبت الزنا أيضاً بإقرار الزاني أربع مرات؛ لأنه زيد في عدد شهادته احتيالاً للدرء فيزاد في عدد إقراره لذلك، وقال الشافعي: يكتفي بإقراره مرة كما في سائر الحقوق؛ لأن الإقرار مظهر، وتكرار الأول لا يفيد زيادة الظهور، بخلاف زيادة العدد في الشهود ولنا حديث ماعز أنه علي أخر إقامة الحد عليه إلى أن تم إقراره أربع مرات في أربعة مجالس، فلو ظهر دونها لما أخرها بعد ثبوت الوجوب، وبه قال مالك، وقوله: "في مجالسه" أي مجالسه الأربعة، الضمير في يرجع إلى المقر فلو أقر أربع مرات في مجلس واحد كان ذلك بمنزلة إقرار واحد؛ لأن النبي عليه طرد ماعزاً في كل مرة حتى توارى بحيطان المدينة، وقال ابن أبي ليلى لا يعتبر اختلاف المجالس، وإنما يعتبر العدد فقط، أحمد كذلك رمز الحقائق: ۳۷۸/۱] (مستخلص) كلما أقر به: أي كلما أقر المقر بالزنا رده القاضي وطرده؛ لأن النبي عليه فعل كذلك، وقال عمر ه: "اطردوا المعترفين" يعني بالزنا، وقوله : "وسأله كما مر" أي وسأل القاضي المقر بالزنا مثل ما مر في الشهادة بأن يسأله : ماهية الزنا وكيفيته ومكانه وزمانه ،والمزنية، وقيل: لا يسأل عن الزمان؛ لأن تقادم العهد يمنع الشهادة دون الإقرار، والأصح أنه يسأله لاحتمال أنه زنى في صباه، وهذا السؤال يكون بعد ما نظر في حال الزاني، وعرف أنه صحيح العقل كما فعل عليها ولا يكتفي بالكناية، فإذا بين ذلك وظهر زناه سأله . عن الإحصان. فإذا قال: إنه محصن بفتح الصاد من أحصن الرجل إذا تزوج وهو من الكلمات التي جاء اسم الفاعل فيها على لفظ اسم المفعول، فإن وصف الإحسان بشرائطه حكم ،برجمه ولا يعتبر إقراره عند غير القاضي ممن لا ولاية له في إقامة الحدود ولو كان أربع مرات حتى لا تقبل الشهادة عليه بذلك؛ لأنه إن كان منكراً فقد رجع، وإن كان مقراً لا تعتبر الشهادة مع الإقرار ، ولو أقر بالزنا مرتين وشهد عليه أربعة لا يحد عند أبي يوسف خلافاً لمحمد. رمز الحقائق: ۳۷۸/۱] (فتح) رده: أي القاضي أو الحاكم حتى يذهب ويغيب عن بصره ثم يجيء ويقر. (عيني) وسأله: أي سأل القاضي المقر بالزنا بعد ما أقر أربع مرات. (ط، عيني) وعن
And by his (the confessor's) confession four times – it is conjoined to his statement 'by the testimony of four' – meaning that zina is also established by the confession of the zani four times; because the number of testimony was increased for the sake of prevention (ihtiyalan li'l-dar'), so the number of confession is increased likewise. Al-Shafi'i said: a single confession suffices as in other rights; because confession is revealing, and repetition does not add to revelation, unlike the increase in the number of witnesses. Our evidence is the hadith of Ma'iz that the Prophet ﷺ delayed the implementation of the hadd until his confession was completed four times in four sittings; if it would have become clear without that, he would not have delayed it after the obligation was established. Malik said the same. His statement 'in his sittings' means his four sittings; the pronoun refers to the confessor. If he confesses four times in one sitting, it is considered as one confession; because the Prophet ﷺ rebuffed Ma'iz each time until he hid behind the walls of Madinah. Ibn Abi Layla said: difference of sittings is not considered, only the number; Ahmad similarly. (Ramooz al-Haqaiq 1/378) (Mukhtasar) Every time he confesses: i.e., every time the confessor confesses to zina, the judge rebuffs and drives him away; because the Prophet ﷺ did so, and 'Umar رضي الله عنه said: 'Drive away the confessors' meaning of zina. His statement: 'and he asks him as before' meaning the judge asks the confessor about the essence, manner, place, time, and the woman, similar to what was mentioned for testimony. It is said that he does not ask about time because lapse of time prevents testimony but not confession; the correct view is that he does ask due to the possibility that he committed zina in his youth. This questioning occurs after the judge examines the confessor's state and knows he is sane, as the Prophet ﷺ did. He does not suffice with allusion. When he clarifies and his zina becomes evident, he asks him about ihsan. If he says he is muhsin (literally 'fortified', meaning he has married), he is stoned. His confession is not considered before anyone other than the judge who has no authority to implement hudud, even if it is four times, so that testimony against him based on that is not accepted; because if he denies, he has retracted, and if he confesses, testimony is not considered alongside confession. If he confesses to zina twice and four witnesses testify against him, he is not flogged according to Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad. (Ramooz al-Haqaiq 1/378) (Fath) 'Rebuffed' means the judge or ruler rebuffs him until he goes and disappears from his sight, then comes and confesses. (Ayni) 'And he asks him' means the judge asks the confessor after he has confessed four times. (T, Ayni) And from...
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage deals with proving zina by confession (iqrar). The matn states that zina is also established by the confessor's confession four times. The commentary explains the reasoning: just as the number of witnesses was increased to four as a precaution against implementing the hadd (ihtiyalan li'l-dar'), similarly the number of confessions is increased to four. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that one confession suffices because confession is revealing and repetition does not add clarity. The Hanafi proof is the hadith of Ma'iz: the Prophet ﷺ deferred the hadd until Ma'iz confessed four times in four separate sittings, and each time the Prophet rebuffed him. This indicates the necessity of four confessions. Additionally, the confessions must be in different sittings; if a person confesses four times in one sitting, it counts as only one confession. The judge must also question the confessor about the five matters (essence, manner, place, time, and the woman) just as with witnesses, though there is a difference of opinion about asking about time. After the confession is established, the judge asks about ihsan (marital status) to determine if the penalty is stoning or flogging. A key point: confession (in private? No, at court) is only valid before a judge with authority to implement hudud; if someone confesses before others, it is not considered. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: if a person confesses twice and then four witnesses testify, Abu Yusuf says he is not punished (because the confession is incomplete), while Muhammad says he is punished (because the testimony is sufficient).

Key Terms
الإقرار (al-iqrar): Confession of zina made by the accused before the judge; must be done four times in separate sittings, each time the judge rebuffs him.
الإحصان (al-ihsan): The state of being muhsan: a free, adult Muslim who has consummated a valid marriage; if the confessor is muhsan, the penalty is stoning; otherwise, flogging.
الدرء (al-dar'): The principle of repelling or averting the hadd punishment through doubts and precautions; the increase in number of confessions is to protect this principle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many confessions and in how many sittings are required to establish zina by confession?
A) One confession in one sitting.
B) Two confessions in two sittings.
C) Four confessions in four separate sittings.
D) Four confessions in any number of sittings.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires four separate confessions in four separate sittings, each followed by the judge's rebuff, to establish the hadd for zina by confession.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: When Confession Meets Testimony
Intra-Hanafi dispute on combining two confessions with four testimonies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding testimony after incomplete confession and identify the practical consequence.

Core Idea
Confession twice and testimony four times: Abu Yusuf says no hadd, Muhammad says yes.

In the Hanafi school, there is a disagreement between Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad about a scenario where a person confesses to zina only twice (not four times) and then four witnesses testify against him. Abu Yusuf holds that the hadd is not applied because the confession is incomplete and testimony cannot complement it, while Muhammad holds that the testimony is sufficient. This lesson analyses the dispute and its practical implication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A person confesses to zina twice (not four times). Then four witnesses testify that they saw him commit zina. The question: should the hadd be implemented?
The confession alone does not meet the four-time requirement.
2
State Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf says the hadd is not implemented. Reason: the confession is an independent basis for hadd, but two confessions are insufficient to establish it. The testimony does not fill the gap because the confession already exists but is incomplete.
Abu Yusuf views the confession as the primary basis; testimony cannot supplement a deficient confession.
3
State Muhammad's position
Muhammad says the hadd is implemented. Reason: the testimony of four witnesses is sufficient in itself to prove zina, regardless of the incomplete confession. The confession does not negate the testimony.
Muhammad views testimony as an independent, stronger proof that overrides the incomplete confession.
4
Analyze the basis of each view
Abu Yusuf: because the confessor's own statement (confession) is a form of evidence, but since it is incomplete, the hadd is not established. Muhammad: the testimony stands on its own and meets the requirement of four witnesses.
The difference stems from how they weigh the interaction between confession and testimony.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Under Abu Yusuf, the accused is not punished; under Muhammad, the accused is punished (flogging or stoning if applicable). The judge would need to choose which view to follow.
This is an unresolved ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school; the text presents both but does not give tarjih.

Four Confessions for Zina: The Hanafi Requirement
Explaining the requirement of four confessions for proving zina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi requirement for proving zina by confession and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Four confessions in four sittings are required to prove zina – a deliberate barrier to avoid punishment.

Confession in Islamic criminal law is not always straightforward. For the crime of zina (unlawful sexual intercourse), the Hanafi school imposes an extra condition: the accused must confess four times in four separate sittings. This requirement, rooted in the Prophet's treatment of Ma'iz, aims to avert the hadd punishment whenever possible. In this lesson, we explore the ruling, the proof, and the disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
State clearly: the Hanafi school requires four confessions in four separate sittings for zina to be proven by confession. A single confession or four in one sitting does not suffice.
This is a condition (shart) for the hadd, not a pillar.
2
Identify the opposing position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that one confession is enough, just as in other crimes. His basis: confession is a revealer; repetition adds no clarity.
Shafi'i position is also supported by analogy to other rights.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi rely on the hadith of Ma'iz: the Prophet (peace be upon him) delayed stoning until Ma'iz confessed four times in four sittings, turning him away each time.
This is a Sunnah ahad, muttafaq alayh in meaning.
4
Understand the principle of dar'
The number is increased as a precaution to avert the hadd (dar'). This is reflected in the analogous requirement of four witnesses for zina.
The maxim 'Hadd is averted by doubts' drives this ruling.
5
Note the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: under Hanafi law, a single confession does not lead to punishment; the accused must be given multiple opportunities to retract. Under Shafi'i, one confession suffices for the hadd.
The Hanafi approach protects against hasty punishment.

وقالوا: رأيناه وطئها كالميل في المكحلة، وعدلوا سراً وجهراً حكم به، وبإقراره أربعاً في مجالسه الأربعة، كلما أقر به رده وسأله كما مر . أي الرجل أي المرأة في الفرج أي وعاء الكحل أي أربع مرات أي مجالس المقر المقر بالزنا القاضي الإمام بموجب الزنا بظهور الحق فيكتب تحت اسمه هو عدل مقبول الشهادة وحاصل التعديل علانية: أن يجمع القاضي بين المزكي والشاهد، فيقول: هذا هو الذي زكيته. والحاصل: أن القاضي لا يكتفي بظاهر العدالة، ولا يقضي بعلمه، بخلاف سائر الحقوق احتيالاً للدرء، وقوله: "حكم به" جزاء الشرط أي فإن بينوا وقالوا حكم الحاكم بموجب الزنا بشهادتهم وأقام الحد على المشهود عليه؛ لظهور الحق، ويجوز حبسه إلى أن يسأل عن الشهود لا أخذ الكفيل؛ لأنه نوع احتياط، فلا يشرع فيما يبتني على الدرء. (مستخلص، فتح، عيني) وعدلوا: على صيغة المجهول أي الشهود وبإقراره أربعاً : عطف على قوله : "بشهادة أربعة" أي ويثبت الزنا أيضاً بإقرار الزاني أربع مرات؛ لأنه زيد في عدد شهادته احتيالاً للدرء فيزاد في عدد إقراره لذلك، وقال الشافعي: يكتفي بإقراره مرة كما في سائر الحقوق؛ لأن الإقرار مظهر، وتكرار الأول لا يفيد زيادة الظهور، بخلاف زيادة العدد في الشهود ولنا حديث ماعز أنه علي أخر إقامة الحد عليه إلى أن تم إقراره أربع مرات في أربعة مجالس، فلو ظهر دونها لما أخرها بعد ثبوت الوجوب، وبه قال مالك، وقوله: "في مجالسه" أي مجالسه الأربعة، الضمير في يرجع إلى المقر فلو أقر أربع مرات في مجلس واحد كان ذلك بمنزلة إقرار واحد؛ لأن النبي عليه طرد ماعزاً في كل مرة حتى توارى بحيطان المدينة، وقال ابن أبي ليلى لا يعتبر اختلاف المجالس، وإنما يعتبر العدد فقط، أحمد كذلك رمز الحقائق: ۳۷۸/۱] (مستخلص) كلما أقر به: أي كلما أقر المقر بالزنا رده القاضي وطرده؛ لأن النبي عليه فعل كذلك، وقال عمر ه: "اطردوا المعترفين" يعني بالزنا، وقوله : "وسأله كما مر" أي وسأل القاضي المقر بالزنا مثل ما مر في الشهادة بأن يسأله : ماهية الزنا وكيفيته ومكانه وزمانه ،والمزنية، وقيل: لا يسأل عن الزمان؛ لأن تقادم العهد يمنع الشهادة دون الإقرار، والأصح أنه يسأله لاحتمال أنه زنى في صباه، وهذا السؤال يكون بعد ما نظر في حال الزاني، وعرف أنه صحيح العقل كما فعل عليها ولا يكتفي بالكناية، فإذا بين ذلك وظهر زناه سأله . عن الإحصان. فإذا قال: إنه محصن بفتح الصاد من أحصن الرجل إذا تزوج وهو من الكلمات التي جاء اسم الفاعل فيها على لفظ اسم المفعول، فإن وصف الإحسان بشرائطه حكم ،برجمه ولا يعتبر إقراره عند غير القاضي ممن لا ولاية له في إقامة الحدود ولو كان أربع مرات حتى لا تقبل الشهادة عليه بذلك؛ لأنه إن كان منكراً فقد رجع، وإن كان مقراً لا تعتبر الشهادة مع الإقرار ، ولو أقر بالزنا مرتين وشهد عليه أربعة لا يحد عند أبي يوسف خلافاً لمحمد. رمز الحقائق: ۳۷۸/۱] (فتح) رده: أي القاضي أو الحاكم حتى يذهب ويغيب عن بصره ثم يجيء ويقر. (عيني) وسأله: أي سأل القاضي المقر بالزنا بعد ما أقر أربع مرات. (ط، عيني)
And they said: We saw him having intercourse with her like a kohl stick in a kohl container, and they declared him just secretly and openly, he (the judge) judged by it, and by his (the confessor's) confession four times in his four sittings, whenever he confessed he (the judge) turned him away and asked him as has passed. Meaning the man, meaning the woman, in the private part, meaning the container of kohl, meaning four times, meaning the sittings of the confessor, the confessor of zina, the judge, the imam, because of the occurrence of zina by the appearance of the truth, so he writes under his name 'he is a just person whose testimony is accepted', and the result of declaring just openly: that the judge gathers between the one who declares just and the witness, saying: this is the one you declared just. The conclusion: that the judge is not content with apparent justice, nor does he judge by his own knowledge, contrary to other rights, as a stratagem for avoidance (of punishment). And His statement: 'he judged by it' is the result of the condition, meaning if they explain and say the judge judged because of the occurrence of zina by their testimony and he established the hadd on the one testified against, due to the appearance of the truth. And it is permissible to imprison him until he asks about the witnesses, but not to take a surety, because it is a type of precaution, so it is not legislated in what is based on avoidance. (Mukhtasar, Fath, Ayni) 'And they declared just' in the passive voice meaning the witnesses. 'And by his confession four times' is conjoined to his statement 'by the testimony of four', meaning zina is also proven by the confession of the zani four times, because the number of his testimony was increased as a stratagem for avoidance, so the number of his confession is increased for that reason. Al-Shafi'i said: He is content with his confession once as in other rights, because confession is a revealer, and repetition of the first does not give increase of revelation, unlike the increase in the number of witnesses. We have the hadith of Ma'iz that he (the Prophet) delayed the establishment of the hadd on him until his confession was completed four times in four sittings. If it were established without that, he would not have delayed it after the obligation was proven. Malik also said this. And His statement: 'in his sittings' meaning his four sittings, the pronoun refers to the confessor. So if he confesses four times in one sitting, it is like one confession, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) turned away Ma'iz each time until he hid behind the walls of Madinah. Ibn Abi Layla said: Difference of sittings is not considered, only the number is considered. Similarly Ahmad. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1:378) (Mukhtasar) 'Whenever he confessed he turned him away': i.e. whenever the confessor confessed to zina, the judge turned him away and expelled him, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did likewise. And Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) said: 'Expel those who confess' meaning to zina. And his statement: 'and asked him as has passed' i.e. the judge asked the confessor of zina similar to what has passed in testimony, by asking him about the nature of zina, its modality, place, and time, and the woman. It was said: He does not ask about time because lapse of time prevents testimony but not confession. The correct view is that he asks him due to the possibility that he committed zina in his youth. This questioning is after he looks into the state of the zani and knows he is of sound mind, as he (the Prophet) did with Ma'iz, and he does not suffice with metaphor. When he explains that and his zina becomes apparent, he asks him about ihsan. If he says he is muhsin (with fat-ha on the sad, from ahsana al-rajulu if he married, and it is one of the words where the active participle comes in the form of the passive participle), then if he describes ihsan with its conditions, he (the judge) judges to stone him. And his confession is not considered before other than the judge who has no authority to establish hadd, even if it is four times, so testimony against him is not accepted; because if he denies then he has retracted, and if he confesses testimony is not considered along with confession. And if he confesses to zina twice and four testify against him, he is not flogged according to Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1:378) (Fath) 'He turned him away': i.e. the judge or ruler until he goes and disappears from his sight, then comes and confesses. (Ayni) 'And asked him': i.e. the judge asked the confessor of zina after he confessed four times. (Tahawi, Ayni)
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage deals with the proof of zina (unlawful sexual intercourse) through confession. It is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i. The passage first clarifies the analogy used in the matn: the act of intercourse is compared to a kohl stick entering a kohl container, indicating full penetration. The text then explains the procedure for establishing zina by confession: the judge first verifies the witnesses' justice publicly, but unlike other cases, does not rely on apparent justice or his own knowledge, all as a measure to avert the hadd (punishment). The key ruling is that zina is proven by the confessor's confession four times in four separate sittings. The Hanafi position is supported by the hadith of Ma'iz (may Allah be pleased with him), where the Prophet (peace be upon him) delayed the hadd until Ma'iz confessed four times in four different sittings. Al-Shafi'i argued that a single confession suffices, as in other rights, because repetition does not increase clarity. The Hanafi response is that the increase in number is a precaution for aversion, hence it is applied to both testimony and confession. The passage also discusses that if the confessor confesses four times in one sitting, it is treated as a single confession, citing the Prophet's practice of turning away Ma'iz each time. Additionally, it covers the judge's duty to question the confessor about the details of the zina (nature, modality, place, time, and the woman) and about ihsan (being married) to determine if stoning applies. There is a subsidiary dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding a case where the confessor confesses twice and four witnesses testify: Abu Yusuf says the hadd is not imposed, while Muhammad disagrees. The passage ends with notes on the judge's actions of turning away and questioning.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): Confession of the accused to the crime of zina.
مجالس (majalis): Sittings or sessions in which the confession is made; each sitting is a separate occasion.
درء (dar'): Aversion or ward off of the hadd punishment through doubts (shubuhat).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many confessions are required to prove zina by confession, and in how many sittings?
A) One confession in one sitting
B) Two confessions in two sittings
C) Four confessions in four separate sittings
D) Three confessions in any number of sittings

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires four confessions in four separate sittings to prove zina by confession, based on the prophetic practice with Ma'iz and the principle of averting hadd.

Retraction of Confession in Zina: The Shubha That Averts Hadd
Ruling on retraction of confession for zina before the punishment is completed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on retraction of confession in zina, explain the reasoning based on shubha, and contrast it with the Shafi'i position by identifying the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Retraction of confession in zina creates doubt (shubha) that averts the hadd — even if the retraction is by action.

This passage from Al-Hidayah commentary presents a key dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i. At stake is whether a person who confesses to zina can later retract and avoid punishment. The Hanafi position, rooted in the principle of averting hudud by doubts, gives weight to the possibility of the retraction being true, while the Shafi'i school treats the confession as conclusive.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school holds retraction before or during the hadd nullifies the punishment; the person is released.
The passage uses 'khulla sabeeluhu' (he is released).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The opposing school (Shafi'i, Ibn Abi Layla, and a narration from Malik) holds that the hadd is still carried out because the confession established the obligation.
They analogize to qisas and hadd al-qadhf.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the opponent's dalil: the hadd becomes obligatory by confession, and retraction does not invalidate it, just as with human rights cases where the victim can accuse the retractor of lying.
Their argument is based on the analogy with testimony.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response distinguishes between rights of Allah (haqq Allah) and rights of humans (haqq al-'abd). In zina, it is a right of Allah, which is waived by doubt. In qisas and qadhf, a human right is involved, so no doubt arises.
Also, in testimony, the denial of the accused is a condition; here the confessor himself retracts.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practically, the Hanafi school releases the person; the Shafi'i school punishes. This difference affects how judges handle retraction in hudud cases.
The Hanafi ruling is mufta bihi in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن بينه حده، فإن رجع عن إقراره قبل الحد، أو في وسطه خلي سبيله. أي إقامة الحد أي رجع في وسط الحد المقر فإن بينه: أي إن بين المقر ما ذكر من الشروط . (عيني) حده : أي الإمام أو القاضي لظهور الحق. (عيني) فإن رجع عن إقراره إلخ: أي فإن رجع المقر عن إقراره قبل إقامة الحد عليه، أو في وسط إقامة الحد ولو رجوعه بالفعل كهروبه، وإنكار الإقرار رجوع كما أن إنكار الردة توبة، وقوله: "خلى سبيله" لأن الرجوع خبر يحتمل الصدق، ولا مكذب له، فتحققت الشبهة، وقال الشافعي وابن أبي ليلى يحد لوجوبه بإقراره، ولا يبطل برجوعه كما إذا وجب بالشهادة، فصار كالقصاص وحد القذف، وبه قال مالك في رواية عنه، ولو ذكر لإقراره تأويلاً قبل وإلا فلا، ولنا ما مر من تحقق الشبهة بخلاف القصاص والقذف؛ لأن فيهما تعلق حق العبد، وصاحب الحق يكذبه، وبخلاف صورة الشهادة؛ لأن إنكار المشهود عليه شرط صحة ثبوت البينة. (مستخلص، فتح، عيني) خلي سبيله : أي تركه ولم يحد إن كان الرجوع قبل الحد أو لم يتم الحد إن كان في وسطه. (عيني)
If he explains his hadd, and if he retracts his confession before the hadd or during it, he is released (his way is cleared). Meaning the establishment of the hadd, meaning he retracted in the middle of the hadd, the confessor. 'If he explains his hadd': i.e. if the confessor explains the conditions mentioned. (Ayni) 'His hadd': i.e. the imam or judge, due to the appearance of the truth. (Ayni) 'If he retracts his confession etc.': i.e. if the confessor retracts his confession before the hadd is carried out on him, or during the carrying out of the hadd, even if his retraction is by actual deed like fleeing, and denial of confession is retraction just as denial of apostasy is repentance. His statement 'he is released' because the retraction is news that may be true, and there is no one who can accuse him of falsehood, so doubt (shubha) is realized. Al-Shafi'i and Ibn Abi Layla said: He is flogged because it is obligatory by his confession, and it is not invalidated by his retraction, just as if it were established by testimony, so it becomes like qisas and the hadd of qadhf. Malik also said this in one narration from him. And if he mentions an interpretation for his confession, it is accepted; otherwise not. We have what has passed: that doubt is realized, contrary to qisas and qadhf, because in those there is involvement of the right of the slave (human right), and the owner of the right accuses him of lying, and contrary to the case of testimony, because the denial of the one against whom testimony is given is a condition for the validity of establishing the evidence. (Mukhtasar, Fath, Ayni) 'He is released': i.e. he is left and not flogged if the retraction was before the hadd, or the hadd is not completed if retraction was during it. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling when a person who has confessed to zina retracts that confession either before the hadd punishment is carried out or during it. The Hanafi position, supported by the text, is that the retraction is accepted and the person is released. The reasoning is that the retraction is a statement that could be true, and there is no one to contradict it, thus it creates a doubt (shubha) which averts the hadd. The text notes that even if retraction is by action like fleeing, or simply denying the confession, it is considered retraction. The commentators contrast this with the views of al-Shafi'i and Ibn Abi Layla, who argue that the hadd becomes obligatory by the confession and is not nullified by retraction, similar to qisas (retribution) and the hadd of qadhf (false accusation of zina). The Hanafi response is that in qisas and qadhf, a human right (haqq al-'abd) is involved, and the victim can accuse the retractor of lying, whereas in the case of zina, it is a right of Allah (haqq Allah) that is waived by doubt. Similarly, in the case of testimony, the denial of the accused is a condition for the validity of the evidence. However, if the confessor gives an interpretation for his confession (e.g., 'I meant something else'), that interpretation is accepted; otherwise, the retraction is still accepted due to doubt. The passage concludes with the practical consequence: if retraction occurs before the hadd, the person is left unpunished; if during the hadd, the punishment is stopped.

Key Terms
رجوع (ruju'): Retraction or withdrawal of a previous confession to zina.
شبهة (shubha): A doubt or uncertainty that prevents the application of the hadd punishment.
خلى سبيله (khulla sabeeluhu): He is released; i.e., no punishment is carried out.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if a person confesses to zina and then retracts during the flogging?
A) Flogging continues.
B) Flogging stops immediately.
C) The person is fined.
D) The person is jailed for perjury.

Key Takeaway
Retraction of confession in zina before or during the hadd creates doubt (shubha) that waives the punishment, reflecting the principle that hudud are averted by doubts.

Talfin (Prompting Retraction) and Stoning of the Muhsan
Ruling on prompting retraction and stoning the muhsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prompting retraction (talqin) and explain when stoning applies to the muhsan.

Core Idea
The judge should prompt the confessor to retract; stoning is only for the muhsan who persists in confession.

This passage presents two interconnected rulings from the chapter on hudud. First, it establishes a recommended procedure for the judge when a person confesses to zina: to actively suggest possible retractions or qualifications to avert the hadd. Second, it clarifies that if the confessor is muhsan and persists, stoning in a public space is the prescribed punishment. The ruling is grounded in the prophetic treatment of Ma'iz, and the commentary addresses a potential objection about his mental state.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that prompting (talqin) the confessor to retract is recommended (nadb/mustahabb). The judge suggests: 'Perhaps you kissed, touched, or had intercourse under a shubha.'
This is a sunnah muakkadah based on the Prophet's practice.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Ma'iz: the Prophet asked him three times if he only kissed or winked, and only ordered stoning when Ma'iz explicitly confessed to sexual intercourse without euphemism.
Reference: Bukhari, Ahmad, Abu Dawud.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action of prompting and then stoning only after explicit confirmation shows that prompt is recommended and that stoning is for the muhsan who does not retract.
The Prophet even asked 'Are you insane?' as a form of prompt, not because of actual doubt.
4
Identify the second ruling
If the confessor is muhsan (married and had conjugal relations), the hadd is stoning in a spacious open area until death, as a deterrent.
This is based on the Prophet's stoning of Ma'iz and al-Ghamidiyyah.
5
Understand the wisdom
The judge should seek to avoid the hadd if possible, by giving the confessor every opportunity to retract or qualify the confession. Stoning is a severe punishment reserved for the most serious cases.
Ali's hadith lists three cases where a Muslim's blood is permissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وندب تلقينه بلعلك قبلت أو لمست أو وطئت بشبهة، فإن كان محصناً رجمه في أي فضاء حتى يموت مكان واسع أو بنكاح أو بملك يمين أي متزوجا أي استحب ثم الرجوع عن الإقرار ويقول له: لعلك لمست أو قبلت؛ لأنه عليه قال لما عز: "لعلك قبلت أو غمزت أو نظرت"، قال: لا يا رسول الله قال: "أنكتَها ولا تُكَنّى، قال: نعم، فعند ذلك أمر برجمه، رواه البخاري وأحمد وأبوداود رمز الحقائق: ۳۷۸/۱] فإن قيل: إنما عرض النبي عليا على ماعز الرجوع؛ لأنه راب في عقله؛ لأنه كان قد جاء متغير اللون إلا أنه لما أصر على الإقرار ودام على نهج العقلاء قبل ذلك الإقرار منه أزال شبهته بالسؤال فقال: "أبك جهل، أبك جنون؟"، قلنا: مجيئه متغيراً دليل التوبة والخوف من الله لا دليل الجنون، وإنما قال: "أبك جهل، أبك جنون؟" تلقيناً لماعز لما يدرأ الحد وقد روي أن أبا بكر له قال لماعز بعد المرة الثالثة: إن أقررت الرابعة رجمناك فثبت أن هذا العدد كان ظاهراً عندهم. (عيني) رجمه في فضاء أي إذا وجب الحد وكان الزاني متزوجاً ضربه الحاكم بالحجارة حتى يموت، ويخرجه إلى مكان واسع ليكون أقرب إلى الاعتبار، ولأنه عليه أمر برجم الغامدية وماعز وكانا محصنين، وأخرج ماعزا إلى الحرة، وقيل: إلى البقيع فرجم بالحجارة حتى مات رمز الحقائق: ۳۷۸/۱] وقال علي: "لا يحل دم امرأ مسلم إلا بإحدى معان ثلاث كفر بعد الإيمان وزنا بعد إحصان، وقتل نفس بغير الحق"، والحديث في المصابيح. تبيين الحقائق: ٥٤٩/٣] (مستخلص)
And it is recommended (nadb) to prompt him: 'Perhaps you kissed or touched or had intercourse with a shubha (doubtful intercourse).' If he is muhsan, he is stoned in any spacious place until he dies. A spacious place. Or by marriage or by right-hand possession, i.e., married. It is recommended. Then retraction from the confession, and he (the judge) says to him: 'Perhaps you touched or kissed,' because he (the Prophet) said to Ma'iz: 'Perhaps you kissed or winked or looked.' He said: 'No, O Messenger of Allah.' He said: 'Did you have intercourse with her without metaphor?' He said: 'Yes.' Then he ordered his stoning. Narrated by Bukhari, Ahmad, and Abu Dawud. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1:378) If it is said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) offered Ma'iz the chance to retract only because he suspected his sanity, because he came with a changed complexion, but when he persisted in his confession and continued on the path of rational people, he accepted that confession and removed his doubt by asking: 'Are you ignorant? Are you insane?' We say: His coming with changed complexion is evidence of repentance and fear of Allah, not evidence of insanity. He only said: 'Are you ignorant? Are you insane?' as a prompt (talqin) to Ma'iz to avert the hadd. And it has been narrated that Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him) said to Ma'iz after the third time: 'If you confess a fourth time, we will stone you.' So it is established that this number (four) was apparent to them. (Mukhtasar) 'Perhaps you kissed': i.e., saying: perhaps you kissed that woman. (Ayni) 'Muhsan': i.e., the one against whom zina is proven. (Ayni) 'Stoned in a spacious place': i.e., when the hadd becomes obligatory and the zani is married, the ruler strikes him with stones until he dies, and he takes him out to a spacious place to be closer to the object lesson, and because the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered the stoning of al-Ghamidiyyah and Ma'iz, and they were both muhsan, and he took Ma'iz out to al-Harrah, and it is said to al-Baqi', and he was stoned with stones until he died. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1:378) And Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) said: 'The blood of a Muslim is not permissible except by one of three things: disbelief after faith, zina after ihsan, and taking a life unjustly.' And the hadith is in al-Masabih. (Tabiyin al-Haqa'iq 3:549) (Mukhtasar)
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage covers two related rulings. First, it is recommended (nadb/mustahabb) for the judge to prompt the person who has confessed to zina to retract his confession, by suggesting that perhaps he only kissed, touched, or had intercourse under a doubtful circumstance (shubha). This is based on the Prophet's (peace be upon him) treatment of Ma'iz, where he gave him multiple opportunities to retract by asking 'Perhaps you kissed, or winked, or looked?' The passage responds to a potential objection that the Prophet's prompt was due to doubt about Ma'iz's sanity. The commentator clarifies that Ma'iz's changed complexion was a sign of fear and repentance, not insanity, and the Prophet's question 'Are you ignorant? Are you insane?' was itself a prompt to avert the hadd. Additionally, it is reported that Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him) warned Ma'iz about the fourth confession, showing that the number of confessions was well-known. Second, if the confessor is muhsan (a married free person who has enjoyed conjugal relations), and the hadd is established, he is to be stoned in a spacious open area until death. The wisdom is for the punishment to be a lesson to others. The passage also cites the hadith of Ali ibn Abi Talib (may Allah be pleased with him) that a Muslim's blood is only permissible in three cases: apostasy, zina after ihsan, and murder.

Key Terms
تلقين (talqin): Prompting or suggesting to the confessor a way to retract or qualify his confession to avoid the hadd.
محصن (muhsan): A person who is married (or has been married) and has had sexual relations; for stoning to apply, one must be muhsan at the time of zina.
فساء (fada' (from text 'في أي فضاء')): An open, spacious area where the stoning is to be carried out.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best describes the Hanafi ruling on talqin?
A) It is obligatory for the judge to prompt retraction before applying the hadd.
B) It is recommended but not obligatory.
C) It is prohibited because it suggests the confessor is lying.
D) It is only done if the confessor appears insane.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends that the judge actively prompt a confessor to zina to retract, and only if the confessor persists and is muhsan should stoning be carried out in an open area.
