Retraction of Confession Nullifies Hadd Due to Shubha
Ruling and inter-madhhab dispute on retraction nullifying hadd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on retraction of confession in hadd, explain why retraction creates shubha, and contrast it with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Retraction before or during hadd creates doubt; hadd is repelled by doubt.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq presents the Hanafi rule that a confessor who retracts before or during the execution of the hadd punishment is released. The rationale is that retraction introduces uncertainty (shubha) about the crime, and the foundational principle 'hadd punishments are repelled by doubts' applies. The text then addresses the objections of al-Shafi'i and others, who argue by analogy to cases where retraction is ineffective. Understanding this ruling requires analyzing the nature of shubha and the limits of analogy in hudud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the Hanafi ruling: if a person confesses to zina and then retracts before or during the hadd, he is released and the punishment is dropped.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
2
Understand the Rationale
The retraction is a statement that could be true, and there is no one to deny it (no private right-holder). Thus, doubt (shubha) is established, and hadd is repelled by doubt.
The principle 'درء الحدود بالشبهات' (repel hadd by doubts) is key.
3
Analyze the Opposing View
Al-Shafi'i, Ibn Abi Layla, and Malik (in one narration) argue that the hadd becomes obligatory by confession and retraction does not invalidate it, just as with testimony, qisas, and qadhf.
They use qiyas to other hadd and qisas cases.
4
Examine the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi response distinguishes these analogies: in qisas and qadhf, a private right is involved, and the right-holder denies the retraction. In testimony, the accused's denial is a condition for evidence. In zina confession, there is no private right-owner, so retraction stands and creates doubt.
The distinction hinges on the presence of a private right (haqq al-'abd).
5
Determine the Practical Consequence
Under the Hanafi school, the confessor goes free; under the Shafi'i school, the punishment would still be carried out. This is the thamarah al-khilaf.
The difference has real-life implications for the accused.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن بينه حده، فإن رجع عن إقراره قبل الحد، أو في وسطه خلي سبيله. فإن بينه: أي إن بين المقر ما ذكر من الشروط . (عيني) حده : أي الإمام أو القاضي لظهور الحق. (عيني) فإن رجع عن إقراره إلخ: أي فإن رجع المقر عن إقراره قبل إقامة الحد عليه، أو في وسط إقامة الحد ولو رجوعه بالفعل كهروبه، وإنكار الإقرار رجوع كما أن إنكار الردة توبة، وقوله: "خلى سبيله" لأن الرجوع خبر يحتمل الصدق، ولا مكذب له، فتحققت الشبهة، وقال الشافعي وابن أبي ليلى يحد لوجوبه بإقراره، ولا يبطل برجوعه كما إذا وجب بالشهادة، فصار كالقصاص وحد القذف، وبه قال مالك في رواية عنه، ولو ذكر لإقراره تأويلاً قبل وإلا فلا، ولنا ما مر من تحقق الشبهة بخلاف القصاص والقذف؛ لأن فيهما تعلق حق العبد، وصاحب الحق يكذبه، وبخلاف صورة الشهادة؛ لأن إنكار المشهود عليه شرط صحة ثبوت البينة. (مستخلص، فتح، عيني) خلي سبيله : أي تركه ولم يحد إن كان الرجوع قبل الحد أو لم يتم الحد إن كان في وسطه. (عيني)
He clarified his hadd to him. Then if he retracts his confession before the hadd, or during it, he is released. 'Fa in bayyana haddahu': i.e., if the confessor clarified the conditions mentioned. (Ayni) 'Haddahu': i.e., the imam or judge due to the manifestation of the truth. (Ayni) 'Fa in raja'a an iqrarihi ila': i.e., if the confessor retracts his confession before the hadd is carried out, or during the hadd, even if his retraction is by action like his escape, and denial of the confession is retraction just as denial of apostasy is repentance. And his statement 'khulli sabiluhu' because retraction is news that could be true, and there is no one to declare it false, so doubt (shubha) is established. Al-Shafi'i and Ibn Abi Layla said: He is punished because it becomes obligatory by his confession, and it is not invalidated by his retraction, just as it becomes obligatory by testimony, so it is like qisas and the hadd of qadhf. Malik also said this in one narration from him. And if he mentions a valid interpretation for his confession, it is accepted; otherwise not. Our (Hanafi) argument is what we mentioned about the establishment of shubha, unlike qisas and qadhf because in those the right of the servant (individual) is involved, and the right-holder denies him, and unlike the case of testimony because the denial of the accused is a condition for the validity of establishing evidence. (Mustakhlas, Fath, Ayni) 'Khulli sabiluhu': i.e., he is left and not punished if the retraction was before the hadd, or not completed if during it. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on the effect of retracting a confession of zina before or during the execution of the hadd punishment. The ruling is that if the confessor retracts at any point before the punishment is fully carried out, the punishment is dropped and he is released. The reason is that retraction creates a doubt (shubha) about his guilt, and the hadd penalties are repelled by doubts (درء الحدود بالشبهات). The text then presents an inter-madhhab dispute: Al-Shafi'i and Ibn Abi Layla (and Malik in one narration) hold that the hadd becomes obligatory by the confession and is not invalidated by retraction, analogous to cases where the hadd is established by testimony (bayyinah) or where qisas or hadd qadhf are involved. The Hanafi response distinguishes these cases: In qisas and qadhf, a private right is involved, and the right-owner (the victim or his heir) does not accept the retraction. In the case of testimony, the denial of the accused is a condition for the evidence to be valid. But in the case of confession of zina, there is no private right-owner to deny the retraction, so retraction stands and creates doubt. Therefore the punishment is dropped. This is based on the prophetic principle of repelling hadd punishments by doubts.

Key Terms
الرجوع (al-ruju'): Retraction of a confession; the act of taking back one's admission.
الشبهة (al-shubha): Doubt or uncertainty about the commission of the crime that serves to repel the hadd punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The punishment is still carried out because the confession was valid.
B) The punishment is dropped and he is released because retraction creates doubt.
C) The punishment is reduced but not dropped.
D) He is imprisoned until he reaffirms the confession.

Key Takeaway
Retraction of confession in hadd cases creates shubha and repels the punishment, a ruling rooted in the Hanafi maxim that penalties are averted by uncertainties.

Recommendation to Prompt the Confessor to Retract
Ruling on prompting the confessor to retract to avoid hadd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prompting a confessor in hudud and explain the proof from the hadith of Ma'iz.

Core Idea
Prompt the confessor to retract; a doubt may avert the hadd.

When a person confesses to a hadd crime like zina, the Hanafi school teaches that the judge should not rush to punishment. Instead, he should proactively suggest possible excuses or reinterpretations, giving the confessor a chance to retract. This practice, known as talqin, is rooted in the Prophet's own conduct with Ma'iz. In this lesson, we will examine the ruling, its proof, and address a common misunderstanding about its purpose.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage explains that talqin (prompting the confessor to retract) is recommended (mustahab/sunnah). Identify: Who performs it? The imam/judge. To whom? The person confessing to zina.
The ruling is not wajib; it is a recommended mercy.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Ma'iz. The Prophet prompted him with 'Perhaps you kissed, or touched, or looked?' Find the exact phrase in the source.
The hadith is narrated by Bukhari, Ahmad, and Abu Dawud.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this action prove recommendation? The Prophet's clear act of prompting – suggesting alternative interpretations – shows it is legislated. The fact that he did it despite Ma'iz's eventual stoning indicates it is a sunnah to create doubt and possibly avert the hadd.
Wajh al-dalalah: the Prophet's practice is a model (uswa hasana).
4
Address the objection
Some claim the Prophet only prompted because he doubted Ma'iz's sanity. The passage refutes this: his changed complexion showed repentance, not insanity. The Prophet's question 'Are you mad?' was itself a form of talqin to repel the hadd.
The Hanafi response insists the prompting was deliberate, not due to suspicion of insanity.
5
Note the practical application
The judge should say: 'Perhaps you only kissed, or touched, or looked.' This gives the confessor an exit without lying. If he insists, the hadd is applied.
Talqin is not limited to zina; it applies to all hudud where possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وندب تلقينه [ أي تفيهم القاضي وتعليمه المقر بالزنا. (عيني)] أي يستحب للإمام أن يعلم المقر : ثم الرجوع عن الإقرار ويقول له: لعلك لمست أو قبلت؛ لأنه علي قال لما عز: "لعلك قبلت أو غمزت أو نظرت"، قال: لا يا رسول الله قال: "أنكتَها ولا تُكَنّى، قال: نعم، فعند ذلك أمر برجمه، رواه البخاري وأحمد وأبوداود رمز الحقائق: ۳۷۸/۱] فإن قيل: إنما عرض النبي عليا على ماعز الرجوع؛ لأنه راب في عقله؛ لأنه كان قد جاء متغير اللون إلا أنه لما أصر على الإقرار ودام على نهج العقلاء قبل ذلك الإقرار منه أزال شبهته بالسؤال فقال: "أبك جهل، أبك جنون؟"، قلنا: مجيئه متغيراً دليل التوبة والخوف من الله لا دليل الجنون، وإنما قال: "أبك جهل، أبك جنون؟" تلقيناً لماعز لما يدرأ الحد وقد روي أن أبا بكر له قال لماعز بعد المرة الثالثة: إن أقررت الرابعة رجمناك فثبت أن هذا العدد كان ظاهراً عندهم. (مستخلص) بلعلك قبلت : أي بأن يقول : لعلك قبلت تلك المرأة. (عيني)
And it is recommended to prompt him: [i.e., to make the judge understand and teach the confessor of zina. (Ayni)] i.e., it is recommended for the imam to teach the confessor: then retract the confession and say to him: Perhaps you only touched or kissed? Because 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) said when he was rebuked: 'Perhaps you kissed, or winked, or looked?' He said: 'No, O Messenger of Allah.' He said: 'Did you have intercourse without euphemism?' He said: 'Yes.' Then he ordered his stoning. Narrated by Bukhari, Ahmad, and Abu Dawud (Ramz al-Haqaiq: 1/378). If it is said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) only offered Ma'iz the chance to retract because he doubted his sanity, since he came with a changed complexion; but when he insisted on the confession and persisted in the manner of rational people, he accepted the confession from him, and removed his doubt by asking: 'Are you insane? Are you mad?' We say: His coming with changed complexion was evidence of repentance and fear of Allah, not evidence of insanity. Rather, he said: 'Are you insane? Are you mad?' as a prompting to Ma'iz to repel the hadd. And it is narrated that Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him) said to Ma'iz after the third time: If you confess a fourth time, we will stone you. So it is established that this number was apparent to them. (Mustakhlas) 'Bal'alla qabbalt': i.e., that he says: Perhaps you kissed that woman. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage discusses the recommendation (nadb) for the imam or judge to prompt a person who confesses to zina to retract or reinterpret his confession, in order to avert the hadd punishment. The practice is derived from the sunnah, specifically the incident of Ma'iz ibn Malik when he came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and confessed. The Prophet (peace be upon him) prompted him by asking if he had only kissed or touched, and when Ma'iz persisted, he confirmed the act and was stoned. The text addresses an objection: some argue that the Prophet did this because he suspected Ma'iz's mental state (as he appeared distressed). However, the Hanafi response explains that the Prophet's questions were a form of prompting (talqin) to repel the hadd, not because of insanity. The scholar notes that Abu Bakr similarly warned Ma'iz after the third confession. The commentary clarifies that the recommended phrasing includes saying 'perhaps you only kissed' or similar. This reflects the Hanafi principle of repelling hadd punishments through any possible doubt or excuse.

Key Terms
التلقين (al-talqin): Prompting or teaching the confessor to possibly retract or reinterpret his confession to avoid the hadd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Talqin is a recommended sunnah for the judge to offer the confessor a chance to avoid the severe hadd punishment.

Stoning the Muhsan in an Open Space
Ruling on stoning the muhsan in a wide open space

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for stoning the muhsan and explain the procedure and its evidence.

Core Idea
Stoning the muhsan must be in an open space for maximum deterrent effect, following the Prophet’s example.

This lesson addresses the hadd punishment for the muhsan adulterer. While the penalty itself is well-known, the Hanafi school emphasizes the importance of carrying it out in a wide open space. We will explore the reasoning behind this procedure and the primary evidence from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal subject
What act is being ruled on? The hadd punishment of stoning (rajm) for the muhsan (one who has had valid marital intercourse) upon committing zina.
The ruling is specific to the muhsan; non-muhsan receive flogging.
2
Determine the condition for the ruling
The person must be muhsan: a free adult Muslim who has consummated a valid marriage. The text explicitly states 'محصناً' meaning the one upon whom zina is established.
This condition is essential; without ihsan, the punishment is not stoning.
3
State the procedural requirement
The judge must take the convict to a wide open space ('فضاء') for stoning. The reason given is 'لِيَكُونَ أَقْرَبَ إِلَى الِاعْتِبَارِ' (to be closer to deterrence).
The open space ensures public visibility and serves as a warning to others.
4
Identify the evidence
Two primary proofs: (1) The Prophet's (peace be upon him) practice with Ma'iz and al-Ghamidiyyah, who were both muhsan and were stoned in open areas. (2) The hadith of 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) listing 'zina after ihsan' as one of three capital offenses.
The hadith of 'Ali is quoted: 'لا يحل دم امرأ مسلم إلا بإحدى معان ثلاث ...'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
محصناً : أي الذي ثبت عليه الزنا. (عيني) رجمه في فضاء أي إذا وجب الحد وكان الزاني متزوجاً ضربه الحاكم بالحجارة حتى يموت، ويخرجه إلى مكان واسع ليكون أقرب إلى الاعتبار، ولأنه عليه أمر برجم الغامدية وماعز وكانا محصنين، وأخرج ماعزا إلى الحرة، وقيل: إلى البقيع فرجم بالحجارة حتى مات رمز الحقائق: ۳۷۸/۱] وقال علي: "لا يحل دم امرأ مسلم إلا بإحدى معان ثلاث كفر بعد الإيمان وزنا بعد إحصان، وقتل نفس بغير الحق"، والحديث في المصابيح. تبيين الحقائق: ٥٤٩/٣] (مستخلص)
'Muhsan': i.e., he upon whom zina is established. (Ayni) 'Stoning in an open space': i.e., when the hadd becomes obligatory and the adulterer is married, the judge strikes him with stones until he dies, and takes him to a wide place because it is closer to deterrence, and because he (peace be upon him) ordered the stoning of al-Ghamidiyyah and Ma'iz, and they were muhsan, and he took Ma'iz out to al-Harrah, and it is said: to al-Baqi', and he was stoned with stones until he died. (Ramz al-Haqaiq: 1/378) And 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) said: 'The blood of a Muslim is not lawful except for one of three things: disbelief after faith, zina after ihsan, and killing a soul without right.' And the hadith is in al-Masabih. (Tabyin al-Haqaiq: 3/549) (Mustakhlas)
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling of stoning (rajm) for the muhsan, i.e., a married person (or one who has previously had valid marital intercourse) who commits zina. The hadd punishment is stoning to death. The judge is to take the convict to a wide open space to perform the stoning. The reason is to maximize the deterrent effect (الاعتبار) and because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did so with Ma'iz and the woman from Ghamid. The passage also cites the famous hadith of 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) listing the three offenses that render a Muslim's blood lawful: apostasy after iman, zina after ihsan (i.e., by a muhsan), and murder without right. This is a core ruling in the chapter of hudud.

Key Terms
المحصن (al-muhsan): In this context, the person who has had valid marital intercourse (whether currently married or previously married) and is thus liable for stoning upon committing zina.
الرجم (al-rajm): Stoning to death as a hadd punishment for the muhsan adulterer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Order of Stoning: Witnesses First, Then Imam, Then People
Ruling on the order of stoning when zina is proven by witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that witnesses must initiate stoning and apply the consequence if they refuse, citing the proof from 'Ali's practice and the principle of repelling hadd through retraction.

Core Idea
If the witnesses to zina refuse to throw the first stones, the entire stoning punishment is dropped — their reluctance is treated as retraction.

This lesson examines a unique procedural rule in Hanafi hudud: when zina is proven by four witnesses, the witnesses themselves must begin the stoning. This requirement serves as a safeguard against false testimony and reflects the principle that hadd punishments are repelled by doubt (shubuhat). We will explore the textual proof from the practice of 'Ali ibn Abi Talib (ra), the inter-madhhab dispute with al-Shafi'i, and the various scenarios that affect the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Step 1: Identify the ruling and its condition
In the text, the first statement is 'The witnesses begin with it; if they refuse, it drops.' This establishes that the beginning of the witnesses is a condition (shart) for the validity of the stoning. Note the hukm: if they refuse, the hadd is completely dropped.
The text uses the phrase 'فإن أبوا سقط' to indicate the consequence.
2
Step 2: Locate the primary proof (dalil)
The text narrates the action of 'Ali ibn Abi Talib (ra) when stoning Sharaha al-Hamdaniyyah. He stated that if a witness had testified, the witness would be the first to throw the stone. This establishes the sunna. Identify the operative phrase: 'أول من يرمي الشاهد'.
This is a dalil naqli from the practice of a companion, which is considered authoritative in Hanafi usul.
3
Step 3: Understand the rationale and the inter-madhhab debate
The text explains that beginning with the witness is a stratagem (ihtiyal) to repel hadd punishments. The witness may retract upon direct involvement. Then the text contrasts with al-Shafi'i and Abu Yusuf who analogize to flogging. Analyze the Hanafi counter-argument: flogging does not necessarily cause death, but stoning is destruction, hence a stricter condition is justified.
This step highlights the difference between qiyas and istihsan/strategic reasoning.
4
Step 4: Apply the condition to various scenarios
The text discusses what happens if witnesses refuse, die, go blind, apostatize, etc. In each case, if the witness cannot or does not begin, the hadd drops (according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). The exception is if the witnesses are physically unable but willing, then stoning proceeds in their presence. Trace the logic: any indication of retraction negates the proof.
Note the intra-Hanafi disagreement: Abu Yusuf holds that if witnesses refuse/die/disappear, the imam still stoning, but this is not the mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويبدأ الشهود به، فإن أبوا سقط، ثم الإمام، ثم الناس، ويبدأ الإمام لو مقراً، أي بالرحم أي أمر القاضي : بجلده أي ثم يبدأ الإمام شر أي بالرحم أي لو كان الزاني بالزنا ويبدأ الشهود به: أي إذا ثبت الزنا بالشهود، والرجم على الزاني فيبدأ الشهود برجمه ولو بحصاة صغيرة إلا لعذر كمرض فيرجم بحضرتهم فبداءة الشهود بالرجم رط بدليل قوله : "فإن أبوا" سقط"، ولو قتله إنسان أو فقأ عينه بعد الحكم بالرجم فهدر، وينبغي أن يعزر ، ولو قبل القضاء بالرجم يجب القصاص في العمد، والدية الخطأ، فيبدأ الشهود؛ لما روي عن علي الله أنه قال حين رجم شراحة الهمدانية: إن الرجم سنة سنها رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ولو كان شهد على هذه أحد لكان أول من يرمي الشاهد، ثم يتبع شهادته حجره، لكنها أقرت فأنا أول من رماها بحجر، قال الراوي: ثم رمى الناس وأنا فيهم ولأن الشاهد قد يتجاسر على أداء الشهادة ثم يستعظم المباشرة، فيرجع، فكان في بداية الشاهد احتيالاً لدرأ الحدود، وقال الشافعي وأبو يوسف في رواية: لا يشترط بداية الشاهد اعتباراً بالجلد، قلنا: عدم اشتراط البداية في الجلد لمعنى أنه ربما يقع مهلكاً، والهلاك غير مستحق في الجلد، ولا كذلك في الرجم؛ لأنه إتلاف. (مستخلص، فتح) من كان منهم ذا فإن أبوا سقط أي فإن أبى الشهود كلهم أو بعضهم عن البداية بالرجم سقط الرجم؛ لأن الإباء دلالة الرجوع وكذلك لو غابوا أو ماتوا أو مات بعضهم ولو بعد القضاء أو صار أعمى أو أخرس أو ارتد أو قذف فحد، وعند الثلاثة: لا يسقط الرحم وعن أبي يوسف إذا امتنعوا أو ماتوا أو غابوا رجم الإمام ثم الناس وإن كان الشهود مرضى لا يستطيعون أن يرموا أو مقطوعي الأيدي رجم بحضرتهم بخلاف ما إذا قطعت أيديهم بعد الشهادة، وقوله: ثم الإمام ثم الناس لما روينا عن أثر علي الله ويقصدون بذلك مقتله إلا أن رحم محرم منه فإنه لا يقصد مقتله. (مستخلص، فتح، عيني) أبوا: أي الشهود من البداءة بالرجم . (ط) عيني) ثم الناس: أي يبدأ الناس ويصطفون كصفوف الصلاة كلما رجم قوم تنحوا ورجم آخرون. (عيني)
And the witnesses begin with it; if they refuse, it drops. Then the imam, then the people. And the imam begins if (the confessor) confesses. 'And the witnesses begin with it': i.e., when zina is proven by witnesses, and the stoning is upon the adulterer, the witnesses begin stoning him, even with a small pebble, unless there is an excuse like illness; then stoning is carried out in their presence. So the beginning of the witnesses with stoning is established by his statement: 'If they refuse, it drops.' And if a person kills him or gouges out his eye after the judgment of stoning, it is of no account (hader), and he should be reprimanded (ta'zir). And if before the judgment of stoning, then qisas is obligatory for intentional act, and diyah for mistake. So the witnesses begin; because it is narrated from 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) that he said when stoning Sharaha al-Hamdaniyyah: 'Stoning is a sunna established by the Messenger of Allah. If anyone had testified against this woman, the first to throw would be the witness, then his stone would follow his testimony. But she confessed, so I am the first to throw a stone at her.' The narrator said: Then the people threw stones, and I was among them. And because the witness may become bold in giving testimony but then find the act severe and retract, so beginning with the witness is a stratagem (ihtiyal) to repel the hadd punishments. Al-Shafi'i and Abu Yusuf (in one narration) said: The beginning of the witness is not a condition, analogizing to flogging. We say: The lack of condition for beginning in flogging is because it may cause death, and death is not deserved in flogging, unlike stoning because it is destruction. (Mustakhlas, Fath) 'If they refuse, it drops': i.e., if all or some of the witnesses refuse to begin the stoning, the stoning drops because refusal is an indication of retraction. Similarly, if they disappear, die, or some of them die, even after the judgment, or if a witness becomes blind, mute, apostatizes, or is convicted of qadhf and then flogged, then according to the three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) the stoning does not drop. And from Abu Yusuf: if they refuse, die, or disappear, the imam stones and then the people. And if the witnesses are sick and unable to throw, or have their hands cut off, stoning is carried out in their presence, unlike if their hands are cut off after testimony. And his statement: 'then the imam, then the people' based on the athar of 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him). And they intend thereby his killing, except if the stoner is a relative, then he is not intended to kill him. (Mustakhlas, Fath, Ayni) 'Abaw': i.e., the witnesses from beginning with stoning. (T, Ayni) 'Then the people': i.e., the people begin and line up like rows of prayer; whenever a group stones they move aside and others stone. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage details the procedure for stoning when zina is proven by four witnesses. The ruling: the witnesses must be the first to throw stones (even with a small pebble). If they refuse, the hadd of stoning drops entirely, because their refusal is taken as an indication of retraction (ruju'). After the witnesses, the imam stones, and then the general public. The reason for starting with witnesses is twofold: first, the precedent of 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) when stoning Sharaha al-Hamdaniyyah, where he stated that if witnesses had testified, they would throw first. Second, the wisdom is that a witness may be bold in testifying but then shrink from executing the punishment, so requiring them to begin acts as a deterrent against false testimony and provides an opportunity for them to retract, thus repelling the hadd. The text also addresses a dispute: al-Shafi'i and Abu Yusuf (in one narration) do not require the witnesses to begin, analogizing to flogging where the witnesses do not necessarily begin. The Hanafi response is that flogging is not intended to kill, whereas stoning is destruction, hence the difference. Further details: if witnesses are unable to throw due to illness or missing hands, stoning is still carried out in their presence. Various scenarios affecting the obligation are discussed, such as death, apostasy, or blinding of witnesses after testimony. The people stone in rows, similar to prayer rows, each group throwing and then leaving.

Key Terms
البداءة (al-bidayah): The requirement that the witnesses be the first to throw stones in stoning punishment.
الإباء (al-iba'): Refusal of the witnesses to begin stoning, which is considered as retraction (ruju') and drops the hadd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if the witnesses to zina refuse to throw the first stones during stoning?
A) The imam proceeds with the stoning instead.
B) The stoning is postponed until they agree.
C) The stoning is dropped and the accused is released.
D) The witnesses are punished for refusal.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the witnesses to zina must begin stoning; their refusal is treated as retraction, causing the entire hadd to drop.

Stoning Procedure for Confessor and Flogging for Non-Muhsan
Ruling on stoning when confessor and flogging of non-muhsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi procedure for stoning a confessor and the flogging punishment for a non-muhsan, and explain the evidence from the sunnah.

Core Idea
For a confessor, the imam initiates stoning; for a non-muhsan, flogging with a knotless whip is prescribed.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses two distinct scenarios in the hudud for zina: the procedure when the offender confesses and is muhsan (eligible for stoning), and the punishment for a non-muhsan offender. The Hanafi school relies on prophetic precedent to establish that the imam begins the stoning for a confessor, while flogging for a non-muhsan must be administered with a whip free of knots to prevent excessive harm—demonstrating the school's concern for proportionality even in mandatory punishments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
The passage covers two situations: (1) a muhsan who confesses to zina, and (2) a non-muhsan (free or slave) whose zina is proven by confession or witnesses.
The ruling for a muhsan proven by witnesses is not discussed here.
2
Determine the ruling for each
For the muhsan confessor: stoning, with the imam throwing the first stone. For the non-muhsan: flogging (100 lashes for free, 50 for slave) with a whip without knots.
The whip condition applies only to flogging.
3
Examine the dalil for the imam's role
The Prophet stoned al-Ghamidiyyah first with a pebble, then commanded the people to throw, establishing that the imam initiates. 'Ali did similarly with Sharaha al-Hamdaniyyah.
The dalil is a hadith ahad (zanni al-thubut) but relied upon in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Analyze the conditions for flogging
The whip must have no knots (la thamara lahu) to prevent each lash from causing two wounds. If the offender is weak, flogging is administered lightly according to his capacity.
This reflects the principle of raf' al-haraj (removing hardship).
5
Understand the post-punishment rites
After stoning, the body is washed, shrouded, and funeral prayer is performed, indicating that the executed person is treated as a Muslim and given proper burial.
This distinguishes stoning for zina from execution for apostasy or brigandage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويبدأ الإمام لو مقراً أي لو كان الزاني مقراً بالزنا ففي رجمه يرمي الحجارة أولاً الإمام ثم الناس؛ لأنه عليها رمى الغامدية بحصاة مثل الحمصة ثم قال للناس: "ارموا"، وكانت أقرت بالزنا. رمز الحقائق: ۳۷۹/۱] ولأن علياً الله رحم الهمدانية كذلك وقال: ولكنها أقرت فأنا أول من رماها بحجر كما مر . (محشي) ثم الناس ويغسل ويكفن ويصلى عليه. (عيني) ولو غير محصن: أي لو كان المشهود عليه بالزنا أو المقر بالزنا غير محصن أمر الإمام بجلده مائة جلدة، وللعبد نصفها أي خمسين بسوط أي الآلة التي يضرب بها لا ثمرة ،له وثمرة السوط مستعارة من ثمرة الشجر وهي ذنبه وطرفه وعذبته والمشهور في الكتب لا ثمرة له أي لا عقدة له؛ لأن كل ضربة بها تصير ضربتين، وإن كان الرجل الذي وجب عليه الحد ضعيف الخلقة، فخيف عليه الهلاك إذا ضرب، يجلد جلداً خفيفاً مقدار ما يتحمله .
And the imam begins if (the confessor) confesses: i.e., if the adulterer confesses to zina, then in his stoning, the imam first throws stones, then the people; because he (peace be upon him) stoned al-Ghamidiyyah with a pebble like a chickpea, then said to the people: 'Throw,' and she had confessed to zina. (Ramz al-Haqaiq: 1/379) And because 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) stoned al-Hamdaniyyah similarly and said: 'But she confessed, so I am the first to throw a stone at her,' as mentioned. (Muhashshi) 'Then the people, and he is washed, shrouded, and prayed upon.' (Ayni) 'And if (the adulterer) is not muhsan': i.e., if the one against whom zina is proven by witnesses or the confessor of zina is not muhsan, the imam orders him to be flogged one hundred lashes, and for a slave half of that, i.e., fifty, with a whip (sawt) which is the instrument with which one strikes. It should have no 'thamar' (knot/end piece); 'thamarat al-sawt' is borrowed from the fruit of a tree, meaning its tail, edge, or tip. The well-known statement in the books is: 'No thamar for it,' i.e., no knot, because each strike with it becomes two strikes. And if the man on whom the hadd becomes obligatory is weak in physique, and it is feared that he might die if struck, he is flogged lightly to the extent he can bear.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage covers two distinct procedures. First, when zina is proven by confession (iqrar), the order of stoning differs: the imam (or judge) himself begins throwing stones, followed by the people. This is based on the Prophet's treatment of al-Ghamidiyyah and 'Ali's treatment of Sharaha al-Hamdaniyyah, both of whom confessed; the imam threw the first stone. After stoning, the body is washed, shrouded, and the funeral prayer is performed (i.e., unlike those killed in combat). Second, for the non-muhsan (unmarried or never validly married) person, the punishment is flogging: 100 lashes for a free person, 50 for a slave. The whip must be without knots (la thamara lahu) to avoid causing excessive injury, as a knotted whip would effectively strike twice per lash. If the guilty one is weak and flogging may kill him, the flogging is to be administered lightly, according to what he can bear. This reflects the Hanafi emphasis on proportionality and avoiding unnecessary harm in hudud punishments.

Key Terms
غير المحصن (ghayr al-muhsan): A person who has never had valid marital intercourse (i.e., unmarried or divorced without consummation?) and is liable for flogging rather than stoning.
السوط (al-sawt): The whip used for flogging; it should have no knots (la thamara lahu) to prevent it from causing multiple wounds per strike.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the punishment for a free, non-muhsan person who commits zina?
A) Stoning to death.
B) One hundred lashes with a whip without knots.
C) Fifty lashes and banishment.
D) Imprisonment for one year.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between stoning for a muhsan confessor (imam starts) and flogging for a non-muhsan (100/50 lashes, whip without knots, leniency for the weak), based on prophetic precedent.

Witnesses Must Begin Stoning: The Hanafi Condition
Ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition that witnesses must initiate stoning, explain the proof from the hadith of Ali (RA), and evaluate the Shafi'i objection by analogical reasoning.

Core Idea
The witness's refusal to throw the first stone creates a doubt that drops the entire penalty.

The stoning penalty for zina is severe and irreversible. The Hanafi school, uniquely, requires that the very witnesses who testified must begin the stoning. This lesson explores the rationale: a witness may reconsider when faced with the act. We examine the textual evidence and the opposing view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
In the matn, the author states 'ويبدأ الشهود به' – the witnesses begin the stoning. Note that this is a condition (shart) for the penalty to proceed.
The base text is concise; the commentary expands.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentary cites the practice of Ali (RA) in the case of Shurahah al-Hamdaniyyah. Find the hadith and note that it is a specific action of a Companion, which serves as evidence in Hanafi fiqh.
This hadith is considered ahad but accepted by the Hanafis.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Ali's statement 'لو كان شهد على هذه أحد لكان أول من يرمي الشاهد' directly indicates that the witness should be the first to throw. This shows that initiating stoning is an obligation (wujub) on the witness.
The imperative 'ليكن' is not present, but the context implies it.
4
Understand the opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i and Abu Yusuf (in one narration) argue by analogy (qiyas) to flogging (jald), where the imam begins, not the witnesses. They say that since flogging is also a hadd penalty, the same procedure should apply.
This is a classic example of qiyas being used by the opposing school.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response distinguishes stoning from flogging: stoning is lethal (إتلاف), while flogging is not. Therefore, the witness must be absolutely certain, and their refusal indicates doubt, which triggers dar' al-hudud (warding off the penalty).
This response shows the Hanafi commitment to avoiding capital punishment in cases of doubt.

Book of Hudud. Conditions of Hadd and its rulings. And the witnesses begin with it (stoning), if they refuse it falls, then the Imam, then the people. And the Imam begins if (the offender) confesses. ... (detailed explanation) ... Then the people, and he is washed, shrouded, and prayer is performed over him.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an inter-madhhab dispute on the procedure of stoning for zina. The Hanafi position is that the witnesses who testified must initiate the stoning, even with a small stone. If they refuse, the stoning is dropped because their refusal indicates retraction. This is proven by the hadith of Ali (RA) regarding Shurahah al-Hamdaniyyah. The Shafi’i and Abu Yusuf (in one narration) disagree, analogizing to flogging where the imam begins. The Hanafi response explains that flogging is not lethal, so beginning by the imam is fine, but stoning is lethal, so witnesses must begin to ensure they are certain.

Key Terms
بداية الشهود (bidayat al-shuhud): The requirement that the witnesses physically begin the stoning by throwing the first stones.
درأ الحدود (dar' al-hudud): The principle of warding off prescribed penalties by any doubt or uncertainty.
إباء (iba'): Refusal of the witnesses to begin stoning, considered a sign of retraction of testimony.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires witnesses to initiate stoning; their refusal drops the penalty, reflecting the principle of warding off penalties by doubts.

Consequences of Witnesses' Refusal and Variations in Stoning Procedure
Ruling statement with detailed scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the rulings when witnesses refuse, die, become incapacitated, or when the offender confesses, and apply the principle of dar' al-hudud to these scenarios.

Core Idea
The witness's refusal is treated as a retraction, but if physically unable, the penalty is still carried out; confession shifts the responsibility to the imam.

The previous lesson covered the requirement that witnesses begin stoning. This lesson examines the practical scenarios: what constitutes a valid refusal? What if witnesses die or become incapable? And how does the procedure differ when the offender confesses rather than being convicted by witnesses? Understanding these details is essential for a complete grasp of Hanafi hudud law.

Guided Path
1
Interpret the phrase 'فإن أبوا سقط'
The phrase means if they refuse to begin, the penalty drops. Refusal can be explicit or implied by absence, death, or other incapacities that prevent initiation.
Refusal is taken as a sign of retraction (ibaa).
2
Analyze the scenarios
The text lists several situations: refusal by all or some witnesses, absence, death (even after judgment), blindness, muteness, apostasy, or qadhf. In each case, the penalty is dropped.
There is an intra-Hanafi difference: according to the three imams, death after judgment may not drop the penalty? The text seems to favor dropping.
3
Note the exception for physical incapacity
If witnesses are ill, have lost hands, or otherwise cannot throw but are present, the stoning is carried out in their presence. Only voluntary refusal drops the penalty.
This distinguishes inability from unwillingness.
4
Understand the ruling on confession
If the offender confesses, the imam begins the stoning, not the witnesses. This is based on the Prophet's (saw) practice with al-Ghamidiyyah.
Confession provides certainty, so the witnesses' role in ensuring certainty is unnecessary.
5
Grasp the underlying principle
All these rulings serve the same principle of dar' al-hudud – ensuring that the penalty is only carried out when certainty is guaranteed. Refusal creates doubt; confession removes doubt.
The Hanafi school prioritizes avoiding execution over carrying it out.

كتاب الحدود
شرائط الحد وأحكامها
ويبدأ الشهود به، فإن أبوا سقط، ثم الإمام، ثم الناس، ويبدأ الإمام لو مقراً،
أي بالرحم
الناس، ولو غير محصن جلده
أي أمر القاضي :
بجلده
أي ثم يبدأ الإمام
شر
أي بالرحم
أي لو كان الزاني بالزنا
ويبدأ الشهود به: أي إذا ثبت الزنا بالشهود، والرجم على الزاني فيبدأ الشهود برجمه ولو بحصاة صغيرة إلا لعذر كمرض فيرجم بحضرتهم فبداءة الشهود بالرجم رط بدليل قوله : "فإن أبوا" سقط"، ولو قتله إنسان أو فقأ عينه بعد الحكم بالرجم فهدر، وينبغي أن يعزر ، ولو قبل القضاء بالرجم يجب القصاص في العمد، والدية الخطأ، فيبدأ الشهود؛ لما روي عن علي الله أنه قال حين رجم شراحة الهمدانية: إن الرجم سنة سنها رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ولو كان شهد على هذه أحد لكان أول من يرمي الشاهد، ثم يتبع شهادته حجره، لكنها أقرت فأنا أول من رماها بحجر، قال الراوي: ثم رمى الناس وأنا فيهم ولأن الشاهد قد يتجاسر على أداء الشهادة ثم يستعظم المباشرة، فيرجع، فكان في بداية الشاهد احتيالاً لدرأ الحدود، وقال الشافعي وأبو يوسف في رواية: لا يشترط بداية الشاهد اعتباراً بالجلد، قلنا: عدم اشتراط البداية في الجلد لمعنى أنه ربما يقع مهلكاً، والهلاك غير مستحق في الجلد، ولا كذلك في الرجم؛ لأنه إتلاف. (مستخلص، فتح)
من
كان
منهم
ذا
فإن أبوا سقط أي فإن أبى الشهود كلهم أو بعضهم عن البداية بالرجم سقط الرجم؛ لأن الإباء دلالة الرجوع وكذلك لو غابوا أو ماتوا أو مات بعضهم ولو بعد القضاء أو صار أعمى أو أخرس أو ارتد أو قذف فحد، وعند الثلاثة: لا يسقط الرحم وعن أبي يوسف إذا امتنعوا أو ماتوا أو غابوا رجم الإمام ثم الناس وإن كان الشهود مرضى لا يستطيعون أن يرموا أو مقطوعي الأيدي رجم بحضرتهم بخلاف ما إذا قطعت أيديهم بعد الشهادة، وقوله: ثم الإمام ثم الناس لما روينا عن أثر علي الله ويقصدون بذلك مقتله إلا أن رحم محرم منه فإنه لا يقصد مقتله. (مستخلص، فتح، عيني) أبوا: أي الشهود من البداءة بالرجم . (ط) عيني) ثم الناس: أي يبدأ الناس ويصطفون كصفوف الصلاة كلما رجم قوم تنحوا ورجم آخرون. (عيني) ويبدأ الإمام لو مقراً أي لو كان الزاني مقراً بالزنا ففي رجمه يرمي الحجارة أولاً الإمام ثم الناس؛ لأنه عليها رمى الغامدية بحصاة مثل الحمصة ثم قال للناس: "ارموا"، وكانت أقرت بالزنا. رمز الحقائق: ۳۷۹/۱] ولأن علياً الله رحم الهمدانية كذلك وقال: ولكنها أقرت فأنا أول من رماها بحجر كما مر . (محشي) ثم الناس ويغسل ويكفن ويصلى عليه. (عيني)
Book of Hudud. Conditions of Hadd and its rulings. And the witnesses begin with it (stoning), if they refuse it falls, then the Imam, then the people. And the Imam begins if (the offender) confesses. ... (detailed explanation) ... Then the people, and he is washed, shrouded, and prayer is performed over him.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an inter-madhhab dispute on the procedure of stoning for zina. The Hanafi position is that the witnesses who testified must initiate the stoning, even with a small stone. If they refuse, the stoning is dropped because their refusal indicates retraction. This is proven by the hadith of Ali (RA) regarding Shurahah al-Hamdaniyyah. The Shafi’i and Abu Yusuf (in one narration) disagree, analogizing to flogging where the imam begins. The Hanafi response explains that flogging is not lethal, so beginning by the imam is fine, but stoning is lethal, so witnesses must begin to ensure they are certain.

Key Terms
إباء (iba'): Refusal of the witnesses to begin stoning, considered a sign of retraction.
مقر (muqirr): One who confesses to zina. In such a case, the imam begins stoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the offender confesses to zina, who begins the stoning?
A) The witnesses
B) The imam
C) The people
D) The judge

Key Takeaway
The stoning penalty is dropped if witnesses refuse, die, or become incapacitated, ensuring execution only with full certainty; confession shifts initiation to the imam.

Flogging for Zina: Method and Conditions
Ruling on flogging method and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi method for flogging a non-muhsan zani and explain the conditions regarding the whip, clothing, and positioning, citing the Quranic proof.

Core Idea
Flogging for zina is a fard punishment, but its execution must prevent harm while ensuring deterrence.

The punishment for zina when the offender is non-muhsan (unmarried) is flogging. However, Islamic law does not leave the method to arbitrary cruelty. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq details the precise conditions: the whip, the clothing, the distribution of lashes, and the posture of the offender. These rules ensure the punishment fulfills its purpose of deterrence without becoming a tool of destruction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is flogging (jald) for a non-muhsan (ghayr muhsan) offender of zina. The ruling is fard (obligatory) on the Imam to carry out.
This is established by Quran 24:2.
2
Locate the primary proof
The Quranic verse is the direct evidence. The imperative 'fajlidu' indicates obligation, and '100' is the prescribed number.
The chain: Quran → Qat'i thubut and dalala → fard.
3
List the mandatory conditions (shurut and wajibat)
Identify the requirements: whip without knots, moderate force, removal of certain clothes, distribution over the body excluding head/face/private parts, and standing for men and sitting for women.
These are derived from hadith and practice of the Companions.
4
Note the ikhtilaf within and between schools
Shafi'i restricts lashes to the back. Abu Yusuf allowed one lash on the head. The Hanafi response rejects these views based on hadith 'protect the face and private parts' and reinterpretation of Abu Yusuf's proof.
The mufta bihi is to avoid head, face, and private parts entirely.
5
Apply the ruling to a hypothetical scenario
Given a free non-muhsan confessing to zina, the Qadi must order 100 lashes with a knotless whip, distributed over the body except the prohibited areas, the man standing and the woman sitting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو غير محصن: أي لو كان المشهود عليه بالزنا أو المقر بالزنا غير محصن أمر الإمام بجلده مائة جلدة، وللعبد نصفها أي خمسين بسوط أي الآلة التي يضرب بها لا ثمرة له وثمرة السوط مستعارة من ثمرة الشجر وهي ذنبه وطرفه وعذبته والمشهور في الكتب لا ثمرة له أي لا عقدة له؛ لأن كل ضربة بها تصير ضربتين، وإن كان الرجل الذي وجب عليه الحد ضعيف الخلقة، فخيف عليه الهلاك إذا ضرب، يجلد جلداً خفيفاً مقدار ما يتحمله . 

كتاب الحدود
۹۲
شرائط الحد وأحكامها
مائة، وتصف للعبد، بسوط لا ثمرة له متوسطاً، وينزع عنه ثيابه، وفرق على أي المائة
متعلق بقوله جلده أي لا عقدة له
الزاني
أي الجلد والضرب
بدنه إلا رأسه ووجهه وفرجه، ويضربُ الرجل قائماً في الحدود غير ممدود، ولا ينزع
أي أعضائه كلها
قيل وصدره وبطنه
ثيابها إلا الفرو والحشو، وتضرب جالسة.
أي حال كونه قائماً كلها والتعزير
وقوله : "متوسطاً" منصوب على أنه صفة لمصدر محذوف أي جلداً متوسطاً، وهو أن يكون بين المبرح وغير المؤلم، فإن المبرح يفضي إلى الهلاك، وغير المؤلم لا يحصل به الزجر المشروع من الحد. رمز الحقائق: ۳۷۹/۱] (مسكين) مائة: أي مائة جلدة؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿الزَّانِيَةُ وَالزَّانِي فَاجْلِدُوا كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا مِائَةَ جَلْدَةٍ ﴾ (النور: ٢). (عيني) ونصف للعبد: لأن الرق منصف للنعمة فكذا العقوبة. (عيني) متوسطاً صفة لمصدر محذوف أي جلده جلداً متوسطاً بين المبرح المؤلم وغير المؤلم. (عيني) وينزع عنه ثيابه : أي ينزع ثياب الرجل الذي يجلد دون الإزار؛ لأن عليا له كان يأمر بالتجريد في الحدود، ولأنه أبلغ في إيصال الألم، غير أن في نزع الإزار كشف العورة ، وكذا ينزع الثياب في سائر الحدود سوى حد القذف. (مستخلص، فتح) وفرق على بدنه أي يفرق الضرب على أعضائه؛ لأن الجمع في عضو واحد يفضي إلى التلف، والحد شرع زاجراً لا متلفاً، وقوله: "إلا رأسه ووجهه وفرجه" أي لا يضرب رأسه ووجهه وفرجه؛ لقوله عليه للجلاد: "اتقوا الوجه والمذاكير تبيين الحقائق: ٥٥٥/٣] ولأن الرأس مجمع الحواس، والوجه مجمع المحاسن، فلو ضرب على الرأس أو الوجه فلا يؤمن من فوات شيء منها بالضرب وذلك إهلاك معنى، والضرب على الفرج متلف، وقال الشافعي: يخص بالضرب ظهره، وقال أبو يوسف آخراً: يضرب الرأس أيضاً سوطاً واحداً، وعن بعض أصحابنا: لا يضرب الصدر والبطن أيضاً؛ لأنه متلف كالرأس، وقول أبي يوسف يضرب الرأس بسوط؛ لقول أبي بكر : اضربوا الرأس فإن فيه شيطاناً، قلنا: تأويله أنه كان مباح القتل فقد نقل أنه قال في حربي كان من دعاة الكفرة والإهلاك فيه مستحق. (مستخلص، فتح عيني) ويضرب الرجل إلخ في الحدود والتعزير؛ لما أخرجه عبد الرزاق عن علي الله أنه قال: يضرب الرجل قائماً، والمرأة قاعدة في الحد، وقوله: "غير ممدود اختلف في معناه، فقيل: لا يلقى على الأرض ولا يمد رجلاه، وقيل: إن الجلاد لا يمد يده فوق رأسه للضرب، وقيل: إن الجلاد بعد ما أوقع السوط على بدن المجلود لا يمده، والخلاف إنما هو في بيان المعنى المراد من قوله : "غير ممدود مع اتفاقهم على كراهة كل ذلك؛ لما فيه من الزيادة على المستحق، والرجل والمرأة في ذلك سواء. (عيني، فتح) غير ممدود: أي حال كونه غير ملقى على الأرض. (عيني) ولا ينزع ثيابها أي ثياب المرأة؛ لأن في نزعها كشف العورة. رمز الحقائق: ۳۸۰/۱۸] إلا الفرو والحشو: لأنهما يمنعان وصول الألم إلى الجسد. (عيني) جالسة : أي حال كونها جالسة؛ لأنه أستر لها. (عيني)
And if (the offender) is non-muhsan: i.e., if the one testified against or the confessor is non-muhsan, the Imam orders his flogging: 100 lashes, and for the slave half, i.e. fifty, with a whip that has no knob (thamar), moderate, and his clothes are removed, and (the lashes) are distributed over his body except his head, face, and private parts. The man is struck standing in hudud, not stretched out, and her clothes are not removed except the fur and padding, and she is struck sitting.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage provides the detailed ruling (hukm) for flogging the non-muhsan (unmarried) offender of zina. The proof is the Quranic verse (24:2). The flogging is 100 lashes for a free person and 50 for a slave. The whip must be moderate, without knots, to avoid excessive harm. The clothing of the man is removed except for the izaar (waist wrapper) to preserve modesty. The woman's clothes are not removed except heavy garments that prevent pain. The man is struck standing, the woman sitting. The blows are distributed over the body, avoiding the head, face, and private parts, as these areas are vulnerable. A dispute with Shafi'i and Abu Yusuf is noted: Shafi'i restricts to the back; Abu Yusuf allows one lash on the head based on a report from Abu Bakr, but the Hanafi response interprets that report as applying to a combatant, not a hudud offender.

Key Terms
غير محصن (ghayr muhsan): A person who has never been married or is not currently in a valid marriage, thus liable to flogging for zina.
ثمرة السوط (thamarat al-sawt): The knob or knot at the end of a whip; a whip without a knot is used to avoid severe cuts.
متوسطا (mutawassitan): Moderate; between harsh and painless, to achieve deterrence without killing.
غير ممدود (ghayr mamdud): Not stretched out; the person flogged should not be laid on the ground or have limbs stretched.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many lashes are given to a free non-muhsan for zina according to the Hanafi school?
A) 80
B) 100
C) 50
D) 40

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prescribes a balanced flogging for zina: 100 lashes for a free person, 50 for a slave, with a knotless whip, moderate force, distributed over the body except head/face/private parts, the man standing and the woman sitting.

Execution of Hadd for Zina: Flogging and Stoning Procedures and Master's Authority
Commentary on conditions and execution of hadd for zina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the execution of flogging for zina (type of whip, position of the offender, areas to avoid) and explain why a master cannot execute hadd on his slave without the imam's permission.

Core Idea
Hadd is a deterrent, not a punishment to kill — the whip is medium, vital areas avoided, and only the imam executes it.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq expands on the procedural details of executing the hadd punishment for zina. It clarifies the number of lashes, the type of whip, the position of the offender, and which body parts are struck. It also addresses a critical dispute: whether a master may flog his own slave without the imam's permission. By studying this lesson, you will understand the Hanafi emphasis on preserving life and dignity even in punishment, and the principle that hudud are the rights of Allah, executed only by His deputy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the components of flogging execution
The passage specifies number of lashes, whip type, clothing removal, distribution over body, and position of the offender. Identify each component from the text.
Use the terms in the arabic_clean: مائة, نصف للعبد, سوط لا ثمرة له متوسطاً, ينزع عنه ثيابه, يفرق على بدنه, يضرب قائماً, تضرب جالسة.
2
Analyze the master's authority dispute
Two positions are presented: the Hanafi view requiring imam's permission, and the Shafi'i view allowing the master to execute. Look for the proofs (hadith) and the Hanafi response (takhsis or interpretation).
The key phrase: 'ولا يحد عبده إلا بإذن إمامه' and the opposing hadith about flogging the slave-girl.
3
Understand the rationale behind the rulings
Why is the whip medium? Why avoid head/face? Why is a pit dug for women in stoning? The underlying principles are to prevent death, preserve dignity, and maintain modesty. Connect each ruling to its legal purpose (zajr, ihtisham, etc.).
Look for phrases like 'لأن الجمع في عضو واحد يفضي إلى التلف' and 'أستر لها'.

(عيني) ونصف للعبد: لأن الرق منصف للنعمة فكذا العقوبة. (عيني) متوسطاً صفة لمصدر محذوف أي جلده جلداً متوسطاً بين المبرح المؤلم وغير المؤلم. (عيني) وينزع عنه ثيابه : أي ينزع ثياب الرجل الذي يجلد دون الإزار؛ لأن عليا له كان يأمر بالتجريد في الحدود، ولأنه أبلغ في إيصال الألم، غير أن في نزع الإزار كشف العورة ، وكذا ينزع الثياب في سائر الحدود سوى حد القذف. (مستخلص، فتح) وفرق على بدنه أي يفرق الضرب على أعضائه؛ لأن الجمع في عضو واحد يفضي إلى التلف، والحد شرع زاجراً لا متلفاً، وقوله: "إلا رأسه ووجهه وفرجه" أي لا يضرب رأسه ووجهه وفرجه؛ لقوله عليه للجلاد: "اتقوا الوجه والمذاكير تبيين الحقائق: ٥٥٥/٣] ولأن الرأس مجمع الحواس، والوجه مجمع المحاسن، فلو ضرب على الرأس أو الوجه فلا يؤمن من فوات شيء منها بالضرب وذلك إهلاك معنى، والضرب على الفرج متلف، وقال الشافعي: يخص بالضرب ظهره، وقال أبو يوسف آخراً: يضرب الرأس أيضاً سوطاً واحداً، وعن بعض أصحابنا: لا يضرب الصدر والبطن أيضاً؛ لأنه متلف كالرأس، وقول أبي يوسف يضرب الرأس بسوط؛ لقول أبي بكر : اضربوا الرأس فإن فيه شيطاناً، قلنا: تأويله أنه كان مباح القتل فقد نقل أنه قال في حربي كان من دعاة الكفرة والإهلاك فيه مستحق. (مستخلص، فتح عيني) ويضرب الرجل إلخ في الحدود والتعزير؛ لما أخرجه عبد الرزاق عن علي الله أنه قال: يضرب الرجل قائماً، والمرأة قاعدة في الحد، وقوله: "غير ممدود اختلف في معناه، فقيل: لا يلقى على الأرض ولا يمد رجلاه، وقيل: إن الجلاد لا يمد يده فوق رأسه للضرب، وقيل: إن الجلاد بعد ما أوقع السوط على بدن المجلود لا يمده، والخلاف إنما هو في بيان المعنى المراد من قوله : "غير ممدود مع اتفاقهم على كراهة كل ذلك؛ لما فيه من الزيادة على المستحق، والرجل والمرأة في ذلك سواء. (عيني، فتح) غير ممدود: أي حال كونه غير ملقى على الأرض. (عيني) ولا ينزع ثيابها أي ثياب المرأة؛ لأن في نزعها كشف العورة. رمز الحقائق: ۳۸۰/۱۸] إلا الفرو والحشو: لأنهما يمنعان وصول الألم إلى الجسد. (عيني) جالسة : أي حال كونها جالسة؛ لأنه أستر لها. (عيني)

ويحفر لها في الرّجم لا له، ولا يحدّ عبده إلا بإذن إمامه، وإحصان الرّجم الحرية أي المولى أو أمته يعني إذا فوض إليه أي شرط إحصان الرحم سبعة
الله
ويحفر لها في الرجم لا له: أي يحفر حفرة لرجم المرأة إلى الصدر لا للرجل، فإنه لا يجوز الحفر له، أما الحفر لها فلقول عبد بن بريدة عن أبيه حفرنا للغامدية إلى صدرها، وأما عدم الحفر للرجل، فلقول أبي سعيد: فوالله ما حفرنا لماعز، ولا أوثقناه، رواهما مسلم وأحمد وأبو داود، وإن ترك الحفر لها جاز؛ لأنه عليه لم يوجبه؛ لأنها مستورة بثيابها، والحفر أحسن؛ لأنه أستر. (عيني، فتح) لا له: أي لا يحفر للرجل ولا يربط ولا يمسك. (ط، عيني) ولا يحد عبده إلخ : يعني ليس للمولى أن يقيم الحد على عبده إلا بإذن الإمام، وقال الشافعي: : له أن يقيم عليه الحد الذي هو خالص حق الله تعالى إذا عاين السبب، أو أقر عنده إذا كان المولى ممن يملك الحد بتولية الإمام بأن كان بالغاً عاقلاً حراً، وإن ثبت الحد بالبينة فله فيه قولان وفي حد القذف والقصاص له وجهان، وإن كان المولى مكاتباً أو ذمياً أو امرأة فليس له أن يقيم الحد على مملوكه وبه قال مالك وأحمد؛ لقوله عليه: "إذا زنت أمة أحدكم فتبين ،زناها فليحدها الحد ولا يثرب عليها، ثم إن زنت فليحدها الحد ولا يثرب عليها، ثم إن زنت الثالثة فليبعها ولو بحبل من شعر"، متفق عليه؛ ولأن للمولى ولاية مطلقة عليه فإنه يملك على التصرف فيه ما لا يملك الإمام فصار كالتعزير.
عنه
ولنا: ما روي عن العبادلة الثلاثة موقوفاً ومرفوعاً: أربعة إلى الولاة الحدود والصدقات والجمعات والفيء، وعن علي له مثله؛ ولأن الحد حق الله تعالى؛ لأن الغرض منه إخلاء العالم عن الفساد فلا يستوفيه إلا نائب الشرع وهو الإمام أو نائبه بخلاف التعزير؛ لأنه حق العبد ألا تری أنه يعزر الصبي مع أن حق الشرع موضوع والمراد بما روي التسبيب لمرافعة إلى الحكام لا المباشرة بغير إذن الإمام، أو يكون ذلك إذناً منه عليه للموالي بأن يقيموا الحدود عليهم، وعندنا تجوز إقامته للمولى بإذن الإمام. (مستخلص، عيني) وإحصان الرجم: قيد بإحصان الرجم احترازاً عن إحصان القذف؛ لأن إحصان القذف أن يكون مكلفاً حراً مسلماً عفيفاً عن الزنا، وقيد بالحرية؛ لأن العبد إذا زنى لا رجم عليه، وقيد بالتكليف أي العقل والبلوغ؛ لأن التكليف شرط أهلية العقوبة؛ إذ لا خطاب بدون العقل والبلوغ، وقيد بالإسلام؛ لأنه يؤكد اعتقاد حرمة الزنا، وهذا الشرط عندنا وعن أبي يوسف أن الإسلام ليس بشرط، و به قال الشافعي وأحمد؛ لأن النبي - عليكم رجم يهوديين ولنا: أنه كان ذلك بحكم التوراة قبل نزول آية الجلد في أول ما دخل علي المدينة، وصار منسوخاً بها. ثم نسخ الجلد في حق المحصن، والكافر ليس بمحصن؛ لقوله : "من أشرك بالله فليس بمحصن"، وقيد بالوطء احترازاً عن البكر، فإن حده الجلد، والمراد بالوطء الإيلاج في القبل؛ لأن الواطئ في الدبر لا يرجم، وقيد بالنكاح الصحيح؛ لأن الإحصان يطلق عليه، قال تعالى: ﴿فَإِذَا أُحْصِنَ) (النساء: ٢٥) أي تزوجن، ولأن الرجم أفحش العقوبات، فيستدعي أغلظ الجنايات والجناية في الإقدام على الزنا بعد إصابة الحلال تكون أغلظ، وقيد بقوله: "وهما بصفة الإحصان معناه هما حالة الدخول على صفة الإحصان؛ لأنه لو دخل بالمنكوحة المملوكة أو الكافرة =
The Book of Hudud. Conditions and rulings of the hadd. One hundred, and half for the slave, with a whip that has no knot, medium, and his clothes are removed, and (the lashes) are distributed over his body except his head, face, and private parts. And the man is beaten standing in the hudud, not stretched out, and her clothes are not removed except the fur and padding, and she is beaten sitting. ... And a pit is dug for her in stoning, not for him. And he does not execute the hadd on his slave except with the permission of his imam. And the ihsan for stoning is freedom, etc.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from Kanz al-Daqa'iq on the execution of hadd punishments for zina (unlawful sexual intercourse). It expands on the matn's rulings regarding flogging and stoning. The author begins by stating the number of lashes: 100 for a free person and 50 for a slave, citing the Quranic verse from Surah al-Nur. The whip must be medium intensity—neither so severe as to kill nor so light as to fail as a deterrent. The clothes of the male offender are removed except the waist-wrapper (izar) to avoid exposing the private parts, while the female's clothes remain except thick fur and padding that block the pain. The lashes are distributed over the body, avoiding the head, face, and private parts to prevent inadvertent killing or loss of senses, as per hadith and the principle that hadd is a deterrent, not lethal. The man is beaten standing, the woman seated, following the practice of 'Ali (ra). There is a discussion on the meaning of 'non-stretched' (ghayr mamdud), with various interpretations, but all agree that any form of stretching or additional restraint is disliked as it exceeds the required punishment. The passage then covers stoning: a pit is dug for the woman up to her chest for modesty, but not for the man. The master cannot execute hadd on his slave without the imam's permission—a dispute with al-Shafi'i, who allows it. The Hanafi proof is based on the hadith that four matters go to the rulers: hudud, sadaqat, jumu'ahs, and fay'. Lastly, the conditions of ihsan for stoning are detailed: freedom (slaves are never stoned), legal capacity (maturity and sanity), Islam (a condition in the Hanafi school, though Abu Yusuf disagrees; the Hanafi response argues the stoning of Jews by the Prophet was before the revelation of the flogging verse, which abrogated it for non-Muslims), actual intercourse (in the front private part), and a valid marriage contract (since ihsan is attained through consummation of a valid marriage). The text cuts off mid-explanation.

Key Terms
حد (hadd): A fixed corporal punishment prescribed by Shariah for specific crimes, considered a right of Allah.
جلد (jald): Flogging with a whip as the hadd punishment for zina (unlawful sexual intercourse).
إحصان (ihsan): A legal status that makes a person eligible for stoning (rajm) upon committing zina; requires being a free, adult, sane Muslim who has consummated a valid marriage.
رجم (rajm): Stoning to death as the hadd punishment for a muhsan (married person) who commits zina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many lashes are prescribed for a slave who commits zina according to the Hanafi school?
A) 100
B) 50
C) 80
D) 40

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prescribes a controlled, deterrent punishment for zina that avoids harm to vital areas and requires imam's permission for execution, upholding the principle that hudud are rights of Allah.

Digging a Pit for Stoning: Ruling and Proof
Ruling on digging a pit for stoning, with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on digging a pit for stoning and identify the hadith evidence for each case.

Core Idea
A pit is dug for the woman for modesty, but not for the man — the Prophet's practice is the proof.

The punishment of stoning (rajm) requires certain procedures to preserve modesty. The Hanafi school specifies that a pit is dug for the woman up to her chest, while no pit is dug for the man. This lesson examines the ruling and the Prophetic practice that establishes it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is digging a pit for the person being stoned. Determine the hukm for a woman and for a man separately.
The ruling differs by gender.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadith are cited: one about al-Ghamidiyyah (woman) and one about Ma'iz (man). Identify each report and its source.
Both are from Muslim, Ahmad, Abu Dawud.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's actual digging for the woman indicates recommendation; his non-digging and not tying Ma'iz indicates prohibition of digging for the man.
The absence of action (tark) can have legal implications.
4
Note the permissibility of leaving it
The commentator states that leaving the pit for the woman is permissible (ja'iz) because the Prophet did not make it obligatory. Understand the distinction between sunnah and wajib.
The woman is covered by her garments, so the pit is only better (ahsan).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويحفر لها في الرّجم لا له: أي يحفر حفرة لرجم المرأة إلى الصدر لا للرجل، فإنه لا يجوز الحفر له، أما الحفر لها فلقول عبد بن بريدة عن أبيه حفرنا للغامدية إلى صدرها، وأما عدم الحفر للرجل، فلقول أبي سعيد: فوالله ما حفرنا لماعز، ولا أوثقناه، رواهما مسلم وأحمد وأبو داود، وإن ترك الحفر لها جاز؛ لأنه عليه لم يوجبه؛ لأنها مستورة بثيابها، والحفر أحسن؛ لأنه أستر. (عيني، فتح) لا له: أي لا يحفر للرجل ولا يربط ولا يمسك. (ط، عيني)
And a pit is dug for her in stoning, not for him: meaning a pit is dug for the stoning of a woman up to the chest, not for a man, for it is not permissible to dig for him. As for digging for her, it is due to the statement of 'Abd ibn Buraydah from his father: 'We dug for al-Ghamidiyyah up to her chest.' As for not digging for the man, it is due to the statement of Abu Sa'id: 'By Allah, we did not dig for Ma'iz, nor did we tie him.' Both are narrated by Muslim, Ahmad, and Abu Dawud. And if one leaves digging for her, it is permissible, because he (the Prophet) did not make it obligatory; because she is covered by her garments, but digging is better because it is more concealing. ('Ayni, Fath) 'Not for him': meaning a pit is not dug for the man, nor is he tied, nor held. (Tahawi, 'Ayni)
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on digging a pit for stoning. For a woman, a pit is dug up to her chest to preserve modesty, as done for al-Ghamidiyyah. For a man, no pit is dug, as was the practice for Ma'iz. The hadith are reliable. Digging is Sunna for a woman but not obligatory; leaving it is permissible. For a man, digging is impermissible and he is not to be tied or held.

Key Terms
الرجم (al-rajm): The punishment of stoning to death for adultery by a muhsan.
الحفر (al-hafr): Digging a pit for the person being stoned, for the woman to her chest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
For whom is a pit dug during stoning according to the Hanafi school?
A) For both the man and the woman
B) For the man only
C) For the woman only
D) For neither

Key Takeaway
For stoning, a pit is dug only for the woman, based on the Prophet's practice; it is recommended but not obligatory.

Master's Authority to Execute Hadd on Slave
Ruling on master executing hadd on his slave, with dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on a master executing hadd on his slave and evaluate the opposing schools' proofs.

Core Idea
A master cannot execute hadd on his slave without the imam's permission — hadd is Allah's right, only His deputy enforces it.

This passage addresses a critical inter-madhhab dispute: can a master personally inflict the fixed punishment (hadd) on his slave? The Hanafi school prohibits it without the imam's permission, while the Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools allow it under certain conditions. The disagreement revolves around the nature of hadd as a right of Allah and the proper interpretation of a relevant hadith. Understanding this dispute highlights the Hanafi emphasis on the imam's exclusive authority over hudud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling
State the explicit ruling from the matn: the master may not execute hadd on his slave except with the imam's permission.
This is the central claim of the text.
2
Understand the opposing view
Describe al-Shafi'i's position: the master can enforce hadd if he witnesses the offense or the slave confesses, provided the master is adult, sane, and free. Note the conditions and exceptions (e.g., if the master is a mukatab, dhimmi, or woman).
Malik and Ahmad agree with certain conditions.
3
Analyze the opposing dalil
Examine the hadith about the slave-girl ('If your slave-girl commits adultery...') and the argument from the master's general authority over the slave.
This hadith is cited by the Shafi'i school as direct permission.
4
Examine the Hanafi response
Consider the Hanafi evidence: the hadith 'Four things are for the rulers' and the reasoning that hadd is a right of Allah, so only His deputy (the imam or his appointee) can enforce it. The opposing hadith is interpreted as a call to bring the matter to the rulers or as a conditional permission with imam's tacit approval.
The Hanafi distinction between hadd (Allah's right) and ta'zir (slave's right) is key.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: in the Hanafi school, the master must go to the qadi to have the hadd carried out; he cannot act alone.
This ensures due process and prevents vigilante justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يحد عبده إلخ : يعني ليس للمولى أن يقيم الحد على عبده إلا بإذن الإمام، وقال الشافعي: له أن يقيم عليه الحد الذي هو خالص حق الله تعالى إذا عاين السبب، أو أقر عنده إذا كان المولى ممن يملك الحد بتولية الإمام بأن كان بالغاً عاقلاً حراً، وإن ثبت الحد بالبينة فله فيه قولان وفي حد القذف والقصاص له وجهان، وإن كان المولى مكاتباً أو ذمياً أو امرأة فليس له أن يقيم الحد على مملوكه وبه قال مالك وأحمد؛ لقوله عليه: "إذا زنت أمة أحدكم فتبين زناها فليحدها الحد ولا يثرب عليها، ثم إن زنت فليحدها الحد ولا يثرب عليها، ثم إن زنت الثالثة فليبعها ولو بحبل من شعر"، متفق عليه؛ ولأن للمولى ولاية مطلقة عليه فإنه يملك على التصرف فيه ما لا يملك الإمام فصار كالتعزير. ولنا: ما روي عن العبادلة الثلاثة موقوفاً ومرفوعاً: أربعة إلى الولاة الحدود والصدقات والجمعات والفيء، وعن علي له مثله؛ ولأن الحد حق الله تعالى؛ لأن الغرض منه إخلاء العالم عن الفساد فلا يستوفيه إلا نائب الشرع وهو الإمام أو نائبه بخلاف التعزير؛ لأنه حق العبد ألا تری أنه يعزر الصبي مع أن حق الشرع موضوع والمراد بما روي التسبيب لمرافعة إلى الحكام لا المباشرة بغير إذن الإمام، أو يكون ذلك إذناً منه عليه للموالي بأن يقيموا الحدود عليهم، وعندنا تجوز إقامته للمولى بإذن الإمام. (مستخلص، عيني)
And he does not execute the hadd on his slave, etc.: meaning it is not for the master to enforce the hadd on his slave except with the permission of the imam. Al-Shafi'i said: He may enforce on him the hadd that is purely the right of Allah if he witnesses the cause, or if the slave confesses before him, provided the master is among those who can own the hadd by delegation of the imam, i.e., being adult, sane, and free. If the hadd is established by evidence, he has two opinions. In the hadd of qadhf and qisas, he has two views. If the master is a mukatab, a dhimmi, or a woman, he may not enforce the hadd on his slave. Malik and Ahmad agreed with this due to his statement: 'If the slave-girl of any of you commits adultery and her adultery is evident, let him execute the hadd on her and not reproach her. Then if she commits adultery, let him execute the hadd and not reproach her. Then if she commits adultery a third time, let him sell her, even for a rope of hair.' Agreed upon. And because the master has absolute authority over him; he possesses the right to dispose of him in ways the imam does not, so it becomes like ta'zir. Our evidence: What is narrated from the three 'Abdullahs, as a stop and as a raised report: 'Four things are for the rulers: the hadd punishments, the charities, the Friday prayers, and the spoils.' And from 'Ali similarly. And because the hadd is a right of Allah; its purpose is to rid the world of corruption, so it should only be carried out by the deputy of the Shari'ah, which is the imam or his deputy, unlike ta'zir because it is a right of the slave. Do you not see that a child is ta'zired although the right of the Shari'ah is not established? And the meaning of what is narrated is to seek to bring the matter to the judges, not direct enforcement without the imam's permission, or that it was a permission from him for the masters to enforce the hadd on them. According to us, it is permissible for the master to enforce it with the imam's permission. (Mustakhlas, 'Ayni)
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about whether a master can execute the hadd punishment on his own slave without the imam's permission. The Hanafi position: He cannot, except with the imam's permission. Al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad argue he can if he witnesses the offense or the slave confesses, based on a hadith about the slave-girl and the master's general authority. The Hanafi response cites the hadith 'Four things are for the rulers' and reasons that the hadd is Allah's right, thus only His deputy can enforce it. The hadith about the slave-girl is interpreted as a reference to the imam's permission or a call to bring the matter to the rulers. The conclusion: The master may enforce the hadd only with the imam's permission.

Key Terms
الحد (al-hadd): Fixed legal punishment for specific crimes, considered a right of Allah.
المولى (al-mawla): The master or owner of a slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when can a master execute the hadd on his slave?
A) Whenever the master witnesses the offense
B) Only with the permission of the imam
C) If the slave confesses to the master
D) The master can never execute hadd

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the master cannot execute hadd on his slave without the imam's permission because hadd is a right of Allah that only His deputy can enforce.
