Conditions of Ihsan for Stoning
Definition and conditions of ihsan for stoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six conditions of ihsan for stoning and explain why Islam is a disputed condition according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Stoning requires both spouses to be muhsan at intercourse; the six conditions guard the severity of the punishment.

Ihsan (the state of being legally protected from stoning) is a key concept in the law of zina. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq details the six conditions that must be present for a person to be subject to stoning (rajm) rather than flogging. Understanding these conditions—and the intra-madhhab debate about the condition of Islam—is essential for accurately applying the Ḥadd punishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term 'ihsan' and its legal function
Recognize that 'ihsan' here refers specifically to the status that triggers stoning for zina. The passage clarifies that this is distinct from 'ihsan' in the context of qadhf (false accusation).
Ihsan is a legal status, not a personal quality.
2
List the six conditions mentioned
From the passage, extract the six conditions: freedom (hurriyya), legal capacity (taklif = sanity and adulthood), Islam, intercourse (wat'), valid marriage (nikah sahih), and both parties being in a state of ihsan at the time of intercourse.
The sixth is not explicitly numbered in the OCR but is mentioned in the commentary as ‘both being in the state of ihsan’.
3
Understand the reasoning for each condition
For each condition, note the legal wisdom (hikma): e.g., slaves are not stoned because their punishment is reduced; minors/insane lack capacity; Islam strengthens deterrence; intercourse excludes virgins; valid marriage excludes doubt; mutual ihsan ensures both enjoy the full grace.
The text emphasizes that ingratitude for abundant grace merits the harshest punishment.
4
Analyze the dispute about the condition of Islam
Abu Yusuf and the Shafi'i/Hanbali schools argue that Islam is not a condition, citing the Prophet's stoning of two Jews. The Hanafi response explains that ruling was under the Torah, later abrogated. The Hanafi position is that a disbeliever cannot be muhsan.
This dispute illustrates how different proofs (naskh, hadith) lead to divergent rulings.
5
Recognize the importance of simultaneity (both muhsan)
The condition that both spouses be muhsan at the time of intercourse means that if one party lacks any condition, neither is muhsan. For example, if the wife is a slave, the husband is not muhsan even if he is free.
This prevents stoning when the ‘complete grace’ is not fully realized.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإحصان الرجم: قيد بإحصان الرجم احترازاً عن إحصان القذف؛ لأن إحصان القذف أن يكون مكلفاً حراً مسلماً عفيفاً عن الزنا، وقيد بالحرية؛ لأن العبد إذا زنى لا رجم عليه، وقيد بالتكليف أي العقل والبلوغ؛ لأن التكليف شرط أهلية العقوبة؛ إذ لا خطاب بدون العقل والبلوغ، وقيد بالإسلام؛ لأنه يؤكد اعتقاد حرمة الزنا، وهذا الشرط عندنا وعن أبي يوسف أن الإسلام ليس بشرط، وبه قال الشافعي وأحمد؛ لأن النبي - عليكم رجم يهوديين ولنا: أنه كان ذلك بحكم التوراة قبل نزول آية الجلد في أول ما دخل علي المدينة، وصار منسوخاً بها. ثم نسخ الجلد في حق المحصن، والكافر ليس بمحصن؛ لقوله : "من أشرك بالله فليس بمحصن"، وقيد بالوطء احترازاً عن البكر، فإن حده الجلد، والمراد بالوطء الإيلاج في القبل؛ لأن الواطئ في الدبر لا يرجم، وقيد بالنكاح الصحيح؛ لأن الإحصان يطلق عليه، قال تعالى: ﴿فَإِذَا أُحْصِنَ) (النساء: ٢٥) أي تزوجن، ولأن الرجم أفحش العقوبات، فيستدعي أغلظ الجنايات والجناية في الإقدام على الزنا بعد إصابة الحلال تكون أغلظ، وقيد بقوله: "وهما بصفة الإحصان معناه هما حالة الدخول على صفة الإحصان؛ لأنه لو دخل بالمنكوحة المملوكة أو الكافرة =  كتاب الحدود ٩٤ شرائط الحد وأحكامها والتكليف والإسلام والوطء بنكاح صحيح وهما بصفة الإحصان، ولا يجمع بين أي الإمام جلد ،ورجم وجلد ونفي، ولو غرب بما يرى صح في المحصن بل يرجم فقط أي بعدة جوزها أي سياسة أو المجنونة أو الصبية لا يكون محصناً؛ لعدم تكامل النعمة؛ إذ الطبع يتنفر عن صحبة المجنونة، وقل ما يرغب في الصبية؛ لقلة رغبتها، وكذا بالمملوكة حذراً عن رق الولد، وكذا تقل الألفة اختلاف الدين في الكافرة خلافاً مع لأبي يوسف، والأصل في هذا أن كفران النعمة يتغلظ عند تكاملها وتكثرها، فهذه الأشياء من جلائل النعم فتكون مزجرة عن الزنا، فعند ارتكابه مع وجود هذه النعم يجب قتله، وكذا لو كان الزوج عبداً أو صبياً أو مجنوناً أو كافراً وهي حرة مسلمة عاقلة بالغة لم تكن محصنة. فإن قلت: كيف يتصور أن يكون الزوج كافراً والمرأة مسلمة؟ قلت صورته أن يكونا كافرين فأسلمت المرأة ودخل بها الزوج قبل عرض الإسلام على الزوج، ولا يعتبر العلم والشرف في إحصان الرجم مع كونهما من جلائل النعم؛ لأن الشرع لم يرد باعتبارهما ولا يمكن نصب الشرع بالرأي ثم المعتبر في الوطء الإيلاج على وجه يوجب الغسل سواء أنزل أو لم ينزل. (مستخلص، عيني) بنكاح صحيح السادس: أن يكون الوطء بالنكاح الصحيح فلا يرجم إذا وطئ بنكاح فاسد أو شبهة. (عيني، مس)
And the ihsan for stoning is restricted to: freedom, taklif, Islam, intercourse in a valid marriage, and both being in the state of ihsan. The condition of freedom is because a slave is not stoned. Taklif means sanity and puberty because it is a condition for the capacity for punishment; there is no address without sanity and puberty. The condition of Islam is because it strengthens belief in the prohibition of zina, and this condition is according to us, though Abu Yusuf holds that Islam is not a condition, and al-Shafi'i and Ahmad agree with him because the Prophet stoned two Jews; our response was that this was by the ruling of the Torah before the revelation of the verse of flogging, and it was abrogated. Then flogging was abrogated for the muhsan, and the disbeliever is not muhsan due to his statement: 'Whoever associates partners with Allah is not muhsan.' The condition of intercourse is to exclude the virgin, whose punishment is flogging, and intercourse means genital penetration, because one who penetrates the anus is not stoned. The condition of valid marriage because ihsan is predicated on it, as Allah said: 'And when they are muhsan (married)' (4:25). The condition of both being in the state of ihsan means at the time of entry they are ihsan; because if he enters the married woman who is a slave, or the disbeliever, or the insane, or the minor, he is not muhsan due to lack of complete grace; for the nature is repelled by the company of an insane woman, and men rarely desire a minor girl; similarly with a slave woman to avoid enslavement of the child; and likewise the lack of affinity due to difference of religion with a disbelieving woman, contrary to Abu Yusuf. The principle is that ingratitude for grace is magnified when grace is complete and abundant. These things are great graces that deter from zina, so when one commits it despite these graces, he must be killed. Similarly if the husband is a slave, minor, insane, or disbeliever while she is free, Muslim, sane, and adult, she is not muhsan. If you ask: How can it be that the husband is a disbeliever and the wife is Muslim? I say: Its image is that they were both disbelievers, then the woman embraced Islam, and the husband had entered her before the presentation of Islam to him. And knowledge and honor are not considered in the ihsan of stoning, despite being great graces, because the Shari'ah has not considered them, nor can Shar'i rulings be established by opinion. Then what is considered in intercourse is penetration in a way that necessitates ghusl, whether or not he ejaculates. (Mustakhlas, 'Ayni) 'By valid marriage' is the sixth condition: that the intercourse be in a valid marriage, so he is not stoned if he has intercourse in a void marriage or under a doubt. ('Ayni, Mus)
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage defines the conditions of ihsan for stoning. Six conditions: freedom, sanity and puberty (taklif), Islam, intercourse, valid marriage, and both being muhsan at the time of intercourse. Each condition is justified: slaves are not stoned; minors and insane are not addressed; Islam strengthens deterrence; intercourse must be vaginal in valid marriage; and the couple must be muhsan at entry. The debate with Abu Yusuf and Shafi'i about Islam is based on the incident of the Jews. The principle: ingratitude for graces is worse when graces are abundant. Also, if one party is not muhsan (slave, minor, insane, disbeliever), the other is not muhsan. The text resolves a hypothetical: a Muslim woman married to a disbeliever who converted after marriage. Knowledge and honor are not conditions.

Key Terms
الإحصان (al-ihsan): The status of being married and having sexual intercourse in a valid marriage, leading to stoning for zina.
التكليف (al-taklif): Legal capacity based on sanity and puberty.
الرجم (al-rajm): Stoning to death as punishment for zina committed by a muhsan person.
المحصن (al-muhsan): A person who meets the conditions of ihsan and is therefore subject to stoning if he/she commits zina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Stoning a fornicator requires six strict conditions—including Islam and mutual ihsan—ensuring the punishment is only applied when complete grace has been fully enjoyed.

The Ruling: No Combining Flogging and Stoning for the Muhsan
Ruling that flogging and stoning are not combined for muhsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the punishment for a muhsan and explain the evidence from the Prophet's practice and the response to the Zahiri argument.

Core Idea
For a muhsan, stoning alone suffices; combining flogging is both unproven and redundant.

This lesson examines a key ruling in Hanafi hudud: the punishment for a muhsan who commits zina. While some schools argue for flogging followed by stoning, the Hanafi school maintains that only stoning is required. The basis is the consistent practice of the Prophet ﷺ and a rational critique of the Zahiri position. You will learn the evidence and the reasoning behind the Hanafi view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What is being ruled upon? The punishment for a muhsan. Ruling: Only stoning, no flogging.
2
Locate the dalil
The Prophet's practice with Ma'iz, al-Ghamidiyyah, and the woman of al-'Usayf — he stoned them without flogging.
This is a Sunnah fi'liyyah (action-based) evidence.
3
Analyze the Zahiri objection
The Zahiris cite the action of 'Ali flogging Sharrah then stoning her as proof for combining punishments.
This is a qawl al-sahabi (Companion's statement/action).
4
Respond to the objection
The Hanafi response: either 'Ali did not know Sharrah was muhsan until after flogging, or his action is a personal opinion that does not outweigh the Prophet's practice and the consensus of the Companions.
This shows the hierarchy of evidence: Sunnah > Companion's action.
5
Consider the rational argument
Flogging is redundant because stoning already achieves the deterrent purpose (zajr i'tibari).
This is a talil (rational reasoning) supporting the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجمع بين جلد ورجم: يعني في المحصن؛ لأنه عليه لم يجمع بين الجلد والرجم في ماعز، ولا في الغامدية، ولا في المرأة التي زنى بها العسيف بل رجمهم من غير جلد، وقالت الظاهرية يجلد ثم يرجم؛ لأن علياً لله جلد شراحة ثم رجمها قلنا هذا الفعل عنه؛ إما لأنه لم يثبت عنده إحصانها إلا بعد جلدها، أو هو رأي لا يقاوم إجماع الصحابة، ولا ما ذكرنا عن رسول الله ﷺ؛ ولأن الجلد يعري عن الفائدة؛ لأن الزجر الاعتباري يحصل بالرجم، فيكون فيه ارتكاب أمر بلا فائدة. (مستخلص، فتح)
And flogging and stoning are not combined: meaning for the muhsan; because he (the Prophet) did not combine flogging and stoning for Ma'iz, nor for al-Ghamidiyyah, nor for the woman with whom the hired man committed adultery, but rather stoned them without flogging. The Zahiris said he should be flogged then stoned because 'Ali flogged Sharrah and then stoned her. We say this action of his is either because he did not confirm her ihsan until after flogging, or it is an opinion that does not outweigh the consensus of the Companions, nor what we mentioned from the Messenger of Allah; and because flogging is devoid of benefit since the deterrent effect is achieved by stoning, so it would be doing something without benefit. (Mustakhlas, Fath)
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof that for a muhsan, only stoning is administered, not flogging. The Prophet's practice with Ma'iz, al-Ghamidiyyah, and the woman of al-'Usayf confirms this. The Zahiris argue for both based on 'Ali's action, but the Hanafi response is that 'Ali's action was due to uncertainty about ihsan or is a lesser opinion not overriding the Prophet's practice and the consensus of the Companions. Also, flogging would be redundant.

Key Terms
الظاهرية (al-Zahiriyyah): A school that follows apparent meaning of texts; they argued for combining punishments.
المحصن (al-muhsan): A person who is free, adult, Muslim, and has had valid married intercourse; the condition for stoning punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What punishment does a muhsan receive for zina according to the Hanafi school?
A) Flogging only
B) Stoning only
C) Flogging then stoning
D) Either flogging or stoning

Key Takeaway
For a muhsan, stoning alone is the hadd punishment; flogging is neither combined nor required.

No Combining Flogging and Banishment for the Virgin (Non-Muhsan)
Ruling that flogging and banishment are not combined for a virgin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on banishment for a virgin, identify the Shafi'i evidence, and explain the Hanafi response including the argument of abrogation and policy.

Core Idea
For the virgin, only flogging is the hadd; banishment is policy, not punishment.

This passage addresses a well-known dispute between the Hanafi school and the majority (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) regarding whether banishment is part of the fixed punishment (hadd) for a non-muhsan fornicator. The Hanafi school argues that the Quranic text specifies only flogging, and the hadith cited by opponents is abrogated or interpreted as discretionary policy. Understanding this dispute reveals how the Hanafi school prioritizes textual strictness and considers practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The hadd for a virgin is only flogging of 100 lashes; banishment is not part of the hadd.
2
Identify the opposing school's view
Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad hold that banishment is part of the hadd, based on the hadith.
3
Analyze the opposing dalil
The hadith 'The virgin with the virgin is flogged one hundred and exiled for a year.'
4
Examine the Hanafi response
The Quranic text (24:2) only mentions flogging; adding banishment is abrogation. Additionally, banishment can cause corruption, as shown by 'Umar's experience.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Hanafi qadis only flog; Shafi'i qadis also banish if possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و جلد ونفي: يقال: نفي فلان من بلده إذا أخرج أي لا يجمع في البكر بين الجلد والإخراج عن البلد، وقال الشافعي: إن تمام حد غير المحصن أن يخرج بعد الجلد إلى موضع بينه وبين الزانية مسيرة سفر؛ لقوله عليها: "البكر بالبكر جلد مائة ونفي سنة"، رواه الجماعة إلا البخاري والنسائي، وبه قال مالك وأحمد، ولنا: أن النص جعل الجلد مائة، والزيادة على مطلق النص نسخ، وما رواه منسوخ، ولأن في التغريب أي الإخراج تعريضاً لها على الفساد، ولهذا قال علي : كفى بالنفي فتنة، وعمر الله نفى شخصاً فارتد ولحق بدار الحرب، فحلف أن لا ينفي بعده أبداً، وبهذا عرف أن نفيهم كان بطريق السياسة والتعزير، لا بطريق الحد؛ لأن مثل يحلف أن لا يقيم الحد. رمز الحقائق: ۳۸۱/۱] (فتح)
And flogging and banishment: it is said: so-and-so is banished from his land if he is expelled, meaning flogging and expulsion from the land are not combined for a virgin. Al-Shafi'i said: The complete punishment for a non-muhsan is that he be expelled after flogging to a place a travel distance away from the fornicator, due to his statement: 'The virgin with the virgin is flogged one hundred and exiled for a year.' Narrated by all except Bukhari and Nasa'i. Malik and Ahmad agreed. Our evidence: The text made flogging one hundred, and any addition to the absolute text is abrogation, and what he narrated is abrogated. And because in banishment, i.e., expulsion, there is an exposure to corruption. For this reason, 'Ali said: 'Banishment is sufficient as a trial.' And 'Umar banished a person who then apostatized and joined the enemy territory, so he swore not to banish anyone ever again. And by this it is known that their banishment was by way of policy and ta'zir, not by way of hadd; because such a person swears not to enforce the hadd. (Fath, Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1:381)
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute about whether a virgin (non-muhsan) should be both flogged and banished. The Hanafi position: Only flogging is the hadd; banishment is not part of the hadd. Al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad argue for both based on a hadith. The Hanafi response: The Quranic text only mentions flogging; addition is abrogation. Also, banishment may lead to corruption, as seen in 'Umar's experience. Therefore, banishment is a matter of policy (siyasah), not hadd.

Key Terms
النفي (al-nafy): Banishment from the land as a punishment; here debated as part of hadd or ta'zir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Flogging of one hundred lashes
B) Flogging of one hundred lashes and banishment for a year
C) Banishment only
D) Stoning to death

Key Takeaway
For a virgin, the Hanafi hadd is only flogging; banishment is an optional policy (ta'zir), not a fixed punishment.

Banishment as Discretionary Political Punishment
Ruling on banishment as discretionary political punishment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on banishment (taghrib), identify who may order it, and distinguish it from fixed hudud punishments.

Core Idea
Banishment is not a hadd but a discretionary policy of the imam for public benefit.

Banishment (taghrib) is sometimes misunderstood as a fixed punishment for zina. However, the Hanafi school classifies it as a discretionary political measure (siyasah) that the just imam may employ for any crime if he deems it beneficial. This lesson clarifies the nature, scope, and authority behind this punishment, distinguishing it from the fixed hudud and emphasizing that it lies solely with the ruler, not the qadi or mufti.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is banishment (taghrib) ordered by the imam. The ruling is that it is permissible (ja'iz) under the imam's discretionary policy (siyasah). It is not a fixed hadd punishment.
The source states 'صح النفي سياسة' — the banishment is valid as siyasah.
2
Determine the authority and conditions
Only the just, knowledgeable imam (al-Imam al-'Adil al-'Alim) who possesses insight (tadbir wa ra'y) may order banishment. He must see a genuine public benefit (maslahah).
The text says 'لو حبس الإمام العالم العادل صاحب التدبير والرأي' — if the just, knowledgeable, insightful imam imprisons/banishes for a period he sees as beneficial.
3
Contrast with fixed hudud
Unlike hudud (e.g., lashing for zina), banishment is not restricted to specific crimes or evidence. It is a ta'zir/policy tool, not a fixed divine punishment.
The text explicitly says 'وهذا لا يختص بالزنا، بل في كل جناية' — it is not specific to zina but applies to every crime.
4
Note the scope and limits
Banishment applies to any crime where the imam sees benefit (salah). The imam sets the duration based on his judgment. The qadi and mufti have no role in ordering banishment.
'والقاضي ولا المفتي' — neither qadi nor mufti has a role.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو غرب بما يرى صح المراد بالتغريب الحبس يعني لو حبس الإمام العالم العادل صاحب التدبير والرأي. (عيني، فتح)] أي لو نفي الإمام العادل بمدة يرى مصلحة صح النفي سياسة، وهذا لا يختص بالزنا، بل في كل جناية رأى الإمام المصلحة في النفي فله ذلك، والسياسة هي فعل الحاكم شيئاً لمصلحة يراها وإن لم يرو بذلك الفعل دليل خبري، والحكم بالسياسة شرع مغلظا إلا أنه لا دخل للقاضي فيها ولا للمفتي وهي نوعان: -
And if he banishes according to what he sees is correct, the meaning of taghrib is imprisonment, meaning if the just, knowledgeable, possessing insight and opinion imam imprisons (or banishes) for a period he sees as beneficial, the banishment is valid as policy. This is not specific to zina, but in every crime where the imam sees benefit in banishment, he may do so. And siyasah is the action of the ruler for a benefit he sees, even if no transmitted evidence is seen for that action. And ruling by siyasah is a strict Shari'ah, but the qadi and mufti have no role in it. And it is of two types:
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage clarifies that banishment (taghrib) in the Hanafi school is not a fixed hadd but a discretionary political punishment (siyasah) that the just imam may employ for any crime if he deems it beneficial. It is not limited to zina. The imam acts based on public interest, not necessarily a text. This is distinct from the fixed hudud. The qadi and mufti do not decide such punishments; it is solely the imam's prerogative.

Key Terms
السياسة (al-siyasah): Discretionary policy of the ruler for public benefit without explicit textual evidence.
التغريب (al-taghrib): Banishment or exile; in this context, it is synonymous with imprisonment (حبس) as a discretionary punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Banishment is a discretionary tool of the just imam for public benefit, not a fixed punishment, and only he may wield it.

Conditions for Ihsan and Who Is Considered Muhsan
Defines ihsan and its conditions for hadd al-rajm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions of ihsan (taklif, Islam, valid marriage) and identify which spouses qualify as muhsan based on these conditions.

Core Idea
Ihsan requires both spouses to be free, adult, Muslim, and married validly — incomplete blessing means no stoning.

The hadd of stoning (rajm) is one of the most severe punishments in Islamic law. But it only applies to a specific category of offenders: those who are muhsan. This lesson defines what constitutes ihsan by examining the conditions the Hanafi school requires. Understanding these conditions is crucial to correctly applying the ruling, especially in cases involving differences of religion or status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two core conditions of ihsan
From the opening sentence, extract that taklif (legal capacity) and Islam are the primary conditions, paired with valid marital intercourse. Note: The passage says 'wa huma bi sifati al-ihsan' meaning both are conditions of ihsan.
2
List the cases where a wife is not muhsan
The text specifies an insane woman, minor girl, slave woman, and disbelieving woman (against Abu Yusuf). For each, state the reason: lack of complete blessing.
3
Examine the husband's status
If the husband is a slave, minor, insane, or disbeliever, the wife is not muhsan. Understand the reasoning: the blessing is incomplete for the husband, so it does not deter him properly.
4
Understand the underlying principle (ta'lil)
The text links ihsan to the completeness of the blessing (ni'mah). When the blessing is complete, ingratitude (kufran al-ni'mah) is more grievous, so sex outside marriage warrants death. This justifies the conditions.
5
Clarify the condition of intercourse
Intercourse must be in a valid marriage and involve insertion requiring ghusl. Fasid marriage or shubhah does not create ihsan. This prevents stoning in ambiguous situations.

كتاب الحدود شرائط الحد وأحكامها والتكليف والإسلام والوطء بنكاح صحيح وهما بصفة الإحصان. أي المجنونة أو الصبية لا يكون محصناً؛ لعدم تكامل النعمة؛ إذ الطبع يتنفر عن صحبة المجنونة، وقل ما يرغب في الصبية؛ لقلة رغبتها، وكذا بالمملوكة حذراً عن رق الولد، وكذا تقل الألفة اختلاف الدين في الكافرة خلافاً لأبي يوسف، والأصل في هذا أن كفران النعمة يتغلظ عند تكاملها وتكثرها، فهذه الأشياء من جلائل النعم فتكون مزجرة عن الزنا، فعند ارتكابه مع وجود هذه النعم يجب قتله، وكذا لو كان الزوج عبداً أو صبياً أو مجنوناً أو كافراً وهي حرة مسلمة عاقلة بالغة لم تكن محصنة. فإن قلت: كيف يتصور أن يكون الزوج كافراً والمرأة مسلمة؟ قلت صورته أن يكونا كافرين فأسلمت المرأة ودخل بها الزوج قبل عرض الإسلام على الزوج، ولا يعتبر العلم والشرف في إحصان الرجم مع كونهما من جلائل النعم؛ لأن الشرع لم يرد باعتبارهما ولا يمكن نصب الشرع بالرأي ثم المعتبر في الوطء الإيلاج على وجه يوجب الغسل سواء أنزل أو لم ينزل. (مستخلص، عيني) بنكاح صحيح السادس: أن يكون الوطء بالنكاح الصحيح فلا يرجم إذا وطئ بنكاح فاسد أو شبهة. (عيني، مس)
The Book of Hudud: Conditions of the Hadd and its Rulings: Legal capacity, Islam, and intercourse in a valid marriage, and both are conditions of ihsan. So the insane woman or the minor girl is not considered muhsan, due to the lack of completeness of the blessing; for nature is averse to companionship with an insane woman, and one rarely desires a minor girl due to her lack of desire. Likewise with a female slave, out of caution for the enslavement of the child. Likewise, affection diminishes due to difference of religion in a disbelieving woman, contrary to Abu Yusuf. The basis of this is that ingratitude for the blessing is aggravated when the blessing is complete and abundant. These things are among the great blessings, so they serve as deterrents against zina. Thus, when one commits zina despite the presence of these blessings, his execution is obligatory. Likewise, if the husband is a slave, a minor, insane, or a disbeliever while the woman is a free, Muslim, sane, adult, she is not muhsan. If you say: How can the husband be a disbeliever and the woman a Muslim? I say: Its form is that both were disbelievers, then the woman embraced Islam and the husband had intercourse with her before presenting Islam to the husband. Knowledge and honor are not considered in ihsan for stoning, even though they are among the great blessings, because the Shari'ah has not considered them, and the Shari'ah cannot be established by opinion. Then what is considered in intercourse is insertion that necessitates ghusl, whether he ejaculated or not. (Mustakhlas, 'Ayni) In a valid marriage: The sixth is that intercourse be in a valid marriage, so one is not stoned if he had intercourse in a fasid marriage or under shubhah. ('Ayni, Mas.)
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage defines ihsan, the condition required for the hadd of stoning (rajm). The author states that the two essential conditions of ihsan are legal capacity (taklif) and Islam, plus intercourse in a valid marriage. He then explains who is not considered muhsan: a woman who is insane or a minor does not qualify because the blessing (ni'mah) is not complete—people naturally avoid an insane spouse and rarely desire a minor. Similarly, a slave woman is excluded to avoid potential enslavement of the child. A Muslim man married to a disbelieving woman is not muhsan due to lack of affection caused by religious difference; Abu Yusuf disagreed on this point. The underlying principle is that ingratitude for blessings is aggravated when blessings are abundant; these blessings deter one from zina, so committing zina despite them warrants the death penalty. The text also addresses the case where the husband is a slave, minor, insane, or disbeliever while the wife is a free adult Muslim—she is not muhsan because the husband lacks the fullness of blessing. A hypothetical question is answered: how can a Muslim woman have a disbelieving husband? The scenario is when both were disbelievers, she embraced Islam, and he had intercourse before Islam was presented to him. Knowledge and honor are not considered for ihsan even though they are great blessings, because the Shari'ah does not recognize them. Finally, the condition of intercourse is clarified: it must be insertion requiring ghusl, regardless of ejaculation, and must occur in a valid marriage (nikah sahih) to qualify for ihsan; intercourse in a fasid marriage or under shubhah does not lead to stoning.

Key Terms
الإحصان (al-ihsan): A state of being free, adult, Muslim, and married in a valid marriage, which subjects the adulterer to stoning.
التكليف (al-taklif): Legal capacity; being of sound mind and having reached the age of majority (bulugh).
الوطء بنكاح صحيح (al-wat' bi nikah sahih): Sexual intercourse that is lawful by virtue of a valid Islamic marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A Muslim man is married to a Jewish woman. They have valid conjugal relations. If he commits zina with another woman, is he considered a muhsan for the purpose of stoning?
A) Yes, because he is Muslim and married.
B) No, because his wife is a disbeliever, so the blessing is incomplete.
C) Yes, because the marriage is valid and he is of sound mind.
D) No, because he must be married to a Muslim woman to be muhsan.

Key Takeaway
Ihsan is defined by complete blessing: both spouses must be free, adult, Muslim, and have engaged in valid marital intercourse.

Combining Lashing and Stoning for the Muhsan
Ruling on combining lashing and stoning for muhsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on combining lashing and stoning for the muhsan and explain the evidence from the Prophet's practice and the Zahiri rebuttal.

Core Idea
The Prophet never combined lashing and stoning; lashing becomes redundant when stoning suffices.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position that a muhsan adulterer is only stoned, not lashed. The source contrasts the prophetic practice with an incident involving 'Ali and defends the Hanafi view using consensus (ijma) and the principle of avoiding pointless acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what legal act is being discussed and the hukm assigned to it by the Hanafi school.
The act is the punishment for a muhsan (married) adulterer; the Hanafi ruling is stoning only, not lashing.
2
Examine the prophetic practice
Review the cases of Ma'iz, al-Ghamidiyyah, and the woman in the Asif story where the Prophet stoned without lashing.
These incidents provide the primary proof (dalil naqli) for the Hanafi view.
3
Analyze the Zahiri objection
Consider the Zahiri claim that lashing should precede stoning, based on 'Ali's treatment of Sharahah.
The Hanafi response explains that 'Ali's action was either due to a later discovery of ihsan or was his personal ijtihad, not overriding the Prophet's practice.
4
Understand the Hanafi legal reasoning
Appreciate the argument that lashing would be devoid of benefit (bilā fā'idah) since stoning provides full deterrence.
This is a logical (qiyās) argument: if lashing adds nothing, it should not be performed.
5
Identify the ruling anatomy
Break down the ruling into its components: hukm level, conditions, and dispute type.
The hukm is wajib (hadd); the act is punishment for muhsan; the dispute is with Zahiris who combine punishments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجمع بين جلد ورجم: يعني في المحصن؛ لأنه عليه لم يجمع بين الجلد والرجم في ماعز، ولا في الغامدية، ولا في المرأة التي زنى بها العسيف بل رجمهم من غير جلد، وقالت الظاهرية يجلد ثم يرجم؛ لأن علياً جلد شراحة ثم رجمها قلنا هذا الفعل عنه؛ إما لأنه لم يثبت عنده إحصانها إلا بعد جلدها، أو هو رأي لا يقاوم إجماع الصحابة، ولا ما ذكرنا عن رسول الله؛ ولأن الجلد يعري عن الفائدة؛ لأن الزجر الاعتباري يحصل بالرجم، فيكون فيه ارتكاب أمر بلا فائدة. (مستخلص، فتح) وجلد ونفي يقال: نفي فلان من بلده إذا أخرج أي لا يجمع في البكر بين الجلد والإخراج عن البلد، وقال الشافعي: إن تمام حد غير المحصن أن يخرج بعد الجلد إلى موضع بينه وبين الزانية مسيرة سفر؛ لقوله عليها: "البكر بالبكر جلد مائة ونفي سنة"، رواه الجماعة إلا البخاري والنسائي، وبه قال مالك وأحمد، ولنا: أن النص جعل الجلد مائة، والزيادة على مطلق النص نسخ، وما رواه منسوخ، ولأن في التغريب أي الإخراج تعريضاً لها على الفساد، ولهذا قال علي: كفى بالنفي فتنة، وعمر الله نفى شخصاً فارتد ولحق بدار الحرب، فحلف أن لا ينفي بعده أبداً، وبهذا عرف أن نفيهم كان بطريق السياسة والتعزير، لا بطريق الحد؛ لأن مثل يحلف أن لا يقيم الحد. (فتح) ولو غرب بما يرى صح المراد بالتغريب الحبس يعني لو حبس الإمام العالم العادل صاحب التدبير والرأي. (عيني، فتح) أي لو نفي الإمام العادل بمدة يرى مصلحة صح النفي سياسة، وهذا لا يختص بالزنا، بل في كل جناية رأى الإمام المصلحة في النفي فله ذلك، والسياسة هي فعل الحاكم شيئاً لمصلحة يراها وإن لم يرو بذلك الفعل دليل خبري، والحكم بالسياسة شرع مغلظا إلا أنه لا دخل للقاضي فيها ولا للمفتي وهي نوعان: سياسة ظالمة فالشريعة تحرمها وسياسة عادلة تخرج الحق من الظالم وتدفع المظالم وتردع أهل الفساد ويتوصل بها إلى المقاصد الشرعية، فالشريعة توجب المصير إلى هذه السياسة أي العمل بها جائز شرعاً بالنسبة للسلطان ونائبه إذا غلب على ظنه أن ظهور الحق يتوقف على العمل بها ولا يجوز أن يعمل بها القاضي والمفتي، وجه صحة السياسة في النفي أنه عليها نفى المخنث، ونفى عمر الله نصر بن الحجاج، وكان غلاماً صبيحاً تفتتن به النساء، والجمال لا يوجب النفي، ولكن فعل ذلك لمصلحة رآها، وقال في النهاية: المراد بالتغريب الحبس، وهو أحسن وأسكن للفتنة من نفيه إلى إقليم آخر، ولهذا كان الحبس حداً في ابتداء الإسلام دون النفي، وحمل النفي المذكور في قطاع الطريق عليه (فتح)
And there is no combining of lashing and stoning: meaning for the muhsan, because he (the Prophet) did not combine lashing and stoning for Ma'iz, nor for al-Ghamidiyyah, nor for the woman with whom al-Asif committed zina, but he stoned them without lashing. The Zahiris said: he should be lashed then stoned, because 'Ali lashed Sharahah then stoned her. We say: this action of his was either because her ihsan was not established to him until after her lashing, or it is an opinion that does not counter the consensus of the Companions, nor what we mentioned from the Messenger of Allah; and because lashing becomes devoid of benefit, since the deterrent effect is achieved by stoning, so it would be committing an act without benefit. (Mustakhlas, Fath) And lashing and exile: It is said: so-and-so was exiled from his country, i.e., they are not combined for the virgin (non-muhsan) between lashing and expulsion from the country. Al-Shafi'i said: The complete hadd of the non-muhsan is that he be taken out after lashing to a place a travel distance away from the woman, due to his saying: 'The virgin for the virgin: one hundred lashes and exile for a year', reported by all except al-Bukhari and al-Nasa'i, and Malik and Ahmad said the same. Our evidence: that the text made it one hundred lashes, and adding to an absolute text is abrogation, and what he narrated is abrogated. And because exile (taghrib) exposes them to corruption. For this reason 'Ali said: 'Exile is sufficient as a trial.' And 'Umar exiled a person who then apostatized and joined the enemy territory, so he swore that he would never exile again after that. By this it is known that their exile was by way of policy and ta'zir, not by way of hadd, for a person like that would swear not to establish the hadd. (Fath) And if he exiled according to what he sees as correct: The meaning of taghrib is imprisonment, i.e., if the knowledgeable, just, prudent ruler imprisons him. („Ayni, Fath) i.e., if the just ruler exiles for a duration he sees as beneficial, the exile is valid as policy. This is not specific to zina, but rather for every crime where the ruler sees benefit in exile, he may do so. Al-siyasah is the ruler doing something for a benefit he sees, even if no transmitted evidence is seen for that action. The ruling of siyasah is legally valid but restricted; the judge and mufti have no part in it. It is of two types: oppressive policy, which the Shari'ah prohibits, and just policy that extracts rights from the oppressor, removes injustices, deters the corrupt, and achieves legal objectives. The Shari'ah requires resorting to this policy, i.e., acting upon it is legally permissible for the sultan and his deputy if it becomes likely that the manifestation of truth depends on it. The judge and mufti may not act on it. The validity of siyasah in exile is that the Prophet exiled the effeminate man, and 'Umar exiled Nasr ibn al-Hajjaj who was a handsome young man that women were tempted by; beauty does not necessitate exile, but he did it for a benefit he saw. And it is said in al-Nihayah: The meaning of taghrib is imprisonment, which is better and more calming for fitna than exiling to another region. Therefore imprisonment was a hadd in early Islam, not exile. The exile mentioned for highway robbers is applied to it. (Fath)
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage addresses two key issues: (1) combining penalties for the muhsan, and (2) combining penalties for the non-muhsan (virgin). For the muhsan, the Hanafi school holds that only stoning is carried out; lashing is not combined because the Prophet did not do so in the cases of Ma'iz and al-Ghamidiyyah. The Zahiris argued for combining based on `Ali's actions, but the Hanafi response is that `Ali's action was either due to uncertainty about ihsan or was a personal opinion that does not outweigh the practice of the Prophet and the consensus of the Companions. Moreover, lashing becomes redundant when stoning suffices for deterrence. For the non-muhsan, the Hanafis maintain that the only penalty is one hundred lashes; exile (nafy) is not part of the hadd. This contradicts al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad, who argue for adding a year of exile based on a hadith. The Hanafi position is that this hadith is abrogated because the Qur'anic text says 'one hundred lashes' and adding to an absolute text is considered abrogation if it claims to be part of the original command. Furthermore, exile can lead to corruption, as experienced by `Umar when an exile apostatized. Thus, Hanafis view exile as a matter of siyasah (policy) for the ruler, not a fixed hadd. The passage then discusses siyasah in detail: it is permissible for the ruler to exile for any crime if he sees a benefit, even without specific textual evidence. This policy is distinct from the fixed hadd and is left to the ruler's discretion. The preferred form of 'taghrib' is actually imprisonment, which is more effective in preventing fitna than geographical exile.

Key Terms
المحصن (al-muhsan): A person who has had valid consummated marriage and is free, adult, and Muslim.
الجلد (al-jald): Lashing, a fixed punishment (hadd) for zina for non-muhsan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is lashing not combined with stoning for the muhsan?
A) Because the Qur'an prohibits lashing for the muhsan.
B) Because the Prophet never did it, and lashing would be redundant.
C) Because the muhsan is already punished by losing his family.
D) Because stoning alone is more merciful.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that stoning for the muhsan is never combined with lashing, based on the Prophet's practice and the principle of avoiding pointless acts.

Exile for the Non-Muhsan: Hadd or Siyasah?
Ruling on exile for non-muhsan: hadd or siyasah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Hanafi view that exile (nafy) is siyasah (policy) and the Shafi'i view that it is part of the hadd, and explain the evidence and practical consequence.

Core Idea
Exile after lashing for the non-muhsan is abrogated; it is a discretionary policy, not a fixed hadd.

This lesson addresses the dispute whether an unmarried adulterer should be exiled after lashing. Hanafis argue that exile is not part of the Qur'anic text and was abrogated; it is a matter left to the ruler's policy (siyasah). Shafi'is, Malikis, and Hanbalis consider it an integral part of the hadd based on a hadith.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on the non-muhsan punishment
The Hanafi school holds that the full hadd for a non-muhsan is 100 lashes only; exile is not part of it.
This contrasts with the majority view.
2
Present the opposing view (Shafi'i et al.)
The Shafi'i school and others argue that exile for one year is part of the hadd, based on the hadith 'The virgin for the virgin: 100 lashes and exile for a year.'
This hadith is reported by Muslim, among others.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response using naskh
Hanafis argue that the Qur'anic text (24:2) only mentions lashing; any addition is abrogation (naskh) of the original command.
They consider the conflicting hadith as mansūkh, because the Prophet's later practice (and the practice of 'Umar) showed exile was harmful.
4
Examine the policy (siyasah) argument
Hanafis argue that even if exile was used by the Prophet or 'Umar, it was an act of siyasah (discretionary policy) not hadd. They cite 'Umar's experience with an apostate exile and his subsequent oath to never exile again.
This shows that exile is not a fixed punishment but a tool for public good.
5
Understand the meaning of taghrib as imprisonment
The preferred Hanafi interpretation of taghrib is imprisonment (habs), not geographical exile, as it is more effective in preventing fitna.
This aligns with the principle that the ruler may order imprisonment as siyasah for any crime.

(فتح) ولو غرب بما يرى صح المراد بالتغريب الحبس يعني لو حبس الإمام العالم العادل صاحب التدبير والرأي. (عيني، فتح) أي لو نفي الإمام العادل بمدة يرى مصلحة صح النفي سياسة، وهذا لا يختص بالزنا، بل في كل جناية رأى الإمام المصلحة في النفي فله ذلك، والسياسة هي فعل الحاكم شيئاً لمصلحة يراها وإن لم يرو بذلك الفعل دليل خبري، والحكم بالسياسة شرع مغلظا إلا أنه لا دخل للقاضي فيها ولا للمفتي وهي نوعان: سياسة ظالمة فالشريعة تحرمها وسياسة عادلة تخرج الحق من الظالم وتدفع المظالم وتردع أهل الفساد ويتوصل بها إلى المقاصد الشرعية، فالشريعة توجب المصير إلى هذه السياسة أي العمل بها جائز شرعاً بالنسبة للسلطان ونائبه إذا غلب على ظنه أن ظهور الحق يتوقف على العمل بها ولا يجوز أن يعمل بها القاضي والمفتي، وجه صحة السياسة في النفي أنه عليها نفى المخنث، ونفى عمر الله نصر بن الحجاج، وكان غلاماً صبيحاً تفتتن به النساء، والجمال لا يوجب النفي، ولكن فعل ذلك لمصلحة رآها، وقال في النهاية: المراد بالتغريب الحبس، وهو أحسن وأسكن للفتنة من نفيه إلى إقليم آخر، ولهذا كان الحبس حداً في ابتداء الإسلام دون النفي، وحمل النفي المذكور في قطاع الطريق عليه (فتح)
And there is no combining of lashing and stoning: meaning for the muhsan, because he (the Prophet) did not combine lashing and stoning for Ma'iz, nor for al-Ghamidiyyah, nor for the woman with whom al-Asif committed zina, but he stoned them without lashing. The Zahiris said: he should be lashed then stoned, because 'Ali lashed Sharahah then stoned her. We say: this action of his was either because her ihsan was not established to him until after her lashing, or it is an opinion that does not counter the consensus of the Companions, nor what we mentioned from the Messenger of Allah; and because lashing becomes devoid of benefit, since the deterrent effect is achieved by stoning, so it would be committing an act without benefit. (Mustakhlas, Fath) And lashing and exile: It is said: so-and-so was exiled from his country, i.e., they are not combined for the virgin (non-muhsan) between lashing and expulsion from the country. Al-Shafi'i said: The complete hadd of the non-muhsan is that he be taken out after lashing to a place a travel distance away from the woman, due to his saying: 'The virgin for the virgin: one hundred lashes and exile for a year', reported by all except al-Bukhari and al-Nasa'i, and Malik and Ahmad said the same. Our evidence: that the text made it one hundred lashes, and adding to an absolute text is abrogation, and what he narrated is abrogated. And because exile (taghrib) exposes them to corruption. For this reason 'Ali said: 'Exile is sufficient as a trial.' And 'Umar exiled a person who then apostatized and joined the enemy territory, so he swore that he would never exile again after that. By this it is known that their exile was by way of policy and ta'zir, not by way of hadd, for a person like that would swear not to establish the hadd. (Fath) And if he exiled according to what he sees as correct: The meaning of taghrib is imprisonment, i.e., if the knowledgeable, just, prudent ruler imprisons him. („Ayni, Fath) i.e., if the just ruler exiles for a duration he sees as beneficial, the exile is valid as policy. This is not specific to zina, but rather for every crime where the ruler sees benefit in exile, he may do so. Al-siyasah is the ruler doing something for a benefit he sees, even if no transmitted evidence is seen for that action. The ruling of siyasah is legally valid but restricted; the judge and mufti have no part in it. It is of two types: oppressive policy, which the Shari'ah prohibits, and just policy that extracts rights from the oppressor, removes injustices, deters the corrupt, and achieves legal objectives. The Shari'ah requires resorting to this policy, i.e., acting upon it is legally permissible for the sultan and his deputy if it becomes likely that the manifestation of truth depends on it. The judge and mufti may not act on it. The validity of siyasah in exile is that the Prophet exiled the effeminate man, and 'Umar exiled Nasr ibn al-Hajjaj who was a handsome young man that women were tempted by; beauty does not necessitate exile, but he did it for a benefit he saw. And it is said in al-Nihayah: The meaning of taghrib is imprisonment, which is better and more calming for fitna than exiling to another region. Therefore imprisonment was a hadd in early Islam, not exile. The exile mentioned for highway robbers is applied to it. (Fath)
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage addresses two key issues: (1) combining penalties for the muhsan, and (2) combining penalties for the non-muhsan (virgin). For the muhsan, the Hanafi school holds that only stoning is carried out; lashing is not combined because the Prophet did not do so in the cases of Ma'iz and al-Ghamidiyyah. The Zahiris argued for combining based on `Ali's actions, but the Hanafi response is that `Ali's action was either due to uncertainty about ihsan or was a personal opinion that does not outweigh the practice of the Prophet and the consensus of the Companions. Moreover, lashing becomes redundant when stoning suffices for deterrence. For the non-muhsan, the Hanafis maintain that the only penalty is one hundred lashes; exile (nafy) is not part of the hadd. This contradicts al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad, who argue for adding a year of exile based on a hadith. The Hanafi position is that this hadith is abrogated because the Qur'anic text says 'one hundred lashes' and adding to an absolute text is considered abrogation if it claims to be part of the original command. Furthermore, exile can lead to corruption, as experienced by `Umar when an exile apostatized. Thus, Hanafis view exile as a matter of siyasah (policy) for the ruler, not a fixed hadd. The passage then discusses siyasah in detail: it is permissible for the ruler to exile for any crime if he sees a benefit, even without specific textual evidence. This policy is distinct from the fixed hadd and is left to the ruler's discretion. The preferred form of 'taghrib' is actually imprisonment, which is more effective in preventing fitna than geographical exile.

Key Terms
السياسة (al-siyasah): Ruler's discretionary policy to achieve legal objectives when no specific textual evidence exists.
التغريب (al-taghrib): Literally sending away; Hanafis interpret it as imprisonment (habis) rather than physical exile.
النسخ (al-naskh): Abrogation of a legal ruling by a later revelation or stronger evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the full fixed punishment (hadd) for an unmarried (non-muhsan) person who commits zina?
A) 100 lashes and one year of exile.
B) Stoning only.
C) 100 lashes only.
D) 80 lashes and exile.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that exile is not part of the hadd for the non-muhsan; it is a discretionary policy (siyasah) that the ruler may use, and its preferred form is imprisonment.

Postponement of Hadd for the Sick Offender
Ruling on sick offender: stoning immediate, lashing delayed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when a sick offender's hadd is carried out immediately versus delayed, and explain the Hanafi rationale based on the distinction between destruction and deterrence.

Core Idea
Stoning is destruction, so illness does not delay it; lashing is deterrence, so it is postponed until recovery.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on administering hudud punishment to a sick person. The key principle is the purpose of the punishment: if the hadd is stoning (rajm), it is intended to destroy the offender, so illness does not justify delay. If the hadd is lashing, it is a deterrent, not lethal, and must be postponed until the offender recovers to avoid causing death. We will also explore the evidence and a differing view from other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is zina by a sick person. The ruling depends on whether the hadd is stoning or lashing.
Stoning is hadd mutlif (destructive); lashing is hadd zajir (deterrent).
2
Distinguish between stoning and lashing
Stoning is carried out immediately regardless of illness because it is meant to destroy. Lashing is delayed until recovery because it is a deterrent and could cause death if applied to a sick person.
Analogy: not cutting a thief's hand in extreme temperatures to prevent death.
3
Examine the dalil
The Hanafis cite the analogy of not cutting a thief's hand in extreme cold/heat, and the hadith of the weak man who was given a symbolic strike with a palm branch (though they treat it as a specific concession).
The hadith is used by opposing schools as evidence for symbolic whipping.
4
Note the cross-madhhab dispute
Malik, Ahmad, and some Shafi'is allow a symbolic whipping for the sick to fulfill the hadd without lethal risk, based on the hadith of the weak man.
Hanafis respond that the hadith is a specific case, not a general rule.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is that the hadd is postponed entirely until recovery; if recovery is hopeless, then a reduced punishment is administered to bearable extent.
This is the mufta bihi view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمريض يرجم، ولا يجلد حتى يبرأ والحامل لا تحد حتى تلد وتخرج من نفاسها لو أي الحامل كان حدّها الجلد. متعلق بقوله: وتخرج من نفاسها سياسة ظالمة فالشريعة تحرمها وسياسة عادلة تخرج الحق من الظالم وتدفع المظالم وتردع أهل الفساد ويتوصل بها إلى المقاصد الشرعية، فالشريعة توجب المصير إلى هذه السياسة أي العمل بها جائز شرعاً بالنسبة بالسلطان ونائبه إذا غلب على ظنه أن ظهور الحق يتوقف على العمل بها ولا يجوز أن يعمل بها القاضي والمفتي، وجه صحة السياسة في النفي أنه عليها نفى المخنث، ونفى عمر الله نصر بن الحجاج، وكان غلاماً صبيحاً تفتتن به النساء، والجمال لا يوجب النفي، ولكن فعل ذلك لمصلحة رآها، وقال في النهاية: المراد بالتغريب الحبس، وهو أحسن وأسكن للفتنة. من نفيه إلى إقليم آخر، ولهذا كان الحبس حداً في ابتداء الإسلام دون النفي، وحمل النفي المذكور في قطاع الطريق عليه رمز الحقائق: ۳۸۱/۱] (فتح) والمريض يرجم إلخ: أي إذا زنى مريض، وحده الرجم يرجم؛ لأنه مستحق الإتلاف، فلا يؤخر بسبب المرض، وإن كان حده الجلد لا يجلد حتى يبرأ؛ لأن الحد شرع زاجراً لا متلفاً، ولهذا لا يقطع يد السارق في شدة الحر، ولا في شدة البرد؛ للإفضاء إلى الهلاك، وعند مالك في رواية وأحمد في رواية وبعض الشافعية: يضرب بحسب ما يحتمله؛ لما أن رجلاً ضعيفاً زنى، فذكر ذلك لرسول الله الله فقال علي: "اضربوه حده"، فقالوا: يا رسول الله ! ضعيف لو ضربناه مائة سوط قتلناه فقال علي: "خذوا عثكالاً فيه مائة شمراخ ثم اضربوه ضربة واحدة"، وعندنا: إذا وقع اليأس من برئه فيقام عليه بقدر ما يطيق. (عيني، فتح) حتى يبرأ: أي من مرضه؛ لأنه ليس بمستحق للهلاك وكان مانعاً. (عيني) والحامل لا تحد: مطلقاً حدها الجلد أو الرجم؛ لأنه يخاف الهلاك على الولد وله حرمة الآدمي وإن كان من الزنا؛ لعدم الجناية منه، ولما ورد من أنه عليه أخر الرحم عن الغامدية حتى وضعت حين أقرت بين يديه عليها بأنها حبلى من الزنا، وقوله: " وتخرج من نفاسها لو كان حدها الجلد"؛ لأن النفاس نوع مرض فينتظر البرء، ولما ورد عن علي له أنه أخر جلد الزانية حين أمره عليه بجلدها، فرءاها حديثة عهد بالنفاس وخاف الهلاك عليها فأخبره بذلك، فقال له عليها: "أحسنت"، وإن كان حدها الرجم ترجم بعد الولادة في الحال؛ لأن التأخير لأجل الولد وقد انفصل. وعن أبي حنيفة: تؤخر إلى أن يستغني الولد؛ لما روي . الغامدية أتت النبي عليه فأقرت بالزنا وإنها حبلى وأمرته أن يطهرها، فقال لها: "اذهبي حتى تلدي ثم أتته به بعد الولادة، فقال: "اذهبي فأرضعيه حتى تفطميه" ثم أتته به بعد أن فطم، (الحديث) ولأن في التأخير صيانة الولد عن الضياع، وهذا إذا لم يكن أحد يقوم بتربيته، ثم الحامل تحبس إلى أن تضع حملها إن كان ثبوت الحد بالبينة، وإن كان بالإقرار لا تحبس؛ لأن الرجوع عن الإقرار جائز. (مستخلص، فتح)
The sick man is stoned, and not lashed until he recovers. And the pregnant woman is not punished until she delivers and emerges from her nifas, if her hadd is lashing. [Text continues with siyasah repetition then returns to topic] The sick man is stoned, etc.: i.e., if a sick person commits zina and his hadd is stoning, he is stoned because he deserves destruction, so it is not delayed due to illness. But if his hadd is lashing, he is not lashed until he recovers, because the hadd is legislated as a deterrent, not as a destructive punishment. For this reason, the hand of a thief is not cut in extreme heat or extreme cold, because that could lead to death. According to Malik (in one narration), Ahmad (in one narration), and some Shafi`is: he is struck according to what he can bear. There is a story of a weak man who committed zina and it was mentioned to the Messenger of Allah, who said, 'Strike him his hadd.' They said, 'O Messenger of Allah, he is weak; if we strike him one hundred lashes, we will kill him.' He said, 'Take a palm branch with one hundred twigs and strike him once.' According to us (Hanafis): if there is no hope of recovery, then the hadd is carried out to the extent he can bear. (`Ayni, Fath) Until he recovers: i.e., from his illness, because he is not deserving of destruction and the illness is a preventer. (`Ayni) And the pregnant woman is not punished: absolutely, whether her hadd is lashing or stoning, because there is fear of harm to the child, and the child has the inviolability of a human being even if from zina, since it is not at fault. And because it is reported that the Prophet delayed stoning al-Ghamidiyyah until she delivered when she confessed before him that she was pregnant from zina. And his saying: 'And she emerges from her nifas if her hadd was lashing', because nifas is a kind of illness, so recovery is awaited. And it is reported from `Ali that he delayed lashing a woman when the Prophet ordered him to lash her; he saw that she had recently given birth and feared for her life, so he informed the Prophet, who said to him, 'You have done well.' And if her hadd is stoning, she is stoned immediately after delivery because the delay was for the sake of the child, who has now separated. According to Abu Hanifah: she is delayed until the child becomes independent, as narrated about al-Ghamidiyyah: she came to the Prophet and confessed to zina and that she was pregnant, and asked him to purify her. He said: 'Go until you give birth.' Then she came after delivery, and he said: 'Go and breastfeed him until you wean him.' Then she came after weaning him. (Hadith) And because delaying protects the child from being lost. This is if there is no one to care for him. Then the pregnant woman is imprisoned until she delivers if the hadd is established by bayyinah; if by iqrar, she is not imprisoned because retraction of iqrar is permissible. (Mustakhlas, Fath)
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage covers two categories: sick persons and pregnant women. For the sick person: if the hadd is stoning (rajm), it is carried out immediately because stoning is meant to destroy, so illness does not justify delay. If the hadd is lashing, it is postponed until recovery because lashing is a deterrent, not a lethal punishment; applying it during illness could cause death, contradicting the purpose of the hadd. The Hanafis cite the analogy of not cutting a thief's hand in extreme temperatures. Some other scholars (Malik, Ahmad, some Shafi'is) allow a symbolic whipping with a palm branch to fulfill the number without causing death. The Hanafi response: if recovery is hopeless, then the lashing is carried out to the extent the person can bear. For the pregnant woman: absolutely no punishment until she delivers, whether the hadd is lashing or stoning, to protect the life of the child. If the hadd is lashing, she is further delayed until after nifas (postpartum bleeding) because nifas is like an illness. The Prophet's treatment of al-Ghamidiyyah is the precedent: he waited until she delivered, then until she weaned the child (according to Abu Hanifah). If the hadd is stoning, she is stoned immediately after delivery because the child is now separate. Abu Hanifah holds that stoning is also delayed until the child is weaned if there is no one else to care for the child. The narration of al-Ghamidiyyah shows this sequence. However, if the hadd is established by testimony (bayyinah), the woman is imprisoned until delivery to prevent her from fleeing; if established by confession (iqrar), she is not imprisoned because she may retract her confession.

Key Terms
النفاس (al-nifas): Postpartum bleeding that follows childbirth; considered a type of illness making the woman legally akin to a sick person.
الإقرار (al-iqrar): Confession of guilt by the accused, which can be retracted before the hadd is carried out.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A sick man is convicted of zina and his hadd is stoning. When is the punishment carried out according to the Hanafi school?
A) Immediately
B) After recovery
C) After he dies
D) Never

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the nature of the hadd determines its timing: stoning is immediate, lashing is postponed for recovery to avoid lethal harm.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
intermediate

Postponement of Hadd for the Pregnant Woman
Ruling on pregnant woman: hadd delayed for delivery and nifas; weaning consideration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on delaying hadd for a pregnant woman, distinguish between lashing and stoning, and describe the intra-Hanafi difference regarding weaning the child.

Core Idea
A pregnant woman's hadd is delayed to protect the child; stoning is immediate after birth, lashing waits until after nifas, and weaning may require further delay.

This lesson covers the Hanafi rules for a pregnant woman convicted of zina. The primary concern is protecting the unborn or newborn child, who bears no fault. The hadd punishment is postponed until after delivery, and for lashing, until after nifas (postpartum bleeding). Additionally, Abu Hanifah holds that stoning may be delayed until the child is weaned if no one else can care for it, while the Sahibayn may disagree.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The pregnant woman is not punished until she delivers, regardless of whether the hadd is stoning or lashing.
The child's life is inviolable even if born from zina.
2
Distinguish between types of hadd
If the hadd is lashing, she must also wait until after nifas (postpartum bleeding) because nifas is considered an illness. If stoning, she is stoned immediately after delivery according to the basic rule.
Nifas is analogous to illness, so the same reasoning as for a sick person applies.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi difference on stoning
Abu Hanifah holds that stoning should also be delayed until the child is weaned if there is no one else to care for the child. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) do not require this delay.
The hadith of al-Ghamidiyyah is the main evidence for Abu Hanifah's view.
4
Examine the evidence
The Prophet delayed stoning al-Ghamidiyyah until she delivered and then until she weaned the child. This is cited by Abu Hanifah as a general principle.
The narration from Ali also supports delaying lashing after nifas.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi jurists prefer Abu Hanifah's view and delay stoning until weaning if there is no other caregiver.
This is to protect the child's welfare, in line with maqasid al-shari'ah.

This passage covers two categories: sick persons and pregnant women. For the sick person: if the hadd is stoning (rajm), it is carried out immediately because stoning is meant to destroy, so illness does not justify delay. If the hadd is lashing, it is postponed until recovery because lashing is a deterrent, not a lethal punishment; applying it during illness could cause death, contradicting the purpose of the hadd. The Hanafis cite the analogy of not cutting a thief's hand in extreme temperatures. Some other scholars (Malik, Ahmad, some Shafi'is) allow a symbolic whipping with a palm branch to fulfill the number without causing death. The Hanafi response: if recovery is hopeless, then the lashing is carried out to the extent the person can bear. For the pregnant woman: absolutely no punishment until she delivers, whether the hadd is lashing or stoning, to protect the life of the child. If the hadd is lashing, she is further delayed until after nifas (postpartum bleeding) because nifas is like an illness. The Prophet's treatment of al-Ghamidiyyah is the precedent: he waited until she delivered, then until she weaned the child (according to Abu Hanifah). If the hadd is stoning, she is stoned immediately after delivery because the child is now separate. Abu Hanifah holds that stoning is also delayed until the child is weaned if there is no one else to care for the child. The narration of al-Ghamidiyyah shows this sequence. However, if the hadd is established by testimony (bayyinah), the woman is imprisoned until delivery to prevent her from fleeing; if established by confession (iqrar), she is not imprisoned because she may retract her confession.

Key Terms
النفاس (al-nifas): Postpartum bleeding that follows childbirth; considered a type of illness making the woman legally akin to a sick person.
الإقرار (al-iqrar): Confession of guilt by the accused, which can be retracted before the hadd is carried out.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A pregnant woman is convicted of zina and the hadd is lashing. She gives birth and is now in nifas. According to the Hanafi school, when is the lashing carried out?
A) Immediately after birth
B) After nifas ends
C) After weaning
D) Not at all

Key Takeaway
The child's welfare takes precedence: a pregnant woman's hadd is delayed until after birth and, if lashing, until after nifas; stoning may be further delayed until weaning.

Shubha in Hadd: Two Types That Preclude Punishment
Defines two types of shubha that preclude hadd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish shubha fi al-mahall from shubha fi al-fi'l and apply the Hanafi rule that hadd is dropped in both.

Core Idea
Hadd for zina is dropped when a legal doubt exists, either in the woman or in the act.

This lesson examines the Hanafi principle that legal punishments are suspended in the presence of doubt (shubha). The passage identifies two categories of shubha that preclude the hadd for unlawful intercourse: shubha in the place (the woman) and shubha in the act. Understanding these categories is crucial for correctly applying the hudud in complex cases.

Guided Path
1
Define shubha
Understand the general definition: shubha is what resembles something established but is not actually established. This leads to doubt that prevents hadd.
The principle: 'al-shubha tadra'u al-hudud' is foundational.
2
Identify shubha fi al-mahall
This type arises when there is a legal evidence that suggests permissibility regarding the woman (mahall). Even if the evidence fails to fully establish permissibility, it creates a doubt that blocks hadd.
Also called shubha hukmiyyah because it originates from a legal (shar'i) evidence.
3
Work through the examples of shubha fi al-mahall
Apply the concept: father with son's slave girl (hadith 'You and your property belong to your father'), iddah from kinayah divorce (Companion disagreement on revocability), sold slave girl before delivery, fasid sale, mudabbara, mahr slave girl before delivery, joint ownership.
In each case, a legal right or evidence of ownership creates doubt.
4
Identify shubha fi al-fi'l
This is shubha ishtibah: the person confuses the evidence, mistakenly believing the act is permissible. It applies when the person claims they thought it was halal.
Contrast: a person who knows it is haram but has a false hope does not benefit from this shubha.
5
Distinguish the two types
Shubha fi al-mahall involves an objective legal indicator in the woman, while shubha fi al-fi'l involves a subjective misunderstanding of the law. Both drop hadd, but their conditions differ.
For shubha fi al-fi'l, a claim of assumption (zann) is required; mere heart assumption is insufficient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(مستخلص، مسكين) ولد ولده أي كوطء الأب أمة ولد إلخ وإن سفل ولو ولده حيا. (ط، عيني) ومعتدة الكنايات [أي وكوطء المعتدة بالطلاق الثلاث؛ لأن حرمتها مقطوع به فلم يبق له فيها ملك. (عيني)] هذا مثال ثان لعدم الحد بشبهة المحل أي إذا وطئ المطلقة طلاقاً بائنا بالكنايات في عدتها لا يحد؛ لأن في الكنايات اختلاف الصحابة، فمذهب عمر الله وابن مسعود همه أنها رجعية، فلا يزول ملك الزوج عنها فأورث شبهة، وإن كان المختار قول علي الله في أن الطلاق بالكنايات بائن ولعدم الحد في شبهة المحل مسائل أخرى، منها: الجارية المبيعة في حق البائع قبل التسليم؛ لأنها في ضمانه ويده فتبقى الشبهة ببقاء اليد وكذا البيع الفاسد قبل القبض وبعده في حق المشتري؛ لأنه ثبت له حق الملك فيها وجارية مكاتبة وعبده المأذون له المستغرق بالدين في حق المولى؛ لأن له حقاً في كسب عبده فكان شبهته في حقه والجارية الممهورة قبل التسليم في حق الزوج؛ لأن يده باقية فتبقى الشبهة، والجارية المشتركة؛ لأن ملكه في البعض ثابت حقيقة. (عيني، فتح) وبشبهة الفعل وتسمى هذه الشبهة شبهة اشتباه وهو أن يظن غير دليل الحل دليلاً أي شبهة في حق من حصل له اشتباه فالاستناد إلى غير دليل الحل اشتباه وظنه الحل منه شبهة فتحقق في حق من اشتبه عليه الحرمة بالحل ولم يعلم دون من لم يشتبه عليه، وعلم الحرمة كقوم سقوا خمراً يحد من علم منهم أ أنه خمر لا من لم يعلم، ولابد من دعوى الظن ليتحقق الاشتباه وهو المراد بقوله : إن ظن حله، أي ادعى ظن الحل، وإلا فمجرد الظن القائم به لا يحقق الشبهة. (مسكين، فتح)
Book of Hudud. Chapter of intercourse that necessitates hadd and that which does not. That is, in explaining its rulings. There is no hadd with a doubt in the place [of intercourse], even if he thinks it is forbidden, like intercourse with a slave girl of his son or grandson, and a woman in 'iddah divorced by kinayah (allusive) pronouncements. That is, the one who has intercourse in that place, like the father [intercourse with] the slave girl of his son, as obligatory. And with a doubt in the act. That is, there is no hadd either. 'No hadd with a doubt in the place': know that shubha is of two types: shubha in the place, i.e., the woman being intercourse with, and it is called shubha hukmiyyah, i.e., arising from a legal evidence that necessitates permissibility in the place; and shubha in the act, called shubha ishtibah. And shubha is what resembles something established, but is not established. So the author began first with shubha in the place. The meaning is that hadd is not obligatory due to a shubha found in the place. And his statement 'and even if he thinks' means although he knows its prohibition, because when shubha exists in the woman, ownership is established in some respect, so the name 'zina' no longer applies, thus hadd is prevented, because the evidence that establishes permissibility is present, even if it fails to actually establish it due to an obstacle, it gives rise to shubha. Hence this type is called shubha in the place, because it arises from evidence that necessitates permissibility in the place. And the evidence is his statement (peace be upon him): 'You and your property belong to your father,' which implies ownership, because the lam al-mulk indicates ownership. So intercourse of the father with the slave girl of his son, even if the son is descended, does not necessitate hadd, as we have narrated. (Mustakhlas, Miskin) 'And his son's son' i.e., like intercourse of the father with the slave girl of his son, etc., even if descended, even if his son is alive. (T., Ayni) 'And a woman in 'iddah divorced by kinayah': this is a second example of no hadd due to shubha in the place, i.e., if one has intercourse with a woman divorced irrevocably (ba'in) by kinayah during her 'iddah, he is not punished with hadd, because there is disagreement among the Companions regarding kinayah. The view of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) and Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) is that it is raj'iyyah (revocable), so the husband's ownership does not cease, thus giving rise to shubha. Even though the chosen view is the statement of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) that divorce by kinayah is ba'in. And for no hadd due to shubha in the place, there are other issues, including: the sold slave girl in the right of the seller before delivery, because she is in his responsibility and his hand, so the shubha remains due to the persistence of the hand; similarly, a void (fasid) sale before and after receipt in the right of the buyer, because he has established a right of ownership in her; and the mudabbar female slave and his authorized slave whose debt exceeds his value in the right of the master, because he has a right in the earnings of his slave, so there is shubha in his regard; and the female slave given as mahr before delivery in the right of the husband, because his hand remains, so shubha remains; and the jointly owned slave girl, because his ownership in part is truly established. (Ayni, Fath) And [no hadd] with shubha in the act, called shubha ishtibah, which is that one considers something other than the evidence of permissibility as evidence, i.e., a shubha in the right of one who has confusion. So relying on something other than the evidence of permissibility is confusion, and his assumption of permissibility from it is shubha. So it is realized in the right of one for whom prohibition is confused with permissibility and he does not know, not for one who does not have confusion and knows the prohibition. For example, a group of people who were given wine to drink: the one among them who knows it is wine is punished, not the one who does not know. And a claim of assumption is necessary for confusion to be realized, and that is meant by his statement 'if he assumes its permissibility,' i.e., he claims the assumption of permissibility; otherwise, mere assumption in his mind does not realize shubha. (Miskin, Fath)
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage defines and elaborates the concept of shubha (doubt) as a bar to the application of hadd for zina. The author explains that there are two types of shubha: shubha fi al-mahall (doubt in the place, i.e., the woman) and shubha fi al-fi'l (doubt in the act itself). The first type, shubha fi al-mahall, arises when there is a legal evidence that suggests permissibility of the intercourse, even if that evidence is overridden by a stronger prohibition. For example, a father's intercourse with his son's slave girl: the hadith 'You and your property belong to your father' implies ownership, even though it is not real ownership; this creates a doubt that prevents hadd. Similarly, intercourse with a woman in 'iddah divorced by kinayah (allusive divorce) does not attract hadd because there was a difference of opinion among the Companions as to whether such divorce is revocable or irrevocable; the doubt (shubha) arises from the possibility that the marriage still exists. The passage lists several other instances where shubha in the place prevents hadd, such as selling contracts before delivery, void sales, and cases involving mudabbar slaves and mahr. The second type, shubha fi al-fi'l, occurs when a person genuinely believes that a certain act is permissible based on a misinterpretation of evidence, such as drinking wine thinking it is allowed. In such cases, hadd is not applied to the ignorant person, but is applied to those who know it is forbidden. The author stresses that for shubha to be valid, the person must claim that they thought it was permissible; mere silent assumption is not enough. This shows the Hanafi principle that legal punishments are suspended when there is any plausible doubt, based on the tradition 'Doubt repels hadd' (al-shubha tadra'u al-hudud).

Key Terms
الشبهة (al-shubha): ما أشبه الثابت وليس بثابت؛ شبهة تمنع إقامة الحد
شبهة في المحل (shubha fi al-mahall): شبهة تنشأ عن دليل شرعي يقتضي الحل في الموطوءة، ولو تخلف أثره لمانع
شبهة في الفعل (shubha fi al-fi'l): شبهة اشتباه: أن يظن غير دليل الحل دليلاً، فيعتقد إباحة المحرم
الكنايات (al-kināyāt): ألفاظ الطلاق التي تحتمل الطلاق وغيره، مثل 'الحقي بأهلك'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the type of shubha that prevents hadd when a father has intercourse with his son's slave girl?
A) Shubha fi al-fi'l
B) Shubha fi al-mahall
C) Shubha in the confession
D) No shubha, hadd applies

Key Takeaway
Hadd for zina is dropped when shubha exists, whether it is shubha fi al-mahall (doubt in the woman due to a legal indicator) or shubha fi al-fi'l (doubt in the act due to a claim of mistaken belief).

Shubhah Fi al-Mahall: No Hadd When Doubt Exists About the Partner
Defines shubhah fi al-mahall and provides its ruling with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of shubhah fi al-mahall and apply the Hadith proof to determine when hadd is not imposed.

Core Idea
If any legal basis suggests permissibility of the partner, even if the act is actually haram, the hadd penalty is dropped.

In the Hanafi school, the fixed punishment (hadd) for zina is not applied when there exists a legal doubt (shubhah) about the permissibility of the partner. This lesson explains the concept of shubhah fi al-mahall and its application through a key hadith and several examples. The principle is that even a semblance of ownership or right, arising from a valid legal proof, prevents the act from being considered pure zina, thus averting the hadd.

Guided Path
1
Define shubhah fi al-mahall
Understand that shubhah fi al-mahall refers to doubt about the legal status of the partner (the woman or slave girl), arising from a legal proof that could indicate permissibility, even if the act is actually forbidden due to an overriding factor.
The Hanafi school classifies shubhah into two types: shubhah fi al-mahall (doubt about the partner) and shubhah fi al-fil (doubt about the act itself).
2
Identify the ruling
State the ruling: hadd is not obligatory when shubhah fi al-mahall exists, even if the person knows the act is haram (e.g., knows the woman is not his own slave).
The hukm level is ghair_wajib (not obligatory) – the hadd is not imposed.
3
Locate the proof (dalil)
The proof is the hadith 'You and your wealth belong to your father' (أنت ومالك لأبيك). The preposition 'li' indicates ownership, providing a legal basis for the father's claim to his son's property, including a slave woman.
This hadith is transmitted as ahad (single-narrator) but is considered strong enough for legal deduction in Hanafi usul.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'li' in Arabic denotes ownership (al-mulk). Although the father does not actually own the son's slave woman (because the son is a separate legal entity), the hadith creates a semblance of ownership that raises a doubt.
Because the doubt is legally grounded, the act is not considered pure zina, and hadd is averted.
5
Apply to additional cases
The passage lists other examples: a sold slave girl before delivery, a woman given as mahr before delivery, a joint slave girl, etc. In each, there is a remaining ownership or possession that creates shubhah.
The principle extends to any case where a legal right or ownership interest remains, even if partial or contested.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
