(مستخلص، مسكين) ولد ولده أي كوطء الأب أمة ولد إلخ وإن سفل ولو ولده حيا. (ط، عيني) ومعتدة الكنايات [أي وكوطء المعتدة بالطلاق الثلاث؛ لأن حرمتها مقطوع به فلم يبق له فيها ملك. (عيني)] هذا مثال ثان لعدم الحد بشبهة المحل أي إذا وطئ المطلقة طلاقاً بائنا بالكنايات في عدتها لا يحد؛ لأن في الكنايات اختلاف الصحابة، فمذهب عمر الله وابن مسعود همه أنها رجعية، فلا يزول ملك الزوج عنها فأورث شبهة، وإن كان المختار قول علي الله في أن الطلاق بالكنايات بائن ولعدم الحد في شبهة المحل مسائل أخرى، منها: الجارية المبيعة في حق البائع قبل التسليم؛ لأنها في ضمانه ويده فتبقى الشبهة ببقاء اليد وكذا البيع الفاسد قبل القبض وبعده في حق المشتري؛ لأنه ثبت له حق الملك فيها وجارية مكاتبة وعبده المأذون له المستغرق بالدين في حق المولى؛ لأن له حقاً في كسب عبده فكان شبهته في حقه والجارية الممهورة قبل التسليم في حق الزوج؛ لأن يده باقية فتبقى الشبهة، والجارية المشتركة؛ لأن ملكه في البعض ثابت حقيقة. (عيني، فتح)
Book of Hudud. Chapter on intercourse that necessitates hadd and that which does not. No hadd is imposed due to a shubhah in the partner, even if he assumes its prohibition, like intercourse with his son's slave woman and his grandson's slave woman and a woman in 'iddah from ambiguous divorce. Know that shubhah is of two types: shubhah in the partner (the one being slept with), also called a legal shubhah arising from a legal proof indicating permissibility in the partner, and shubhah in the act, also called shubhah of confusion. The proof is his statement 'You and your wealth belong to your father' which implies ownership because the lam indicates ownership.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq opens the chapter on hadd for zina by distinguishing between two types of legal doubt (shubhah). The author first addresses shubhah fi al-mahall, meaning doubt about the legal status of the partner herself. The key principle is that if there is any legal basis that could establish permissibility (ownership or a right), even if the person knows it is actually forbidden due to an overriding reason, the hadd penalty is not applied. The classic example is a father having intercourse with his son's slave woman: the hadith 'You and your wealth belong to your father' creates a semblance of ownership for the father, so the act is not pure zina. The commentary explains that the hadith uses the preposition 'li' which indicates ownership in Arabic, but the actual ownership is prevented by the son's independent rights. This creates doubt, hence no hadd. Other examples include a woman divorced by ambiguous wording (kinayat) during her 'iddah, because the Companions differed on whether such divorce is revocable or irrevocable, so the wife may still be considered his property somewhat. Additional cases are mentioned such as a sold slave girl before delivery, a woman given as mahr before delivery, etc., all due to remaining ownership or possession.

Key Terms
شبهة المحل (shubhat al-mahall): Doubt concerning the legal status of the partner, arising from a proof that could indicate permissibility.
حد (hadd): The fixed corporal punishment for crimes like zina, qadhf, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the father not subject to hadd when he has intercourse with his son's slave woman?
A) Because the father owns his son's property entirely.
B) Because a hadith establishes a certain right of the father over his son's property, creating a legal doubt.
C) Because the son consented.
D) Because it was a simple mistake.

Key Takeaway
The existence of a legal doubt about the partner's permissibility (shubhah fi al-mahall) prevents the imposition of hadd, even if the act is actually forbidden.

Shubhah Fi al-Fi'l: Examples and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Hadd
Examples of shubhah fi al-fi'l and an intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four examples of shubhah fi al-fi'l, explain the requirement of claiming suspicion (da'wa al-zann), and evaluate Imam Zafar's dissenting opinion on the parents' slave woman.

Core Idea
Hadd is averted when the act is accompanied by a plausible doubt, even if the partner is unlawful, provided the person claims he thought it permissible.

This lesson continues the topic of shubhah in hudud, now focusing on doubts about the act itself (shubhah fi al-fi'l). The passage lists four key examples—the irrevocably divorced woman, the parents' slave woman, the wife's slave woman, and the master's slave woman—and explains why each creates a semblance of permissibility. It also highlights that the person must claim the suspicion (da'wa al-zann) in court, and notes Imam Zafar's dissenting opinion on the case of the parents' slave woman.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of shubhah fi al-fi'l
Shubhah fi al-fi'l is confusion where one assumes a non-proof of permissibility as a proof. It is a doubt about the act itself, not the object.
This differs from shubhah fi al-mahall discussed previously.
2
Identify the requirement of claiming suspicion
The person must actually claim (da'wa) that they thought the act was permissible. Mere inner suspicion without articulation does not exempt from hadd.
3
List the four examples and their basis for doubt
The examples: (1) woman divorced three times – residual effects of marriage cause doubt; (2) parents' slave woman – common usage (basuta) in property dealings; (3) wife's slave woman – Quranic allusion to husband's enrichment by wife's wealth; (4) master's slave woman – basuta again.
Each has a plausible reason that makes the person think the act is permissible.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Zafar holds that the parents' slave woman does not create a valid doubt because there is no ownership or right; hence hadd applies. The majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) rely on basuta to negate hadd. The mufta bihi is the majority position.
The disagreement is only on this specific case; the other examples are agreed upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبشبهة الفعل وتسمى هذه الشبهة شبهة اشتباه وهو أن يظن غير دليل الحل دليلاً أي شبهة في حق من حصل له اشتباه فالاستناد إلى غير دليل الحل اشتباه وظنه الحل منه شبهة فتحقق في حق من اشتبه عليه الحرمة بالحل ولم يعلم دون من لم يشتبه عليه، وعلم الحرمة كقوم سقوا خمراً يحد من علم منهم أ أنه خمر لا من لم يعلم، ولابد من دعوى الظن ليتحقق الاشتباه وهو المراد بقوله : إن ظن حله، أي ادعى ظن الحل، وإلا فمجرد الظن القائم به لا يحقق الشبهة. (مسكين، فتح) إن ظن حله كمعتدة الثلاث وأمة أبويه وزوجته وسيده، والنسب يثبت في الأولى فقط كمعتدة الثلاث: مثال لعدم الحد بشبهة الفعل أي كوطء المعتدة بالطلقات الثلاث ولو جملة؛ لأنها حرمتها مقطوع به؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَإِنْ طَلَّقَهَا فَلا تَحِلُّ لَهُ مِنْ بَعْدُ﴾ (البقرة: ۲۳۰) فلم يبق له فيها ملك ولا حق، غير أنه بقي فيها بعض الأحكام كالنفقة والسكنى والمنع من الخروج، وثبوت النسب، وحرمة أختها وأربع سواها، وعدم قبول شهادة كل واحد منهما لصاحبه، فحصل الاشتباه، فأورث شبهة إن ظن حله؛ لأنه في موضع الاشتباه فيعذر. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٨٢/١] إذا طلق امرأة طلاقاً صحيحاً فوطئها في العدة وقال: ظننت أنها تحل لي أي علمت أن الزنا حرام لكن ظننت يعني أن هذا الوطء ليس محرماً لا يحد ولو قال علمت أن هذا الوطء حرام يحد. (فتح) وأمة أبويه مثال ثان لعدم الحد بشبهة الفعل أي كوطء أمة أبويه؛ لأنها لا تحل للولد لتباين الأملاك بينهم غير أن البسوطة تجري بينهم في الانتفاع بالأموال والرضا عادة، فإذا ظن الوطء من هذا القبيل يعذر ولا يحد، وقال زفر يحد. رمز الحقائق: ۳۸۲/۱] (محشي) وزوجته أي وكوطء أمة زوجته، فإن غنى الزوج بمال زوجته قوله تعالى: ﴿وَوَجَدَكَ عَائِلاً فَأَغْنَى﴾ (الضحى: ۸) أي بمال خديجة لها فيورث شبهة أن مال الزوجة ملك الزوج، فلا يحد إذا ظن الحل، وقوله : "وسيده" وكوطء أمة سيده إذا ظنه حلالاً تجري البسوطة بينهما لا يحد، وكذا المطلقة على مال وأم الولد إذا أعتقها مولاها. (عيني، فتح)
And by shubhah in the act, and this shubhah is called shubhah of confusion, which is that one assumes a non-proof of permissibility as a proof. So it is a shubhah for one who experiences confusion, and claiming suspicion is necessary. ... The examples: a woman divorced by three talags, a slave woman of his parents, his wife's slave woman, and his master's slave woman. ... For the slave woman of parents, it is not allowed for the son, but common usage (basuta) creates a shubhah, so if he claims he thought it permissible, he is excused and not to be penalized. Zafar said he would be penalized.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of shubhah, now focusing on shubhah fi al-fi'l (doubt about the act itself). Unlike shubhah fi al-mahall, here the partner is clearly not owned, but there is a plausible reason why the person might think the act is permissible. The text lists examples: (1) a woman irrevocably divorced by three talags during her 'iddah – the Quranic verse clearly states she is forbidden, but certain residual effects like maintenance and lineage create confusion, so if the man claims he thought it permissible, hadd is not applied. (2) The slave woman of his parents – although ownership is separate, common usage (basuta) in handling property creates a semblance of permissibility. Imam Zafar dissents and says hadd is applied, but the relied-upon position is no hadd. (3) The wife's slave woman – the verse 'He found you in need and enriched you' (by Khadija's wealth) suggests a wife's wealth is effectively the husband's, creating a shubhah. (4) The master's slave woman – again, basuta applies. The key point is that the claim of suspicion must be made; mere inner suspicion is insufficient.

Key Terms
شبهة الفعل (shubhat al-fi'l): Doubt concerning the act itself, where the person assumes a non-proof of permissibility as a proof, e.g., common usage or residual effects of marriage.
بسوطة (basuta): Common usage or mutual dealing, especially in property, that creates a semblance of permissibility.
دعوى الظن (da'wa al-zann): The legal claim of suspicion that the person must articulate in court for the shubhah to be considered.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is the basis for averting hadd in the case of intercourse with a parent's slave woman?
A) The slave woman's consent
B) Common usage (basuta) in family property dealings
C) The person's ownership of the slave woman
D) The absence of a Quranic prohibition

Key Takeaway
Shubhah fi al-fi'l averts hadd when the act is accompanied by a plausible doubt arising from common usage or residual legal effects, and the person claims that doubt in court.

Lineage Established Only in Shubhah Fi al-Mahall
States and explains the rule that lineage is established only in cases of shubhah fi al-mahall, not shubhah fi al-fi'l

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between shubhah fi al-mahall and shubhah fi al-fi'l in terms of establishing nasab, state the condition for nasab (claim by the man), and explain the rationale based on the requirement of firash or its semblance.

Core Idea
Nasab requires a marital bed or its semblance; shubhah fi al-mahall provides it, but shubhah fi al-fi'l does not.

In the previous lesson, you learned that hadd is dropped in both types of shubhah. However, the legal consequences differ for the child's lineage. This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq, as explained by the commentator, clarifies that nasab is only established in shubhah fi al-mahall, provided the man claims paternity. The key is the presence or absence of a basis for the marital bed (firash). Let's unpack the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of shubhah
Recall our earlier classification: shubhah fi al-mahall (doubt about the partner's status, e.g., a man having intercourse with his son's slave woman) and shubhah fi al-fi'l (doubt about the permissibility of the act, e.g., intercourse in a dark room mistaken for wife). This lesson applies a different ruling for each regarding nasab.
2
State the ruling for each type
The passage states: nasab is established only in shubhah fi al-mahall, not in shubhah fi al-fi'l. Furthermore, in the first type, the man must claim the child for nasab to be established.
Even if the man claims the child in shubhah fi al-fi'l, nasab is not established.
3
Understand the proof (dalil)
The commentator explains: nasab depends on the existence of ownership or a right in the partner (i.e., the woman must be owned or have a marital right). This is because nasab requires a firash (marital bed) or its semblance. In shubhah fi al-mahall, such right exists (e.g., semblance of ownership), so the act is not pure zina. In shubhah fi al-fi'l, there is no semblance of ownership, so the act is pure zina regarding nasab.
The underlying principle is the hadith: 'The child belongs to the bed' (al-walad li al-firash).
4
Distinguish from the dropping of hadd
Note that hadd is dropped in both types due to the doubt, but nasab differs. The reason for dropping hadd is the man's personal uncertainty, which does not create a basis for firash. Thus, the dropping of hadd does not automatically establish nasab.
This distinction is crucial to avoid conflating two different legal effects.
5
Apply the ruling to new scenarios
Given a scenario of doubtful intercourse, first determine the type of shubhah. If it is shubhah fi al-mahall, check if the man claims paternity. If both conditions are met, nasab is established. If shubhah fi al-fi'l, nasab is never established, regardless of claim.
Example: A man mistakenly has intercourse with his own female slave (shubhah fi al-mahall) – nasab established if he claims. A man mistakenly has intercourse with a stranger thinking she is his slave (shubhah fi al-fi'l) – nasab not established.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مستفاد من النسب يثبت في الأولى فقط: أي يثبت نسب الولد من الواطئ في الوطء بشبهة في المحل بشرط إن ادعاه الواطئ ولا يثبت في الوطء بشبهة الفعل ولو ادعاه؛ لأن النسب يعتمد قيام الملك أو الحق في المحل؛ لأنه لا يثبت بدون الفراش والفراش أو شبهته يوجد بأحدهما، وفي النوع الأول وجد أحدهما، فلم يتمحض زنا، ولم يتحقق في الثاني؛ لفرض أن لا شبهة ملك فتمحض زنا إلا أن الحد سقط؛ لظنه وهو أمر راجع إليه لا إلى المحل. رمز الحقائق: ۳۸۲/۱] (فتح)
It is understood from this that lineage is established only in the first type (shubhah fi al-mahall): the lineage of the child is established from the man who had intercourse in a case of shubhah fi al-mahall, provided that the man claims it. It is not established in intercourse with shubhah fi al-fi'l even if he claims it, because lineage depends on the existence of ownership or a right in the partner; it is not established without a marital bed (firash) or its semblance. In the first type, one of these exists, so the act is not pure zina. In the second, since there is no semblance of ownership, the act is pure zina, except that the hadd penalty is dropped due to his suspicion, which relates to himself, not the partner.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage clarifies an important corollary: although hadd is dropped in both types of shubhah, the child's lineage (nasab) is only established in shubhah fi al-mahall, not in shubhah fi al-fi'l. The reasoning is that lineage requires a 'firash' (marital bed) or its semblance, which exists when there is some ownership or right in the partner. In shubhah fi al-mahall, such a right exists (e.g., the father's semblance of ownership over his son's slave woman), so the child is attributed to the man if he claims paternity. In shubhah fi al-fi'l, no such right exists; the partner is clearly not owned, so the act is pure zina from the perspective of lineage, but the hadd is still dropped because the man's mistake was excusable. Thus, lineage establishes a child's parentage only when the doubt is about the partner's status, not about the act's permissibility.

Key Terms
نسب (nasab): Lineage or paternity of a child, which is legally established based on the existence of a marital bed (firash) or its semblance.
فراش (firash): The marital bed, a legal basis for establishing paternity. Its semblance can be created by ownership or a right.
شبهة في المحل (shubhah fi al-mahall): Doubt regarding the partner's status (e.g., whether she is owned or marriageable). This type can create a semblance of firash.
شبهة في الفعل (shubhah fi al-fi'l): Doubt regarding the permissibility of the act itself (e.g., thinking intercourse is permissible when it is not). This does not create a semblance of firash.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is lineage not established in cases of shubhah fi al-fi'l?
A) Because the act is considered pure zina in terms of lineage.
B) Because the man did not claim the child.
C) Because the woman is married to someone else.
D) Because the hadd is dropped, so lineage cannot be established.

Key Takeaway
Nasab requires a marital bed or its legal semblance; therefore, it is established only in shubhah fi al-mahall when claimed, never in shubhah fi al-fi'l.

When Claimed Doubt Does Not Prevent Hadd
Lists specific cases where shubhah is not accepted and hadd is imposed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two specific cases where shubhah is rejected and apply the concept of insibasat to determine when a claim of doubt is invalid.

Core Idea
Valid shubhah requires a legal or customary basis; mere assumption is insufficient.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq clarifies important boundaries in hudud: when a claim of doubt about the permissibility of intercourse fails. The two cases—intercourse with a relative's slave woman and with a woman found on one's bed—illustrate that shubhah must be grounded in recognized ownership, practice, or perception. The analysis hinges on the concept of insibasat (common usage) and the intimacy of marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Cases
State the two scenarios: (1) intercourse with a brother's or uncle's slave woman, (2) intercourse with an unrelated woman found on one's own bed.
The first case extends to all relatives except children/descendants.
2
Articulate the Claimed Shubhah
In each case, the man claims he assumed the act was permissible or that the woman was his wife. Identify these claims.
For the slave woman: claim of mistaken ownership or permissibility. For the bed: claim of mistaken identity.
3
Apply the Hanafi Criterion for Shubhah
Determine whether the claim rests on a recognized basis: insibasat (common usage) for ownership, or perceptible confusion for identity. The text denies insibasat between brothers/uncles and denies confusion after long companionship.
Even a blind man knows his wife after long companionship by touch, smell, voice.
4
Conclude on Hadd
Because no valid shubhah exists, the hadd penalty is wajib (obligatory) and not waived.
This contrasts with theft from these relatives, where hadd is still not applied due to lack of hifz.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أمة أخيه وعمه التقييد بهما اتفاقي؛ لأن وجوب الحد لا يختلف في إماء سائر المحارم سوى الولاد لانتفاء الشبهة في الملك وفي الفعل لعدم انبساط كل مال الآخر فدعوى ظنه الحل غير معتبرة؛ لأنها لم تستند إلى دليل بخلاف السرقة من هؤلاء حيث لا يقطع بها يده؛ لأن حد السرقة يجب بهتك الحرز و لم يوجد رمز الحقائق: ۳۸۲/۱] (فتح) وامرأة وجدها إلخ: أي وحد أيضاً بوطء امرأة أجنبية وجدها على فراشه وإن قال: ظننت أنها امرأتي؛ لأنه لا اشتباه بعد طول صحبة فلم يكن ظنه مستنداً إلى دليل الشبهة وكذا إذا كان أعمى؛ لأن امرأته لا تخفى عليه بعد طول الصحبة، يعرفها بالحس والنفس والرائحة والصوت، بخلاف إذا دعاها فأجابته أجنبية فقالت: أنا امرأتك فوطئها، =
The slave woman of his brother and his uncle: the restriction to these is incidental, because the obligation of hadd does not differ regarding slave women of all other relatives except children, because there is no shubhah in ownership or in the act due to lack of common usage (insibasit) of each other's property. So the claim of assuming permissibility is not considered, because it is not based on any proof, unlike theft from these where the hand is not cut because the hadd for theft requires breaking the Hitz, which is not present. And a woman he found on his bed: he is also penalized for having intercourse with an unrelated woman he found on his bed, even if he says 'I thought she was my wife', because there is no confusion after long companionship, so his assumption is not based on any proof of shubhah. Similarly, if he is blind, because his wife would not be unknown to him after long companionship; he recognizes her by touch, smell, and voice. The exception is if he calls, and an unrelated woman responds saying 'I am your wife', and he has intercourse with her.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage addresses situations where the excuse of shubhah is not accepted. The first case is intercourse with a brother's or uncle's slave woman. Unlike a father's slave woman, there is no common usage (basuta) between brothers or uncles of each other's property, so there is no basis for a claim of doubt. The hadd is applied. The text notes this is different from theft from these relatives, where the hand is not cut because the owner's property is not adequately protected. The second case is a man who finds a woman on his bed and has intercourse with her, claiming he thought she was his wife. After long companionship, a man knows his wife, so no confusion can be claimed. Even a blind man knows his wife by other senses. However, if a woman answers his call and claims to be his wife, and he then has intercourse, that might create a shubhah (text cuts off).

Key Terms
انبساط (insibasat): Common usage or mutual dealing in property. Its absence between relatives like brothers/uncles negates any claim of doubt in ownership.
الشبهة (shubhah): A legally recognized doubt that could prevent the application of criminal penalties (hadd).

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the brother consented.
D) Because the man is not allowed to have intercourse with any slave woman.

Key Takeaway
Hadd for illicit intercourse is imposed when a claim of doubt lacks an objective basis such as common usage or perceptible confusion.

Shubha in Act vs. Object and Paternity Rule
Ruling with proof on shubha and paternity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between shubha in the act and shubha in the object, and apply the Hanafi rule that paternity is established only in the latter.

Core Idea
Paternity requires some right or ownership in the woman—mere shubha in the act drops the hadd but does not establish lineage.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains a critical distinction in Hanafi hudud law: the difference between shubha in the act (shubhat al-fi‘l) and shubha in the object (shubhat al-mahall). Both types of ambiguity prevent the hadd penalty for unlawful intercourse, but only the latter also establishes paternity (nasad) of the child. We will examine the four classical examples and the underlying proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of shubha
Shubha in the act relates to a mistaken belief about the permissibility of the act itself; shubha in the object relates to a mistaken belief about the status of the woman (e.g., thinking she is his wife when she is not). The text gives four examples of the former and one of the latter.
The only example of shubha in the object here is the woman in 'iddah from three divorces.
2
Analyze the four examples of shubha in the act
The four cases: (1) woman in 'iddah of three divorces, (2) parents' female slave, (3) wife's female slave, (4) master's female slave. In each, the prohibition is certain but due to lingering rights or customary ease (bast), the hadd is dropped if the man thought it permissible.
For case (1), remaining rights include maintenance and the prohibition of remarrying her sister.
3
Examine the proofs for each case
For the 'iddah case, the Qur'an (2:230) proves absolute prohibition, but remaining rights create shubha. For the wife's slave, the verse (93:8) about the Prophet's enrichment by Khadija is cited to suggest a possible misunderstanding. For parents' and master's slaves, customary ease (bast) is the basis.
The proofs are both textual (Qur'an) and customary (urf).
4
Distinguish the paternity rule
Lineage (nasad) is established only in the 'iddah case (shubha in the object) because some form of right or ownership remains in the woman, providing a 'marital bed' (firash). In the other four cases, no such right exists, so the intercourse is pure zina except that the penalty is waived.
Paternity requires the child to be born on a valid marital bed or its shubha.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Zufar holds that the man should be punished for intercourse with his parents' female slave even if he thought it permissible, because the shubha is weak. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that no hadd is applied.
This disagreement is recorded in Ramz al-Haqa'iq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الوطء الذي يوجب إن ظن حله كمعتدة الثلاث وأمة أبويه وزوجته وسيده، والنسب يثبت في الأولى فقط أي الواطئ أي نسب الولد من الواطئ فقط، وحد بوطء أمة أخيه وعمّه وإن ظنّ حلّه، وامرأة وجدها على فراشه، أي الواطئ أي وبوطئ أمة عمه أي وحد أيضاً بوطء امرأة ظن حله لقيام الشبهة حتى إذا ظن حرمته لا يسقط الحد لعدم الملك. (عيني) كمعتدة الثلاث: مثال لعدم الحد بشبهة الفعل أي كوطء المعتدة بالطلقات الثلاث ولو جملة؛ لأنها حرمتها مقطوع به؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَإِنْ طَلَّقَهَا فَلا تَحِلُّ لَهُ مِنْ بَعْدُ﴾ (البقرة: ۲۳۰) فلم يبق له فيها ملك ولا حق، غير أنه بقي فيها بعض الأحكام كالنفقة والسكنى والمنع من الخروج، وثبوت النسب، وحرمة أختها وأربع سواها، وعدم قبول شهادة كل واحد منهما لصاحبه، فحصل الاشتباه، فأورث شبهة إن ظن حله؛ لأنه في موضع الاشتباه فيعذر. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٨٢/١] إذا طلق امرأة طلاقاً صحيحاً فوطئها في العدة وقال: ظننت أنها تحل لي أي علمت أن الزنا حرام لكن ظننت يعني أن هذا الوطء ليس محرماً لا يحد ولو قال علمت أن هذا الوطء حرام يحد. (فتح) وأمة أبويه مثال ثان لعدم الحد بشبهة الفعل أي كوطء أمة أبويه؛ لأنها لا تحل للولد لتباين الأملاك بينهم غير أن البسوطة تجري بينهم في الانتفاع بالأموال والرضا عادة، فإذا ظن الوطء من هذا القبيل يعذر ولا يحد، وقال زفر يحد. رمز الحقائق: ۳۸۲/۱] (محشي) وزوجته أي وكوطء أمة زوجته، فإن غنى الزوج بمال زوجته قوله تعالى: ﴿وَوَجَدَكَ عَائِلاً فَأَغْنَى﴾ (الضحى: ۸) أي بمال خديجة لها فيورث شبهة أن مال الزوجة ملك الزوج، فلا يحد إذا ظن الحل، وقوله : "وسيده" وكوطء أمة سيده إذا ظنه حلالاً تجري البسوطة بينهما لا يحد، وكذا المطلقة على مال وأم الولد إذا أعتقها مولاها. (عيني، فتح) مستفاد من النسب يثبت في الأولى فقط: أي يثبت نسب الولد من الواطئ في الوطء بشبهة في المحل بشرط إن ادعاه الواطئ ولا يثبت في الوطء بشبهة الفعل ولو ادعاه؛ لأن النسب يعتمد قيام الملك أو الحق في المحل؛ لأنه لا يثبت بدون الفراش والفراش أو شبهته يوجد بأحدهما، وفي النوع الأول وجد أحدهما، فلم يتمحض زنا، ولم يتحقق في الثاني؛ لفرض أن لا شبهة ملك فتمحض زنا إلا أن الحد سقط؛ لظنه وهو أمر راجع إليه لا إلى المحل. رمز الحقائق: ۳۸۲/۱] (فتح)
Chapter of intercourse that necessitates [the hadd]. If he thought it permissible, like [intercourse with] a woman in her waiting period of three divorces, and a female slave of his parents, and his wife's female slave, and his master's female slave. Lineage is established only in the first. (Meaning: the lineage of the child from the man who had intercourse.) And he is punished for intercourse with his brother's female slave and his uncle's female slave even if he thought it permissible. And a woman he found on his bed. (Meaning: he is also punished for intercourse with his uncle's female slave; and he is also punished for intercourse with a woman he thought permissible due to the presence of shubha, but if he thought it forbidden, the hadd is not dropped because of lack of ownership.) (Ayni) "Like a woman in her waiting period of three divorces": an example of no hadd due to shubha in the act, i.e., like intercourse with a woman in her waiting period from three divorces even if collectively; because her prohibition is certain due to His saying: "Then she is not lawful for him after that" (2:230). So he has no ownership or right over her, but some rulings remain like maintenance, housing, prohibition of leaving, establishment of lineage, prohibition of her sister and four others, and inadmissibility of each other's testimony. So confusion occurred, which gave rise to shubha if he thought it permissible; because he is in a place of confusion, so he is excused. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 382/1] If he divorced his wife validly and then had intercourse with her during the waiting period and said, "I thought she was permissible for me," i.e., he knew that zina is forbidden but he thought that this act is not forbidden, he is not punished. But if he said, "I knew that this act is forbidden," he is punished. (Fath) "And his parents' female slave": a second example of no hadd due to shubha in the act, i.e., like intercourse with his parents' female slave; because she is not permissible for the son due to the separation of ownership between them, except that ease (bast) generally exists between them in benefiting from wealth and mutual consent. So if he thought the intercourse was of this type, he is excused and not punished. Zufar said he is punished. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 382/1] (Mahshi) "And his wife's [female slave]": i.e., like intercourse with his wife's female slave. Indeed, the husband is enriched by his wife's wealth due to His saying: "And He found you poor and made you rich" (93:8), i.e., by Khadija's wealth. So this gives rise to shubha that the wife's wealth is the husband's property, so he is not punished if he thought it permissible. And His (saying): "And his master's" and like intercourse with his master's female slave if he thought it was permissible; there is ease between them, so he is not punished. Similarly, the woman divorced for a compensation and the umm walad when her master frees her. (Ayni, Fath) Benefited: "Lineage is established only in the first": i.e., the lineage of the child from the man who had intercourse is established in intercourse with shubha in the object, on condition that he claims the child, and it is not established in intercourse with shubha in the act even if he claims it; because lineage depends on the existence of ownership or right in the object, since it is not established without a marital bed (firash) or its shubha, which exists by one of them. In the first type, one of them existed, so it was not pure zina; in the second, it was not realized because it is assumed that there is no shubha of ownership, so it was pure zina, except that the hadd was dropped due to his thought, which is something pertaining to him, not to the object. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 382/1] (Fath)
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explained by al-‘Ayni and others. It addresses the crucial distinction between two types of shubha (legal ambiguity) that prevent the hadd penalty for unlawful intercourse: shubha in the act (shubhat al-fi‘l) and shubha in the object (shubhat al-mahall). The chapter begins by listing four cases where the hadd is not imposed if the person thought the act was permissible: (1) intercourse with a woman during her ‘iddah after three irrevocable divorces, (2) intercourse with a parent's female slave, (3) intercourse with one's wife's female slave, and (4) intercourse with one's master's female slave. In all these, the prohibition is clear, but due to some lingering rights or customary practices, a person might genuinely misunderstand, so the hadd is dropped. However, paternity (nasad) is established only in the first type—shubha in the object—because there, some form of right or ownership exists in the woman, making the intercourse resemble a valid marriage bed. In shubha in the act, no such right exists, so the intercourse is considered pure zina except that the penalty is waived due to ignorance. The text provides detailed proofs, including the Qur’anic verse from Surah al-Baqarah for the irrevocably divorced woman, and the verse from Surah al-Duha for the wife's wealth. A disagreement with Zufar is noted for the case of the parent's slave. The paternity rule is critical: lineage is a right of the child and is only established when the intercourse occurred under some semblance of ownership or marital right.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubha): Legal ambiguity that prevents the application of the hadd penalty, based on a reasonable but mistaken belief in permissibility.
نسب (nasad): Paternity or lineage; established by valid marriage or intercourse under shubha in the object.
معتدة الثلاث (mu‘taddat al-thalath): A woman observing the waiting period after three irrevocable divorces.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which of the following cases does paternity (nasad) of the child become established according to the Hanafi school?
A) A man has intercourse with a woman he found on his bed, thinking she is his wife, but she is a stranger.
B) A man has intercourse with his wife's female slave, thinking it is permissible.
C) A man has intercourse with a woman in her 'iddah from three divorces, thinking it is permissible.
D) A man has intercourse with his brother's female slave, thinking it is permissible.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, shubha in the act drops the hadd but does not give lineage; shubha in the object drops the hadd and also establishes paternal lineage because it provides a semblance of a marital bed.

Hadd for Intercourse with Relative's Slave and Found Woman
Establishes hadd for intercourse with relative's slave and found woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on hadd for intercourse with a brother's/uncle's female slave and a woman found on one's bed, and explain why shubha is absent in each case.

Core Idea
Hadd is imposed where no shubha exists; bare claims of mistake without objective evidence are insufficient.

The passage presents two additional cases where the hadd penalty applies: intercourse with a brother's or uncle's female slave, and intercourse with a foreign woman found on one's bed. In both, the Hanafi school holds that there is no valid doubt (shubha) to excuse the offender. The reasoning turns on the absence of customary mutual use (bast) between siblings and the impossibility of confusion after long companionship, even for a blind man. The passage also notes a significant intra-madhhab disagreement regarding the woman on the bed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage first states that hadd is obligatory for intercourse with a brother's or uncle's female slave. Then it extends the same ruling to a foreign woman found on one's bed. Note the incidental specification: the rule applies to all mahram relatives except parents/children.
The exception for parents is due to bast (customary ease) which creates shubha.
2
Analyze the absence of shubha
For the slave case, there is no shubha in ownership (no mutual property use between siblings/uncles and nephews) and no shubha in the act itself. For the found woman, after long marriage there is no confusion; even a blind man can identify his wife by touch, smell, or voice. Thus claims of mistaken belief are invalid without objective evidence.
This contrasts with the earlier case of a parent's slave where bast creates shubha.
3
Examine the exceptions to the found woman case
If a man calls his wife and a stranger answers claiming to be his wife, no hadd because his belief is based on the woman's statement (shar'i evidence). Similarly, if the stranger gives his wife's name, no hadd. But if she merely responds without identifying, hadd applies.
The key is whether the belief is founded on a shar'i evidence.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (madhhab dispute)
The passage mentions that according to 'the three' (likely Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar, or the three other schools), the man who finds a woman on his bed is not punished. Their reasoning is that the woman being on his bed creates sufficient shubha. The Hanafi position responds that after long companionship this doubt is removed.
This ikhtilaf illustrates the strict Hanafi stance on shubha derived from custom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أمة أخيه وعمه التقييد بهما اتفاقي؛ لأن وجوب الحد لا يختلف في إماء سائر المحارم سوى الولاد لانتفاء الشبهة في الملك وفي الفعل لعدم انبساط كل مال الآخر فدعوى ظنه الحل غير معتبرة؛ لأنها لم تستند إلى دليل بخلاف السرقة من هؤلاء حيث لا يقطع بها يده؛ لأن حد السرقة يجب بهتك الحرز و لم يوجد رمز الحقائق: ۳۸۲/۱] (فتح) وامرأة وجدها إلخ: أي وحد أيضاً بوطء امرأة أجنبية وجدها على فراشه وإن قال: ظننت أنها امرأتي؛ لأنه لا اشتباه بعد طول صحبة فلم يكن ظنه مستنداً إلى دليل الشبهة وكذا إذا كان أعمى؛ لأن امرأته لا تخفى عليه بعد طول الصحبة، يعرفها بالحس والنفس والرائحة والصوت، بخلاف إذا دعاها فأجابته أجنبية فقالت: أنا امرأتك فوطئها، فإنه لا حد عليه أو قال: حسبتها امرأتي؛ لأن ظنه استند إلى دليل شرعي وهو الإخبار، وبخلاف ما لو قالت: أنا فلانة باسم امرأته فواقعها لا يحد لما ذكرنا، وإن أجابته ولم تقل أنا امرأتك ولا أنا فلانة يحد كالمسألة الكتابية، وعند الثلاثة: لا يحد فيمن وجدها على فراشه [ رمز الحقائق: ۳۸۲/۱] (مستخلص)
His brother's and his uncle's female slaves: the specification to these two is incidental; because the obligation of hadd does not differ regarding female slaves of other mahram relatives except parents [because of the shubha from the custom of mutual use], due to the absence of shubha in ownership and in the act due to the lack of mutual ease in each other's wealth. So his claim of thinking it permissible is not considered because it is not based on evidence, unlike theft from these people where the hand is not cut because the hadd of theft requires breaking the hiraz, which did not exist. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 382/1] (Fath) "And a woman he found etc.": i.e., he is also punished for intercourse with a foreign woman he found on his bed, even if he said, "I thought she was my wife," because there is no confusion after long companionship, so his thought was not based on evidence of shubha. Similarly, even if he is blind, because his wife is not hidden from him after long companionship; he recognizes her by touch, smell, voice. But if he called and a foreign woman responded and said, "I am your wife," and he had intercourse with her, then he is not punished, or if he said, "I thought she was my wife" because his thought was based on shar‘i evidence, which is the information. And unlike if she said, "I am so-and-so" using his wife's name and he had intercourse with her, he is not punished as we mentioned. But if she responded and did not say "I am your wife" nor "I am so-and-so," he is punished, like the case of the book (the earlier ruling). According to the three (Imams), he is not punished for one he found on his bed. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 382/1] (Mustakhlas)
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage continues the same chapter, now addressing cases where the hadd penalty IS imposed. First, intercourse with a brother's or uncle's female slave: unlike the earlier cases of parents' slave, there is no customary ease (bast) between siblings/uncles and nephews regarding property, so there is no shubha at all. Therefore, the claim of mistaken belief is ineffective, and hadd is obligatory. The text notes an incidental detail: the same applies to all mahram relatives except parents (including children? actually 'siva al-wilad' means except parents/children? but the exception is for parents only because of the custom). Second, a foreign woman found on one's bed: even if the man claims he thought she was his wife, after long companionship there is no ambiguity; so hadd is imposed. This extends to a blind man who can recognize his wife by other senses. However, if a man calls his wife and a stranger responds claiming to be his wife, no hadd applies because he relied on a shar‘i evidence (the woman's statement). If the responding woman gives his wife's name, similarly no hadd. But if she merely responds without identifying herself, hadd is imposed. The passage ends with a notable ikhtilaf: the three (probably referring to Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar, or the three other schools) say that the man who finds a woman on his bed is not punished, contradicting the Hanafi position stated here. This highlights the strictness of the Hanafi view in presuming knowledge after long cohabitation.

Key Terms
بسوطة (bastutah): Customary ease and mutual use of property between family members, which can create shubha.
حرز (hirz): Proper storage or protection of property; necessary for hadd of theft.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a man has intercourse with his uncle's female slave, is he liable for hadd?
A) Yes, because there is no shubha from bast between uncle and nephew.
B) No, because an uncle's slave is like a parent's slave.
C) Yes, but only if the slave was not previously shared.
D) No, because hadd only applies to freewomen.

Key Takeaway
Hadd for zina is applied whenever the accused cannot point to objective evidence (shubha) supporting his claim of mistake; the absence of bast or long companionship negates potential doubt.

No Hadd for a Man Deceived by a False Claim of Marriage
Ruling on sent woman with wife claim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a man has intercourse with a woman sent to him as his wife, and explain why hadd is not imposed while mahr and iddah remain wajib.

Core Idea
Shubha from credible report exempts hadd but not financial and post-marital obligations.

This lesson examines a nuanced case in hudud: a man led to believe a woman is his wife due to others' testimony. Although the act is technically zina, the hadd penalty is suspended because the man relied on shar'i evidence. Yet, he must pay the mahr and she must observe iddah. We will unpack the reasoning and the disagreement over ihsan removal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and initial ruling
What is the specific case? A woman is sent to a man with the claim 'she is your wife'. He has intercourse. The ruling is: no hadd penalty for zina.
2
Locate the dalil and reasoning
Why no hadd? Because the man relied on evidence (the report) in a place of confusion. He is likened to a maghrur (deceived person). The judgment of 'Ali (r.a.) supports this.
3
Determine the remaining obligations
Though no hadd, the man must pay mahr al-mithl and the woman must observe iddah. Why? Because in Dar al-Islam, unlawful intercourse either incurs hadd or mahr; since hadd fell, mahr becomes wajib.
The mahr is due regardless of the man's mistake.
4
Analyze the consequence for ihsan
The man's ihsan (state of being married) is removed because the act is still zina in reality. This means if he commits zina again, he will be lashed, not stoned. Note the disagreement: Abu Yusuf holds ihsan is not removed.
Zahir al-riwayah (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) holds ihsan is removed.
5
Distinguish from the previous case
In the earlier case (woman found on bed without claim), the man is liable for hadd. Here, the external claim creates a shubha that exempts him from hadd. The key difference is the presence of credible misinformation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا بأجنبية: أي لا حد بوطء أجنبية بعثت إلى الزوج وقلن له هي زوجتك، لكن يجب عليه المهر، وعليها العدة، وبذلك قضى علي الله ؛ لأنه اعتمد دليلاً في موضع الاشتباه، والدليل هو الإخبار؛ إذ الإنسان لا يميز بين امرأته وغيرها في أول الوهلة فصار كالمغرور ولهذا يثبت نسبه ولا يحد قاذفه؛ لأنه وطئ حرام في غير الملك، فيسقط به إحصانه، وعن أبي يوسف لا يسقط، وقوله : وعليه المهر؛ لأن الوطء في دار الإسلام لا يخلو عن حد ومهر، وقد سقط الحد، فوجب مهر المثل. (مستخلص، فتح عيني) زوجتك وكان قد تزوج امرأة ولم يدخل بها . ( عيني) وعليه المهر : أي وعلى واطئ المزفوفة مهر المثل وعليها العدة. (ط)
"No to a foreign woman": i.e., no hadd for intercourse with a foreign woman who was sent to the husband and they said to him, "She is your wife," but he must pay the dower (mahr) and she must observe the waiting period. And by this did ‘Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) judge, because he relied on evidence in a place of confusion, and the evidence is the report; since a person does not distinguish between his wife and another in the first instance, so he becomes like one deceived. For this reason, his lineage is established and his defamer is not punished, because he committed a forbidden act without ownership, so his ihsan is removed. According to Abu Yusuf, it is not removed. His statement: "and he must pay the dower" because intercourse in Dar al-Islam cannot be free from either hadd or dower; and since the hadd has fallen, the dower of the like (mahr al-mithl) becomes obligatory. (Mustakhlas, Fath Ayni) "your wife" and he had married a woman but had not consummated with her. (Ayni) "And he must pay the dower": i.e., upon the one who had intercourse with the woman sent in the wedding procession is the mahr al-mithl, and upon her is the waiting period. (Tayyibi?)
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage deals with a specific scenario: a woman is sent to a man's house with the claim that she is his wife (perhaps after a marriage contract that he may not have been aware of). The ruling is that he is not subject to the hadd penalty for zina, because his mistake is based on credible evidence—the people's statement. He is considered like a deceived person (maghrur). However, he must pay the mahr al-mithl (proper dower) to the woman, and she must observe an ‘iddah (waiting period) before remarrying. This was the judgment of Caliph ‘Ali (r.a.). The text also notes a consequence for the man's ihsan (state of being married): since he committed a forbidden act (zina in reality) without ownership, his ihsan is removed, meaning he is no longer considered muhsan for the purpose of stoning in future zina. There is a disagreement with Abu Yusuf on whether ihsan is removed. The dower is obligatory because in Dar al-Islam, any unlawful intercourse either incurs hadd or necessitates dower; since hadd is dropped due to the shubha, dower is due. This case is distinguished from the earlier one where the man finds a woman on his bed without any claim; there, hadd is imposed. The key factor is the presence of an external claim that the woman is his wife, which creates a valid shubha.

Key Terms
مغرور (maghrur): One who is deceived; a person whose mistake is due to misinformation from others, thus excused from hadd.
إحصان (ihsan): The legal status of being married and having consummated the marriage, which makes one liable for stoning if zina is committed.
شبهة (shubha): A doubt or ambiguity in the legal status of an act, often arising from incorrect information or mistaken belief.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a woman sent to a man with the claim 'she is your wife', why is the man not punished with hadd?
A) Because the woman was sent and he was forced.
B) Because he relied on shar‘i evidence (the people's report) in a place of confusion.
C) Because he did not have intercourse.
D) Because the woman was actually his wife.

Key Takeaway
When a man is deceived by a credible claim that a woman is his wife, the hadd penalty for zina is lifted, but he must pay mahr and she must observe 'iddah; his ihsan is also removed.

No Hadd for Marriage to a Permanently Forbidden Woman: The Hanafi Doctrine of Shubhat al-‘Aqd
Intra-Hanafi dispute on hadd for forbidden marriage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on hadd for intercourse with a permanently forbidden woman and distinguish Abu Hanifa's view from that of the Sahibayn, citing the concept of shubhat al-‘aqd.

Core Idea
A void marriage contract creates shubha sufficient to avert hadd, though ta‘zir may apply.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute about the application of hadd (fixed penalty) when a person marries a woman who is permanently forbidden (e.g., a mahram by blood, fosterage, or affinity) and has intercourse with her. The central question is whether the defective marriage contract creates a legal ambiguity (shubhat al-‘aqd) that averts the hadd penalty, or whether the decisive nature of the prohibition makes the contract completely void and thus no shubha exists. The lesson contrasts the positions of Abu Hanifa and his two foremost disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of the Hanafi school as presented in the text: according to Abu Hanifa, no hadd is applied for intercourse with a permanently forbidden woman, regardless of knowledge, because the marriage contract creates a shubha. If the person knew, ta‘zir is given.
This is the mufta bihi position of the school.
2
Identify the intra-madhhab dispute
Note that the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree: if the person knew the prohibition, hadd is applied because the prohibition is based on decisive proof (nas qat‘i) and the contract is void ab initio.
The other three imams (Shafi‘i, Maliki, Hanbali) also hold this view.
3
Analyze the reasoning of each side
For Abu Hanifa: the contract has a valid subject (a woman capable of procreation) and should have been valid, but the text prevents actual permissibility, creating doubt (shubha). For the Sahibayn: the contract fails because the woman is not a valid object (mahall) for the ruling of permissibility, so it is completely void.
Focus on the concept of shubhat al-‘aqd versus the requirement of a valid mahall.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
According to Abu Hanifa, lineage is established from such intercourse, and hadd is not applied. According to the Sahibayn, lineage is not established, and hadd is applied if knowledge is present.
This difference affects family law and criminal punishment.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The text supports Abu Hanifa's view as the primary position of the school, and it is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view for fatwa.
Later Hanafi authorities have consistently adopted this position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبمحرمة نكحها [ أي ولا يحد أيضاً بوطء امرأة محرم نسباً ورضاعاً أو صهرية. (ط، عيني] أي من تزوج امرأة لا يحل له نكاحها فوطئها لم يجب عليه الحد، وهذا هو الشبهة في العقد سواء كان عالماً بالحرمة أو لم يكن عند أبي حنيفة، لكن إن كان عالماً يوجع بالضرب تعزيراً، وعندهما: إن كان عالماً بالحرمة يحد في وطء كل امرأة محرمة عليه على التأبيد، أو ذات زوج؛ لأن حرمتهن بدليل قطعي، وبه قالت الثلاثة، وله: أن فيه شبهة الحل وهو النكاح، ويثبت النسب عنده لا عندهما. وهذا هو الشبهة في العقد، ومنها وطء المتزوجة بغير شهود ووطء أمة تزوجها على حرة، أو تزوج خمساً في عقد واحد فوطئهن أو جمع بين الأختين في عقد وطئهما لا يجب الحد في جميع ذلك عنده، لهما وللثلاثة: أن هذا عقد لا يصادف محله فيلغو؛ لأن محل التصرف ما يكون محلاً للحكم، وحكمه الحل، ولا حل في المحرمة، فلا يكون محل العقد، وله أن العقد صادف محله؛ لأن محل التصرف ما يقبل المقصود، والأنثى من بنات آدم قابلة للتوالد وهو المقصود وكان ينبغي أن ينعقد في جميع الأحكام، إلا أنه تقاعد عن إفادة حقيقة الحل بالنص، فيورث الشبهة إلا أنه أرتكب جريمة، وليس فيها حد مقرر فيعزر. (مستخلص، عيني)
"And a permanently forbidden woman he married" [i.e., he is also not punished for intercourse with a woman who is forbidden by lineage, fosterage, or affinity. (T, Ayni)] i.e., whoever marries a woman whose marriage is not permissible for him and then has intercourse with her, the hadd is not obligatory upon him. This is the shubha in the contract (shubhat al-‘aqd), whether he was aware of the prohibition or not according to Abu Hanifa. However, if he was aware, he is subjected to painful beating as ta‘zir. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): if he was aware of the prohibition, he is punished for intercourse with every woman who is permanently forbidden to him, or a married woman, because their prohibition is based on a decisive proof (dalil qat‘i). And the three (Imams) also said this. His (Abu Hanifa's) argument: there is a shubha of permissibility, which is the marriage contract (nikah). And lineage is established according to him, not according to them. This is the shubha in the contract. Among [examples] are: intercourse with a married woman without witnesses, intercourse with a female slave one marries while having a free wife, or one marries five women in one contract and has intercourse with them, or marries two sisters in one contract and has intercourse with them — in all these, the hadd is not obligatory according to him. According to them and the three, such a contract does not meet its object, so it is void; because the object of the contract is that which is a place for the ruling, and its ruling is permissibility (hill), and there is no permissibility in the forbidden woman, so she is not a valid object of the contract. His (Abu Hanifa's) argument: the contract does meet its object because the object of the contract is that which can receive the intended purpose, and a female descendant of Adam is capable of procreation, which is the purpose; so it should have been valid in all rulings, except that it falls short of communicating actual permissibility due to the text [of Qur'an], so it gives rise to shubha. Nevertheless, he has committed a crime for which there is no fixed hadd, so he is given ta‘zir. (Mustakhlas, Ayni)
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage presents a significant intra-Hanafi dispute regarding intercourse with a woman whom one has married despite a permanent prohibition (e.g., mahram by blood, marriage to two sisters in one contract, etc.). According to Abu Hanifa, the hadd penalty is not applied in any of these cases, because the marriage contract itself, even if invalid, creates a shubha of permissibility (shubhat al-‘aqd). This shubha is strong enough to avert the hadd, regardless of whether the person knew the prohibition or not. However, if he was aware, he is subject to ta‘zir (disciplinary beating). In contrast, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that if the person knew the prohibition, the hadd is obligatory because the prohibition is based on a decisive text (dalil qat‘i), and the contract is void ab initio; it does not create any valid shubha. They are joined by the three (the other imams: Shafi‘i, Maliki, Hanbali) on this point. The practical consequence: according to Abu Hanifa, lineage is established from such intercourse; according to the Sahibayn, it is not. The text provides the rationale: for Abu Hanifa, the contract is defective but not completely void because the woman is capable of procreation, which is the intended purpose, so it creates doubt. For the Sahibayn, the contract fails to meet its object (mahall) because the woman is not a valid subject for the ruling of permissibility, so it is completely void and no shubha exists.

Key Terms
شبهة العقد (shubhat al-‘aqd): Legal ambiguity created by a defective contract that resembles a valid marriage, sufficient to avert the hadd.
تعزير (ta‘zir): Discretionary punishment for crimes without fixed penalties; used here for knowingly entering an invalid marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling for a man who knowingly marries his foster sister and has intercourse with her?
A) He is liable for hadd (stoning or flogging).
B) He is not liable for hadd but is given ta‘zir.
C) He is not liable for any punishment because it was a valid marriage.
D) He is liable for hadd only if he did not know the prohibition.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a void marriage contract creates shubhat al-‘aqd, which averts the hadd penalty for intercourse, though ta‘zir may apply if the prohibition was known.

No Hadd for Intercourse Outside the Vagina
States the absence of hadd for non-vaginal intercourse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intercourse with a foreign woman outside the vagina and distinguish between hadd and ta'zir.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, hadd for zina applies only to vaginal intercourse; all other illicit sexual acts incur ta'zir.

This lesson presents a key distinction in Hanafi hudud law: the penalty for unlawful sexual intercourse is strictly defined by the type of act. While zina (vaginal penetration) incurs a fixed hadd penalty, other forms of sexual contact are treated differently. Understanding this ruling clarifies the precise boundaries of the hudud penalties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Act
Recognize that the passage deals with intercourse with a foreign woman in an orifice other than the vagina (e.g., anus, navel).
2
Determine the Ruling
The ruling is that no hadd penalty (flogging or stoning) applies. The act is still haram and subject to ta'zir.
Ta'zir is a discretionary punishment decided by the judge.
3
Understand the Rationale
The absence of hadd is because the act does not fall under the legal definition of zina, which is specifically vaginal penetration.
4
Compare Cross-Madhhab
Note that the Shafi'i school holds that anal intercourse does incur hadd. This is a point of ikhtilaf.
The Hanafi position is based on their strict definition of zina.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبأجنبية في غير القبل: [أي في الدبر أو في السرة ونحوها. (عيني)] أي ولا حد أيضاً بوطء أجنبية فيما دون الفرج مطلقاً، لا جلداً ولا رجماً، ولكن يعزر ؛ لأنه أتى بفعل منكر ليس فيه شيء مقدر من الحدود فيعزر. (مستخلص)
"And [no hadd] for a foreign woman in other than the vagina": [i.e., in the anus or navel, etc. (Ayni)] i.e., there is also no hadd for intercourse with a foreign woman in anything less than the vagina absolutely, neither flogging nor stoning, but he is given ta‘zir; because he committed a reprehensible act for which there is no fixed amount among the hudud, so he is given ta‘zir. (Mustakhlas)
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This is a clear ruling that the hadd penalty for zina (whether flogging or stoning) is only applicable to vaginal intercourse (al-farj). Any other form of sexual contact, such as anal intercourse, intercourse with the navel, etc., does not incur the hudud penalty. However, such acts are still sinful and subject to ta‘zir (discretionary punishment) because they are immoral acts that do not have a specified hadd amount. This ruling is consistent with the Hanafi definition of zina, which is specifically penetration of the vagina (qubul). The source clarifies that the absence of hadd is absolute, meaning no jald or rajm, but the judge may impose ta‘zir based on the circumstances.

Key Terms
دون الفرج (dun al-farj): Less than the vagina; any orifice other than the female genitals (anterior).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the penalty for anal intercourse with a foreign woman?
A) The same as zina: flogging or stoning.
B) No penalty at all because it is not illegal.
C) Ta'zir (discretionary punishment).
D) Only a verbal reprimand.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the hadd penalty for zina is exclusively for vaginal intercourse; non-vaginal illicit acts incur ta'zir.

Hadd for Sodomy: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on punishment for sodomy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on hadd for sodomy, explain the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: no hadd for sodomy; Sahibayn: same as zina. The Hanafi school follows Abu Hanifa: ta‘zir, not hadd.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq presents the intra-Hanafi disagreement on the punishment for sodomy (lawatah). While all agree the act is haram, they differ on whether it incurs the fixed hadd of zina or only a discretionary ta‘zir penalty. Abu Hanifa restricts hadd to vaginal intercourse; the Sahibayn analogize sodomy to zina. The mufta bihi follows Abu Hanifa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the legal question
The act is lawatah (sodomy). The question: does it incur the hadd of zina (stoning/flogging) or only ta‘zir?
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling and rationale
Abu Hanifa says no hadd – only ta‘zir. His rationale: hadd is specific to vaginal penetration (the legal definition of zina); sodomy is not zina.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
State the Sahibayn's ruling and rationale
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it is like zina, so the same hadd applies. Their rationale: sodomy is analogous in meaning (ma‘nan): both fulfill sexual desire in a forbidden manner.
They are joined by the other three madhhabs.
4
Note the evidence cited
The Sahibayn use qiyas (analogy) and the hadith of Ibn ‘Abbas ordering execution of participants. Abu Hanifa rebuts that qiyas cannot create a new hadd penalty, since hudud are fixed by nass.
The hadith is incomplete in the text: 'Whoever you find doing the deed of the people of Lut, kill the active and passive.'
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical difference
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view: ta‘zir. Practically, a convicted sodomite receives a discretionary penalty (e.g. beating, imprisonment) rather than stoning/flogging.
Later Hanafi scholars allow death for recidivists as ta‘zir, but not as hadd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبلواطة: أي ولا يحد أيضاً بلواطة عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا : هو كالزنا فيحد حد الزنا، فيرجم إن كان محصناً، ويجلد إن لم يكن؛ لأنه ملحق بالزنا في المعنى؛ إذ اللواطة قضاء الشهوة في محل مشتهى على سبيل الكمال على وجه تمحض حراماً وبه قالت الثلاثة، وعنهم: يرجم لقول ابن عباس لما أنه قال: "من وجدتموه يعمل عمل قوم لوط
"And [no hadd for] sodomy": i.e., there is also no hadd for sodomy according to Abu Hanifa. But the two (Sahibayn) said: it is like zina, so he is punished with the hadd of zina: stoning if he is muhsan, flogging if not; because it is annexed to zina in meaning, since sodomy is the fulfillment of desire in a desired place in a complete manner, purely forbidden. And the three (other imams) also said this. And from them (some narrations): he is stoned due to the saying of Ibn ‘Abbas: "Whoever you find doing the deed of the people of Lut..."
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage addresses the punishment for sodomy (lawatah, i.e., anal intercourse between males). According to Abu Hanifa, the hadd penalty is not applied; instead, the offender is given ta‘zir. This is because he does not consider sodomy to be legally equivalent to zina, as the definition of zina specifically involves vaginal intercourse. The two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, disagree: they analogize sodomy to zina in meaning (ma‘nan), since it is also a complete fulfillment of sexual desire in a forbidden manner. Therefore, they apply the same hadd: if the offender is muhsan (married and had consummated his marriage), he is stoned; otherwise, he is flogged. The three other imams (Shafi‘i, Maliki, Hanbali) also hold this view. The passage mentions a report from Ibn ‘Abbas that the Prophet said to kill the active and passive participants in sodomy, which supports the severe penalty. However, the text is cut off, but it is known that the Hanafi school relies on the principle that hadd is only for zina defined as vaginal intercourse; sodomy is a separate crime (a reprehensible act) for which no fixed hadd exists, only ta‘zir. The mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school is that sodomy merits ta‘zir, not hadd, though some later Hanafi scholars have allowed the death penalty for recidivists based on policy.

Key Terms
لواطة (lawatah): Sodomy, anal intercourse between males.
عمل قوم لوط (‘amal qawm Lut): The act of the people of Lut (sodomy).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the punishment for sodomy?
A) Stoning if the offender is muhsan, otherwise flogging.
B) No punishment at all.
C) Ta‘zir (discretionary punishment).
D) Death penalty automatically.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, sodomy is not punished by hadd because the definition of zina is limited to vaginal intercourse; the mufta bihi is ta‘zir.

The Shubha Defense in Zina: The Case of the Deceived Husband
Ruling on the shubha defense when a non-mahram woman is sent as a wife.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a man is exempt from the hadd of zina when a non-mahram woman is sent to him as his wife, and identify the consequent obligations (mahr, iddah) and the effect on ihsan.

Core Idea
If a man has intercourse based on a credible report she is his wife, hadd is dropped, but mahr and iddah are wajib.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in Hanafi jurisprudence where a man is deceived by a report that a woman is his wife. The key legal issue is whether the shubha (ambiguity) arising from the report is sufficient to avert the hadd punishment for zina. We will explore the rulings, the proof from the action of 'Ali (ra), and the distinction depending on the woman's statement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario and ruling
A non-mahram woman is sent to a man, and he is told she is his wife. He has intercourse. The ruling: no hadd upon him.
This is the basic case from the text.
2
Examine the basis for exemption
The man's suspicion relied on a legal evidence (the report). This creates a shubha that averts hadd. The proof is the judgment of 'Ali (ra).
The report (khabar) is considered a valid evidence.
3
Determine the consequences
Though no hadd, the man must pay mahr al-mithl, and the woman must observe iddah. Also, his ihsan (if he had it) is dropped according to Abu Hanifa.
Hadd and mahr are mutually exclusive in this context.
4
Distinguish subcases
If the woman says 'I am your wife' or names herself as his wife, the same ruling applies. But if she merely responds without claiming, then hadd applies.
The key is whether a report (khabar) exists to support his belief.
5
Note intra-Hanafi difference
Abu Yusuf holds that ihsan is not dropped in this case. The majority view (mufta bihi) is that it is dropped.
This affects the punishment for future zina.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا بأجنبية زفت وقيل: هي زوجتك، وعليه المهر. أي لا حد بوطء أجنبية بعثت إلى الزوج وقلن له هي زوجتك، لكن يجب عليه المهر، وعليها العدة. فإنه لا حد عليه أو قال: حسبتها امرأتي؛ لأن ظنه استند إلى دليل شرعي وهو الإخبار. وبخلاف ما لو قالت: أنا فلانة باسم امرأته فواقعها لا يحد لما ذكرنا. وإن أجابته ولم تقل أنا امرأتك ولا أنا فلانة يحد كالمسألة الكتابية. وعند الثلاثة: لا يحد فيمن وجدها على فراشه. وبذلك قضى علي الله ؛ لأنه اعتمد دليلاً في موضع الاشتباه، والدليل هو الإخبار؛ إذ الإنسان لا يميز بين امرأته وغيرها في أول الوهلة فصار كالمغرور ولهذا يثبت نسبه ولا يحد قاذفه؛ لأنه وطئ حرام في غير الملك، فيسقط به إحصانه، وعن أبي يوسف لا يسقط. وقوله: وعليه المهر؛ لأن الوطء في دار الإسلام لا يخلو عن حد ومهر، وقد سقط الحد، فوجب مهر المثل. زوجتك وكان قد تزوج امرأة ولم يدخل بها. وعليه المهر: أي على واطئ المزفوفة مهر المثل وعليها العدة.
No (hadd) for a non-mahram woman sent (to the husband) and it was said: she is your wife, and upon him is the mahr. That is, there is no hadd for intercourse with a non-mahram woman sent to the husband and they said to him: she is your wife, but upon him is the mahr, and upon her is the iddah. Indeed, there is no hadd upon him if he said: I thought she was my woman; because his suspicion relied on a legal evidence, which is the report. And contrary to if she said: I am so-and-so, the name of his wife, and he had intercourse with her, there is no hadd for what we mentioned. And if she responded to him and did not say 'I am your wife' nor 'I am so-and-so', he is subject to hadd like the case of the scriptural woman. And according to the three (madhabs): no hadd on one who finds her on his bed. And with this 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) judged; because he relied on evidence in a place of doubt, and the evidence is the report; since a person cannot distinguish between his wife and another at first glance, so he becomes like the deceived, and therefore his lineage is established and his defamer is not flogged; because he made unlawful intercourse outside ownership, so his ihsan is dropped, and from Abu Yusuf it is not dropped. And his statement: and upon him is the mahr; because intercourse in the abode of Islam does not lack either hadd or mahr, and the hadd has been dropped, so the mahr of the like is obligatory. She was sent to him as a wife and he had married a woman and not consummated with her. And upon him is the mahr: i.e., upon the one who had intercourse with the sent woman is the mahr of the like, and upon her is the iddah.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the action of 'Ali (ra). It states that if a non-mahram woman is sent to a man's house and he is told she is his wife, and he has intercourse with her, then the hadd punishment is not applied because he acted on a legal evidence (the report). However, he must pay the mahr of the like, and the woman must observe iddah. The shubha (ambiguity) here arises from the report, which is a legitimate evidence in Hanafi law. If the woman says 'I am so-and-so' (naming his wife), the same ruling applies. But if she does not claim to be his wife, and he proceeds, he is subject to hadd. The passage also notes that according to the other three madhabs (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali), a man who finds a woman on his bed (without further evidence) is also not subject to hadd. Abu Yusuf holds that ihsan is not dropped in such a case. The mahr is wajib because hadd and mahr cannot both be absent; since hadd is dropped, mahr is due.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubha): An ambiguity or doubt that arises from a legal evidence (like a report) that makes the act resemble a lawful act.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The mahr equivalent to that of a woman of similar status (by family, age, beauty, etc.) when no specific mahr is agreed.
إحصان (ihsan): The quality of being free and having consummated a valid marriage, which when present makes the hadd for zina stoning instead of flogging.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a man who has intercourse with a woman sent to him as his wife when she says 'I am your wife'?
A) He is subject to hadd (flogging).
B) He is not subject to hadd but must pay mahr and the woman observes iddah.
C) He is not subject to hadd and no mahr is required.
D) He is subject to hadd and also must pay mahr.

Key Takeaway
A shubha based on a report (khabar) can avert the hadd of zina, but does not remove the obligation of mahr and iddah, and it drops ihsan.

Marrying a Mahram Relative: No Hadd due to Shubha
Ruling on marriage to a mahram relative, no hadd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on hadd for marrying a mahram relative and explain why Abu Hanifa differs from the Sahibayn using the concept of shubha fi al-'aqd.

Core Idea
A marriage contract with a mahram creates shubha, averting hadd even if the prohibition is known.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute on hudud: whether a person who knowingly marries a mahram relative (by lineage, suckling, or affinity) and consummates the marriage is subject to hadd. The disagreement hinges on the definition of shubha in the contract. Understanding this dispute clarifies how the Hanafi school balances textual prohibitions with the objective of marriage contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Dispute
The act is marrying a mahram relative (e.g., sister, aunt) and having intercourse. The dispute is whether hadd (fixed punishment) applies if the person knows the prohibition.
The ruling differs between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).
2
State the Hanafi Position (Abu Hanifa)
Abu Hanifa holds that no hadd is due because the marriage contract itself creates a shubha of permissibility, regardless of knowledge. However, if he knew, he receives ta'zir (discretionary punishment).
Lineage (nasab) is established for the child under Abu Hanifa.
3
State the Sahibayn Position and Their Dalil
The Sahibayn (and the three other madhabs) argue that if the prohibition is known, hadd applies because the prohibition is definitive (qat'i) and the contract is void (batil), so no shubha exists.
They compare this to marrying a married woman or other permanently prohibited women.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's Response (Dalil 'Aqli)
Abu Hanifa argues that the contract does encounter its subject (the woman) who is capable of procreation, the objective of marriage. Therefore, the contract has some substance, falling short only due to the textual prohibition, thus generating shubha.
This is a rational argument (dalil 'aqli) based on the purpose of marriage.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf and Mufta Bihi
The practical difference: Under Abu Hanifa, no hadd, only ta'zir; under Sahibayn, hadd applies. The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's view.
This ruling extends to other cases: marriage without witnesses, marrying over a free wife, etc.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبمحرمة نكحها [ أي ولا يحد أيضاً بوطء امرأة محرم نسباً ورضاعاً أو صهرية. (ط، عيني] أي من تزوج امرأة لا يحل له نكاحها فوطئها لم يجب عليه الحد، وهذا هو الشبهة في العقد سواء كان عالماً بالحرمة أو لم يكن عند أبي حنيفة، لكن إن كان عالماً يوجع بالضرب تعزيراً، وعندهما: إن كان عالماً بالحرمة يحد في وطء كل امرأة محرمة عليه على التأبيد، أو ذات زوج؛ لأن حرمتهن بدليل قطعي، وبه قالت الثلاثة، وله: أن فيه شبهة الحل وهو النكاح، ويثبت النسب عنده لا عندهما. وهذا هو الشبهة في العقد، ومنها وطء المتزوجة بغير شهود ووطء أمة تزوجها على حرة، أو تزوج خمساً في عقد واحد فوطئهن أو جمع بين الأختين في عقد وطئهما لا يجب الحد في جميع ذلك عنده، لهما وللثلاثة: أن هذا عقد لا يصادف محله فيلغو؛ لأن محل التصرف ما يكون محلاً للحكم، وحكمه الحل، ولا حل في المحرمة، فلا يكون محل العقد، وله أن العقد صادف محله؛ لأن محل التصرف ما يقبل المقصود، والأنثى من بنات آدم قابلة للتوالد وهو المقصود وكان ينبغي أن ينعقد في جميع الأحكام، إلا أنه تقاعد عن إفادة حقيقة الحل بالنص، فيورث الشبهة إلا أنه أرتكب جريمة، وليس فيها حد مقرر فيعزر. (مستخلص، عيني)
And by a mahram he married: i.e., also no hadd for intercourse with a woman who is a mahram by lineage, suckling, or affinity. That is, whoever marries a woman it is not permissible for him to marry and then has intercourse with her, hadd is not obligatory upon him. This is the shubha in the contract, regardless of whether he knew the prohibition or not according to Abu Hanifa. However, if he knew, he is pained by beating as ta'zir. And according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): if he knew the prohibition, he is subject to hadd for intercourse with every woman who is perpetually prohibited to him, or a married woman; because their prohibition is by a definitive evidence, and the three (madhabs) said the same. And for him (Abu Hanifa) that there is a shubha of permissibility, which is the marriage contract, and lineage is established according to him, not according to them. This is the shubha in the contract. From among these is intercourse with a married woman without witnesses, and intercourse with a slave woman he married over a free woman, or marrying five in one contract and having intercourse with them, or combining two sisters in one contract and having intercourse with them – hadd is not obligatory in all that according to him. For them (the two) and the three (madhabs): this is a contract that does not encounter its proper subject, so it is void; because the subject of action is that which is a subject for the ruling, and its ruling is permissibility, and there is no permissibility in that which is prohibited, so it is not a subject of the contract. And for him (Abu Hanifa): the contract encountered its subject; because the subject of action is that which accepts the objective, and the female offspring of Adam accept procreation, which is the objective, and it should have been valid in all rulings, except it fell short of giving the reality of permissibility by the text, so it gives rise to shubha; but he committed a crime, and there is no fixed hadd for it, so he is punished with ta'zir.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a marriage to a mahram relative (lineage, suckling, or affinity) is subject to hadd. According to Abu Hanifa, no hadd is applied due to the shubha in the contract itself, regardless of whether the person knew the prohibition. However, if he knew, he is given ta'zir (discretionary punishment). According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), if he knew the prohibition, he is subject to hadd because the prohibition is definitive (Quran and Sunnah). The other three madhabs agree with the Sahibayn. Abu Hanifa argues that the marriage contract creates a shubha of permissibility (because marriage is lawful in principle), and therefore hadd is averted. He also notes that lineage is established (the child is attributed to him) according to his view, while it is not according to the Sahibayn. This shubha in the contract extends to other cases: marriage without witnesses, marrying a slave over a free woman, marrying five in one contract, and combining two sisters in one contract – all these have shubha according to Abu Hanifa, so no hadd. The Sahibayn and the other schools say these contracts are void (batil) because they do not encounter a lawful subject, so hadd applies. Abu Hanifa's response is that the contract does encounter a subject (the woman) who accepts the objective of procreation, so it should be valid, but because it falls short of effecting actual permissibility by explicit text, it generates shubha. Therefore, hadd is not applied, but ta'zir is given.

Key Terms
شبهة في العقد (shubha fi al-'aqd): An ambiguity arising from the form of a contract that appears valid in its structure but is substantively invalid due to prohibition.
تعزير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment for crimes that have no fixed hadd, determined by the judge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling for a person who unknowingly marries his mother (mahram by lineage) and has intercourse?
A) He is subject to hadd because the prohibition is definitive.
B) He is not subject to hadd and also not subject to ta'zir.
C) He is subject to ta'zir but not hadd.
D) He is subject to hadd only if the marriage was witnessed.

Key Takeaway
A marriage contract with a mahram creates shubha due to its form and objective, averting hadd even when the prohibition is known, though ta'zir may apply.
