The Hanafi Ruling on Sodomy (Liwaṭa): Ta'zir Not Hadd
Ruling on sodomy, no hadd, only ta'zir according to Abu Hanifa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's position on the punishment for sodomy, explain the Hanafi dalil, and compare it with the opposing view.

Core Idea
Sodomy is not zina – no fixed hadd, only ta'zir in the Hanafi school.

This passage addresses the punishment for sodomy (liwaṭa), a topic of disagreement among schools. According to Abu Hanifa, it is not equivalent to zina and thus does not carry the hadd punishment, only discretionary ta'zir. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and the other three madhhabs hold that it is like zina and carries the same hadd. Let's examine the proofs and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that Abu Hanifa rules sodomy has no fixed hadd; the punishment is ta'zir left to the judge's discretion.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opposing view
Note that the Sahibayn and the three other madhhabs consider sodomy equivalent to zina, thus subject to stoning for muhsan and flogging for non-muhsan.
3
Examine the Hanafi dalil
Analyze Abu Hanifa's evidence: the Companions' disagreement on punishment methods and the rational argument that sodomy lacks the harms of zina.
The dalil is based on inference from the absence of consensus and on difference in 'illa (effective cause).
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
Understand that the opposing hadith from Ibn 'Abbas is interpreted as a political (siyasa) measure or against one who deems sodomy halal, not as a fixed hadd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبلواطة: أي ولا يحد أيضاً بلواطة عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا : هو كالزنا فيحد حد الزنا، فيرجم إن كان محصناً، ويجلد إن لم يكن؛ لأنه ملحق بالزنا في المعنى؛ إذ اللواطة قضاء الشهوة في محل مشتهى على سبيل الكمال على وجه تمحض حراماً وبه قالت الثلاثة، وعنهم: يرجم لقول ابن عباس لما أنه قال: "من وجدتموه يعمل عمل قوم لوط فاقتلوا الفاعل والمفعول به" رواه أحمد وأبو داود، ولأبي حنيفة أن الصحابة قد اختلفوا في حكم اللواطة، قال بعضهم: يحرق بالنار، وقال بعضهم: يهدم عليه الجدار ، وقال بعضهم: ينكس من موضع مرتفع ويتبع بالأحجار فلو كانت مساوية للزنا لما اختلفوا؛ إذ لا يظن بهم الاختلاف في المنصوص عليه فيعزر بأمثال هذه الأمور والرأي إلى الإمام، وليست هي في معنى الزنا؛ لأنه ليس فيها إضاعة الولد واشتباه الأنساب وإفساد الفراش؛ ولأنه نادر وقوعاً لانعدام الداعي في أحد الجانبين والداعي إلى الزنا من الجانبين، وما رووه فمحمول على السياسة أو على المستحل. (مستخلص، عيني)
And sodomy: i.e., also no hadd for sodomy according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it is like zina, so he is subject to the hadd of zina: if he is muhsan (free and married), he is stoned; if not, he is flogged; because it is annexed to zina in meaning, since sodomy is fulfilling desire in a desired place in a complete manner on a purely forbidden basis. And the three (madhabs) said the same. And from them is the narration (that he is stoned) due to the statement of Ibn 'Abbas: "Whoever you find doing the deed of the people of Lut, kill the doer and the one with whom it is done," narrated by Ahmad and Abu Dawud. And for Abu Hanifa: the Companions differed on the ruling of sodomy. Some said: he should be burnt with fire; some said: a wall should be collapsed upon him; some said: he should be thrown from a high place and followed with stones. So if it were equivalent to zina, they would not have differed; for it cannot be thought that they would differ on a matter that is prescribed by text. So he is ta'zired with these sorts of things, and the opinion is left to the Imam. And it is not like zina in meaning, because in it there is no loss of offspring, confusion of lineage, or corruption of the marriage bed; and because it occurs rarely, as there is no desire on one side, while the desire for zina is from both sides. And what they narrated is interpreted as a political (disciplinary) measure or as being against one who considers it permissible.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute on the punishment for sodomy (liwaṭa). According to Abu Hanifa, sodomy is not subject to hadd but is punished with ta'zir (discretionary punishment), and the specific form is left to the judge's discretion. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn), and the other three madhabs (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali), sodomy is equivalent to zina and thus carries the same hadd: stoning for muhsan, flogging for non-muhsan. They cite a hadith from Ibn 'Abbas (which is weak according to Hanafi scholars) ordering execution. Abu Hanifa argues that the Companions themselves differed on the method of punishment (burning, burying alive, throwing from height), which indicates that no fixed punishment is prescribed by the Quran or Sunnah. Additionally, he gives rational arguments: sodomy does not cause the same harms as zina (no offspring, no confusion of lineage, no corruption of marriage), and it is rare because the natural disposition is averse to it. Therefore, the proper punishment is ta'zir, not hadd. The hadith is interpreted as a political penalty or as applying only to those who consider it halal.

Key Terms
لواطة (liwaṭa): Anal intercourse between men (sodomy).
سياسة (siyāsa): Discretionary justice administered by the ruler for public order, not necessarily based on fixed punishments.
تعزير (ta‘zīr): Discretionary punishment left to the judge's discretion for acts that are sinful but have no fixed hadd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the punishment for sodomy according to Abu Hanifa?
A) Stoning for muhsan, flogging for non-muhsan.
B) Execution by any means.
C) Only ta'zir (discretionary punishment).
D) No punishment at all.

Key Takeaway
According to Abu Hanifa, sodomy is not equivalent to zina and is punished with ta'zir, not hadd.

Bestiality: No Hadd, Only Ta'zir, Animal Disposal
Ruling on bestiality, no hadd, ta'zir, and animal disposal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on bestiality, explain why it does not carry hadd, and identify the disposal rules for the animal and the intra-Hanafi disagreement.

Core Idea
Bestiality carries no hadd in the Hanafi school—only ta'zir—because it is not analogous to zina.

The classical Hanafi jurists address bestiality as a crime repugnant to human nature, thus not comparable to zina. This lesson examines the reasoning behind the Hanafi position, the consensus on ta'zir, and the detailed rulings on the disposal of the animal. You will also see how the other madhabs differ and where the Sahibayn disagree with Abu Hanifa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the core dispute
What is being ruled upon? The punishment for bestiality. The dispute: does it carry hadd or not?
2
Trace the Hanafi dalil
Why is there no hadd? Because it is not in the meaning of zina: no mutual desire, nature is repulsed.
3
Note the consensus on ta'zir
Despite no hadd, the perpetrator is punished by ta'zir (discretionary punishment) by consensus.
4
Analyze the animal disposal rules
Depends on whether the meat is eaten and who owns the animal.
5
Compare the intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab differences
Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn on eating; other schools on hadd and disposal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وببهيمة أي ولا يحد أيضا بوطء ببهيمة؛ لأنه ليس في معنى الزنا في كونه جناية وفي وجود الداعي؛ لأن الطبع السليم يتنفر عنه والحامل عليه غاية السفه أو فرط السبق فلا يجب الحد ولكنه يعزر بالإجماع، وعن الثلاثة يحد ثم إن كانت الدابة مما لا يؤكل لحمها تذبح،وتحرق وإن كانت مما تؤكل تذبح وتؤكل عند أبي حنيفة حاله، وقالا تحرق هذه أيضاً هذا إذا كانت البهيمة للفاعل، وإن كانت لغيره ضمن الفاعل قيمتها لصاحبها ثم تذبح، وعن الشافعي: لو كانت مما يؤكل تذبح، وعليه قيمتها لو لغيره، ويأكل منها غيره لا هو، وعن مالك: يأكل هو منها أيضاً، وعنه: لا تذبح بحال يعني سواء كانت له أو لغيره، وعن أحمد: لا يأكل هو ولا غيره. [رمز الحقائق: ۳۸۳/۱] ثم إن الإحراق ليس بواجب عندنا وإنما يفعل لقطع التحدث به إذا كانت البهيمة باقية ولما روي عن علي له أنه أمر بذبح هذه البهيمة وحرقها بعد ذبحها. (مستخلص)
And by a beast: i.e., also no hadd for intercourse with a beast; because it is not like zina in being a felony and in existence of desire; because the sound nature is averse to it, and what drives it is extreme foolishness or excessive impulsiveness, so no hadd is obligatory, but he is given ta'zir by consensus. And from the three (madhabs) he is subject to hadd. Then if the animal is of the type whose meat is not eaten, it is slaughtered and burnt. And if it is of the type whose meat is eaten, it is slaughtered and eaten according to Abu Hanifa, his current position. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: this one is also burnt. This when the animal belongs to the perpetrator. If it belongs to another, the perpetrator is liable for its value to its owner, then it is slaughtered. And from al-Shafi'i: if it is of the type eaten, it is slaughtered, and he pays its value if for another, and others eat from it but not him. And from Malik: he may eat from it also. And from him (another narration): it is not slaughtered at all, meaning whether it is his or another's. And from Ahmad: neither he nor others eat from it. Then burning is not obligatory with us (Hanafis); rather it is done to prevent talking about it if the animal is still alive, and because it was narrated from 'Ali (ra) that he ordered the slaughter of such an animal and its burning after slaughter.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage covers bestiality (intercourse with an animal). According to Hanafi law, there is no hadd for this act because it is not analogous to zina: normal human nature is repulsed by it, and the urge is not mutual. However, the perpetrator is given ta'zir (discretionary punishment) by consensus (including Hanafis and others). The other three madhabs (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) say there is hadd. The text then discusses the disposal of the animal. The Hanafi ruling: if the animal's meat is not eaten (e.g., donkey), it is slaughtered and burned. If the meat is eaten (e.g., sheep), Abu Hanifa says it is slaughtered and can be eaten (i.e., it is not impure). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say even such an animal is burned. If the animal belongs to someone else, the perpetrator must pay its value to the owner, then it is slaughtered. The other schools have various positions: Shafi'i says the animal is slaughtered, and the meat may be eaten by others but not by the perpetrator; Malik has two narrations: one allows the perpetrator to eat, another says no slaughter at all; Ahmad says no one eats. Finally, the text notes that burning is not obligatory according to the Hanafis but is done to prevent people talking about it, and it is based on a report from 'Ali (ra) who did that.

Key Terms
بهيمة (bahīma): A beast, an animal, typically applied to four-legged animals.
إجماع (ijmā'): Consensus; here it refers to the consensus of the Companions or scholars on ta'zir for bestiality (not hadd).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what happens to an animal (whose meat is eaten) that is subjected to bestiality by its owner?
A) It is slaughtered and may be eaten by anyone.
B) It is slaughtered and burned.
C) It is not slaughtered but kept alive.
D) It is given to the owner without slaughter.

Key Takeaway
Bestiality carries no hadd in the Hanafi school; the perpetrator gets ta'zir, and the animal is slaughtered—its disposal depends on the type of meat and ownership, with a dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Hadd for Musta'min in Zina: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on a musta'min (harbi with aman) committing zina, intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) on whether a musta'min is subject to hadd for zina and explain the underlying rationale for each.

Core Idea
A musta'min's aman limits his criminal liability: no hadd for zina on him, but the woman is punished.

In this lesson, we examine a classic intra-Hanafi dispute about the extent of a musta'min's liability under Islamic criminal law. The source text from *Kanz al-Daqa'iq* presents the three positions of the founding imams regarding zina committed by a musta'min with a dhimmi or muslim woman. Understanding this dispute clarifies how the Hanafi school balances the aman contract with the enforcement of hudud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and parties
Recognize that the act is zina by a musta'min (harbi with aman) with a dhimmi or muslima in dar al-Islam.
The musta'min is a non-Muslim from enemy territory granted temporary safe passage.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and dalil
Abu Hanifa: hadd on the woman, not on the musta'min. His dalil: actual zina is found from her; the musta'min's aman blocks liability.
This is the mufta bihi view.
3
State Abu Yusuf's position and dalil
Abu Yusuf: both are subject to hadd, because the musta'min accepted Islamic rulings by entering with aman (except for wine).
He analogizes the musta'min to a dhimmi regarding criminal liability.
4
State Muhammad's position and dalil
Muhammad: neither is subject to hadd. If the man's hadd drops, the woman's also drops because she is a dependent (tabi') in the act.
This view is not relied upon.
5
Consider the opposite case
If a dhimmi or muslim commits zina with a musta'mina, the dhimmi/muslim is subject to hadd, but the musta'mina is not (except by Abu Yusuf). This shows consistency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبزنا حربي أي لا يحد حربي مستأمن بالزنا بذمية أو مسلمة. (ط) بذمية في حقه [ أي لا يجب الحد في حق الحربي وحدت الذمية أو المسلمة. (عيني)] أي إذا دخل الحربي دارنا بأمان فزنى بذمية أو زنى مسلمة فلا يجب الحد في حق الحربي المستأمن وأما الذمية والمسلمة فتحدان هذا عند أبي حنيفة وعند أبي يوسف: يحد المستأمن أيضاً، وعند محمد: لا يحد واحد منهما، ولو كان بالعكس بأن زنى ذمي أو مسلم بمستأمنة يحد الذمي والمسلم دون المستأمنة عند الطرفين، وعند أبي يوسف تحد المستأمنة أيضاً؛ لأن المستأمن التزم أحكامنا في دارنا فيحد إلا في شرب الخمر؛ لأنه لا يعتقد حرمتها ولمحمد أن الحد سقط في حق الأصل، أي الرجل فأوجب سقوطه في التبع أي المرأة، ولأبي حنيفة أنه وجد حقيقة الزنا منها، فتحد خاصة. (مستخلص، عيني)
And by zina of a harbi: i.e., a harbi musta'min (one who has aman) is not subject to hadd for zina with a dhimmi or a muslima. By a dhimmi in his right: i.e., hadd is not obligatory on the harbi, and the dhimmi or muslima is subject to hadd. That is, if a harbi enters our territory with aman and commits zina with a dhimmi or a muslima, then hadd is not obligatory on the harbi musta'min. As for the dhimmi and muslima, they are subject to hadd. This is according to Abu Hanifa. According to Abu Yusuf: the musta'min is also subject to hadd. According to Muhammad: neither of them is subject to hadd. And if it were the opposite, that a dhimmi or a muslim commits zina with a musta'mina, then the dhimmi and the muslim are subject to hadd, not the musta'mina, according to both (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). According to Abu Yusuf: the musta'mina is also subject to hadd, because the musta'min has committed to our rulings in our territory, so he is subject to hadd, except for drinking wine because he does not believe it is prohibited. And for Muhammad: the hadd dropped for the original (the man) so it causes dropping for the dependent (the woman). And for Abu Hanifa: actual zina is found from her, so she is subject to hadd specifically.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a musta'min (a non-Muslim from enemy territory who has been granted aman) who commits zina with a dhimmi or a muslima in dar al-Islam. According to Abu Hanifa, the musta'min is not subject to hadd (because his criminal liability is limited by the aman), but the woman (dhimmi or muslima) is subject to hadd. Abu Yusuf says the musta'min is also subject to hadd because he has accepted the protection of Islamic law. Muhammad says neither is subject to hadd: the musta'min because he is not fully bound, and the woman because the act is not considered valid zina against her? Actually, Muhammad's reasoning: if the man's hadd is dropped, then the woman's is also dropped because she is a dependent in the act. Abu Hanifa counters that the woman committed actual zina, so she is punished. The opposite case (dhimmi or muslim with musta'mina) is also discussed: the dhimmi/muslim is subject to hadd, and the musta'mina is not according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad; Abu Yusuf also subjects her. The exception for wine is noted: a musta'min is not punished for drinking because he may not believe it is haram.

Key Terms
مستأمن (musta'min): A non-Muslim from dar al-harb who enters dar al-Islam with a temporary safe passage (aman).
ذمية (dhimmī): A non-Muslim (usually Christian or Jew) living permanently under Muslim rule with a contract of protection (dhimma).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what happens to a musta'min (non-Muslim with aman) who commits zina with a muslim woman in dar al-Islam?
A) Both are subject to hadd.
B) Neither is subject to hadd.
C) The musta'min is subject to hadd, but the woman is not.
D) The woman is subject to hadd, but the musta'min is not.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a musta'min's aman prevents the application of hadd for zina to him, but the woman (whether dhimmi or muslima) remains subject to hadd.

8 min
Ruling on Bestiality: No Hadd, Only Ta'zir
Ruling on bestiality: no hadd but ta'zir, and fate of the animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bestiality and distinguish it from the hadd of zina, and explain the fate of the animal and the disagreements among scholars.

Core Idea
Bestiality carries no hadd—only ta'zir—because it lacks the core elements of zina.

This lesson examines a controversial topic in Islamic criminal law: bestiality. While the act is unanimously haram, the schools differ on its punishment. The Hanafi school distinguishes it from zina and imposes only a discretionary punishment (ta'zir). The passage also details the fate of the animal and the disagreements among the Hanafi imams themselves.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling: no hadd for bestiality
The text clearly states that the hadd of stoning is not applied. Only ta'zir (discretionary punishment) is given.
Hadd is a fixed punishment; ta'zir is left to the judge's discretion.
2
Understand the reasoning: why not analogous to zina
Bestiality lacks the key elements of zina: procreation, confusion of lineage, and natural mutual desire. Therefore, it is not considered equivalent.
The text says 'ليس في معنى الزنا في كونه جناية وفي وجود الداعي' – not like zina in transgression and desire.
3
Note the consensus on ta'zir and disagreement of other schools
All Hanafi jurists agree on ta'zir, but the three other imams (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) hold that the hadd of zina applies. This is an ikhtilaf.
The text says 'وعن الثلاثة يحد' – from the three, the hadd is applied.
4
Examine the fate of the animal: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Abu Hanifa's later view: if the animal is halal, it is slaughtered and eaten; if not halal, it is slaughtered and burned. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say the animal is burned in both cases.
The text says at Abu Hanifa 'حاله' (his later view), indicating a change of position.
5
Recognize that burning is not obligatory but recommended
Burning is done to prevent people from talking about the incident, based on the action of Ali (RA). It is wajib only in the sense of a recommended measure.
The text says 'الإحراق ليس بواجب عندنا' – burning is not obligatory according to us.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وببهيمة أي ولا يحد أيضا بوطء بهيمة؛ لأنه ليس في معنى الزنا في كونه جناية وفي وجود الداعي؛ لأن الطبع السليم يتنفر عنه والحامل عليه غاية السفه أو فرط السبق فلا يجب الحد ولكنه يعزر بالإجماع، وعن الثلاثة يحد ثم إن كانت الدابة مما لا يؤكل لحمها تذبح ،وتحرق وإن كانت مما تؤكل تذبح وتؤكل عند أبي حنيفة حاله، وقالا تحرق هذه أيضاً هذا إذا كانت البهيمة للفاعل، وإن كانت لغيره ضمن الفاعل قيمتها لصاحبها ثم تذبح، وعن الشافعي: لو كانت مما يؤكل تذبح، وعليه قيمتها لو لغيره، ويأكل منها غيره لا هو، وعن مالك: يأكل هو منها أيضاً، وعنه: لا تذبح بحال يعني سواء كانت له أو لغيره، وعن أحمد: لا يأكل هو ولا غيره. [رمز الحقائق: ۳۸۳/۱] ثم إن الإحراق ليس بواجب عندنا وإنما يفعل لقطع التحدث به إذا كانت البهيمة باقية ولما روي عن علي له أنه أمر بذبح هذه البهيمة وحرقها بعد ذبحها. (مستخلص)
And [the section on] bestiality: i.e., he is not stoned [i.e., given the hadd punishment] also for intercourse with an animal because it is not comparable to zina in being a transgression and in the existence of desire; for a sound nature recoils from it, and what drives one to it is extreme foolishness or excessive haste, so the hadd is not obligatory, but he is given a discretionary punishment by consensus. And from the three [imams] that he is given the hadd. Then if the animal is of a type whose meat is not eaten, it is slaughtered and burned; if it is of a type whose meat is eaten, it is slaughtered and eaten according to Abu Hanifa in his [later] view, and the two companions [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] said this one is also burned. This applies if the animal belongs to the perpetrator; if it belongs to another, the perpetrator guarantees its value to its owner, then it is slaughtered. And from al-Shafi'i: if it is of a type whose meat is eaten, it is slaughtered, and he [the perpetrator] owes its value if it belongs to another, and others eat from it but not him. From Malik: he may eat from it as well, and also from him: it is not slaughtered at all, meaning whether it is his or another's. From Ahmad: neither he nor others eat. [Rumuz al-Haqa'iq: 383/1] Then burning is not obligatory according to us; it is done only to prevent people talking about it if the animal remains, and due to what was narrated from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) that he ordered the slaughter of such an animal and its burning after slaughter. (Mukhtalaf)
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on bestiality (wat' al-bahimah). It begins by stating that there is no hadd (prescribed punishment) for this act, because it is not analogous to zina: zina involves procreation, confusion of lineage, and corruption of the marital bed, which do not exist here, and natural desire is absent in one party, so it is far rarer. Therefore, the Hanafi school imposes only ta'zir (discretionary punishment) by consensus of the companions. However, the three other imams (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) hold that the hadd of zina applies. The passage then addresses the fate of the animal. According to Abu Hanifa's later view, if the animal is halal to eat, it is slaughtered and can be eaten (by the owner? actually by others, not the perpetrator); if it is not halal, it is slaughtered and burned. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it is burned either way. If the animal belongs to another person, the perpetrator must pay its value to the owner, then it is slaughtered. Views of Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad are mentioned for comparison. Finally, it notes that burning is not obligatory (wajib) but is done as a social measure to prevent people from talking; this is supported by the narration of Ali commanding slaughter and burning.

Key Terms
الحد (al-hadd): The prescribed corporal punishment for specific crimes (zina, theft, etc.).
التعزير (al-ta'zir): Discretionary punishment left to the judge's ijtihad, not fixed in the Quran or Sunnah.
البهيمة (al-bahimah): Any dumb animal; in this context, the animal that was copulated with.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what punishment is given for bestiality?
A) The hadd punishment of stoning
B) The hadd punishment of lashing
C) Discretionary punishment (ta'zir)
D) No punishment at all

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, bestiality is punished by ta'zir, not hadd, due to its lack of analogy to zina, and the animal's fate depends on its edibility and ownership.

No Hadd for Zina in Enemy Territory
Ruling on zina committed in enemy territory and enforcement after leaving

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hadd for zina in dar al-harb and explain the evidence from the hadith and the principle of jurisdiction.

Core Idea
No hadd for zina in enemy territory because the imam's authority is severed and the act did not obligate punishment at inception.

This passage addresses a nuanced case: a Muslim commits zina in enemy territory (dar al-harb) or rebel territory (dar al-baghy) and then comes to Muslim lands. Should the hadd be enforced? The Hanafi school says no, based on a specific hadith and a legal principle that the obligation of punishment does not arise if the imam lacks jurisdiction at the time of the act. The Shafi'i school, along with Malik and Ahmad, disagrees. Understanding this ruling requires grasping the relationship between jurisdiction, the purpose of hadd, and how a ruling can or cannot 'revive' after the fact.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is zina committed by a Muslim in dar al-harb or dar al-baghy. The ruling is that the hadd (stoning or flogging) is not enforced on him after he leaves that territory and enters dar al-Islam.
The ruling applies only if the person was under the jurisdiction of the imam at the time of the act.
2
Locate the Hanafi proof
The text cites two proofs: a direct hadith, 'La tuqamu al-hudud fi dar al-harb' (Hudud are not established in enemy territory), and a rational argument that because the purpose of hadd is deterrence, and the imam's authority (wilaya) is absent there, the obligation to enforce the hadd does not arise.
The rational argument reinforces the textual proof.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof proves the ruling)
The hadith explicitly forbids establishing hudud in dar al-harb, so the hadd cannot be applied there. The rational argument adds that the act at its inception (ibtaada') did not obligate the hadd because the imam could not enforce it; therefore, later entry into dar al-Islam does not revive the obligation, as something that did not exist cannot come into being later.
This reasoning mirrors the principle 'ma lam yan'aqid fi al-ibtida' la yanqalib fi al-intiha'.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (disagreement)
Imam al-Shafi'i, along with Malik and Ahmad, hold that the hadd must be enforced because a Muslim is always bound by Islamic law wherever he is. They rely on the general obligation of hadd for zina.
The Hanafi response distinguishes between the obligation upon the individual to abstain from zina and the duty of the imam to enforce punishment.
5
Consider the exception for commanders with direct authority
The text notes that if the caliph or a provincial governor (amir al-misr) personally resolves to enforce the hadd on a soldier in his own camp, he may do so because his authority extends over that camp. This does not apply to lower-ranking officers who have not been delegated enforcement authority.
This shows that the ruling is about the imam's jurisdiction, not a blanket exemption for any Muslim in enemy territory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبزنا في دار الحرب أي من زنا في دار الحرب أو في دار البغي ثم خرج إلينا لا يقام عليه الحد عندنا، وقال الشافعي: يحد؛ لأن المسلم ملتزم أحكام الإسلام أين كان مقامه، وبه قال مالك وأحمد، ولنا: قوله عليه: "لا تقام الحدود في دار الحرب"؛ ولأن المقصود هو الانزجار وولاية الإمام منقطعة عنهما فيعري الوجوب عن ولا يقام بعد ما خرج؛ لأن الفعل لما لم ينعقد في الابتداء موجباً فلا ينقلب موجباً في الانتهاء ولو عزم من له ولاية الإقامة بنفسه كالخليفة وأمير المصر يقيم الحد على من زنا من عسكره؛ لأن العسكر تحت يده بخلاف أمير العسكر والسرية؛ لأنه لم يفوض إليهما الإقامة. (عيني، مص)
And [the section on] zina in dar al-harb: i.e., whoever commits zina in enemy territory or in a rebel territory then comes out to us, the hadd is not established upon him according to us. Al-Shafi'i said: he is stoned because the Muslim is bound by the rulings of Islam wherever he is, and Malik and Ahmad said the same. Our proof: His statement (peace be upon him): 'The hudud are not established in dar al-harb'; and because the goal is deterrence and the imam's authority is severed from them, so the obligation becomes devoid. And it is not established after he leaves because the act did not bring about [the hadd] at its inception, so it does not become obligating at the end. If someone who himself has the authority of execution, like the caliph or the governor of a province, resolves [to enforce], he may establish the hadd on one of his army who committed zina; because the army is under his hand, unlike a battalion commander or a raiding party, because enforcement has not been delegated to them. (Ayni, Misbah)
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage discusses zina committed in dar al-harb (enemy territory) or dar al-baghy (rebel territory). The Hanafi position is that the hadd punishment is not enforced on the person after he leaves that territory, because the act did not immediately obligate the hadd due to the absence of the imam's authority. The Shafi'i school (with Malik and Ahmad) holds that the hadd should be applied because the Muslim is obligated to Islamic law everywhere. The Hanafi proof is a hadith: 'The hudud are not established in dar al-harb.' Additionally, the purpose of hadd is deterrence, and if the imam cannot enforce it at the time, it is not later revived. However, if the caliph or a regional amir has authority over his own camp (e.g., an army), he can enforce it within that camp.

Key Terms
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): Territory under enemy (non-Muslim) control where Muslims may be present but the imam lacks authority.
دار البغي (dar al-baghy): Territory controlled by rebels (bughat) who have a ta'wil (interpretation) for their rebellion.
ولاية الإمام (wilayat al-imam): The authority (jurisdiction) of the imam (supreme leader) to implement Islamic legal punishments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary textual proof cited by the Hanafi school for not enforcing hadd for zina committed in dar al-harb?
A) Qiyas on apostasy
B) A hadith: 'La tuqamu al-hudud fi dar al-harb'
C) The consensus of the companions
D) The principle that Islamic law applies only in dar al-Islam

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school does not enforce hadd for zina in enemy territory because the imam's jurisdiction is absent and the obligation does not revive later.

Hadd for a Harbi Musta'man Who Commits Zina
Intra-Hanafi dispute on hadd for a harbi musta'man who commits zina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the hadd for a harbi musta'man who commits zina and explain the underlying reasoning (ta'lil) for each position.

Core Idea
A musta'man's zina triggers differing hadd rulings because the extent of his submission to Islamic jurisdiction is debated by the three Hanafi Imams.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq examines an intra-Hanafi dispute: when a harbi musta'man commits zina with a Muslim or dhimmi woman, should the hadd be applied to him? Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani each present a distinct position based on their understanding of the musta'man's legal status in Dar al-Islam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and act
Clarify that the case involves a musta'man (enemy non-Muslim with safe conduct) who commits zina with a Muslim or dhimmi woman in Muslim territory.
2
State each imam's ruling
List the three rulings concisely: Abu Hanifa – man not stoned, woman stoned; Abu Yusuf – both stoned; Muhammad – neither stoned.
Also note the reverse case (dhimmi/Muslim man with musta'mana woman).
3
Examine each imam's ta'lil (reasoning)
From the text: Abu Hanifa views the woman as independently guilty; Abu Yusuf emphasizes the musta'man's commitment to our laws; Muhammad sees the woman's hadd as dependent on the man's.
Compare the arguments for the reverse case as well.
4
Compare the reverse case
When a dhimmi or Muslim man commits zina with a musta'mana woman, the men are stoned but the woman is not according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad; Abu Yusuf stones the woman too.
This symmetry reveals each imam's consistent principle.
5
Synthesize the jurisprudential principle
The dispute centers on whether the musta'man is fully subject to Islamic criminal law and whether the woman's hadd is dependent on the man's.
This reflects broader Hanafi methodology of weighing jurisdiction and dependency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبزنا حربي أي لا يحد حربي مستأمن بالزنا بذمية أو مسلمة. (ط) بذمية في حقه [ أي لا يجب الحد في حق الحربي وحدت الذمية أو المسلمة. (عيني)] أي إذا دخل الحربي دارنا بأمان فزنى بذمية أو زنى مسلمة فلا يجب الحد في حق الحربي المستأمن وأما الذمية والمسلمة فتحدان هذا عند أبي حنيفة وعند أبي يوسف: يحد المستأمن أيضاً، وعند محمد: لا يحد واحد منهما، ولو كان بالعكس بأن زنى ذمي أو مسلم بمستأمنة يحد الذمي والمسلم دون المستأمنة عند الطرفين، وعند أبي يوسف تحد المستأمنة أيضاً؛ لأن المستأمن التزم أحكامنا في دارنا فيحد إلا في شرب الخمر؛ لأنه لا يعتقد حرمتها ولمحمد أن الحد سقط في حق الأصل، أي الرجل فأوجب سقوطه في التبع أي المرأة، ولأبي حنيفة أنه وجد حقيقة الزنا منها، فتحد خاصة. (مستخلص، عيني)
And [the section on] zina of a harbi: i.e., a harbi musta'man (protected person) is not stoned for zina with a dhimmi or Muslim woman. (T) [It is said: the hadd is not obligatory on the harbi, and the dhimmi or Muslim woman is stoned. (Ayni)] That is, if a harbi enters our territory under safe conduct and commits zina with a dhimmi woman or a Muslim woman, the hadd is not obligatory on the harbi musta'man. As for the dhimmi or Muslim woman, they are stoned. This is according to Abu Hanifa. According to Abu Yusuf: the musta'man is also stoned. According to Muhammad: neither of them is stoned. If the reverse occurs, that a dhimmi or Muslim commits zina with a musta'mana woman, the dhimmi and Muslim are stoned but not the musta'mana, according to both [Abu Hanifa and Muhammad?], and according to Abu Yusuf, the musta'mana is also stoned. Because the musta'man is committed to our laws in our territory, so he is stoned, except for drinking wine because he does not believe in its prohibition. And according to Muhammad, the hadd fell from the origin, i.e., the man, so it necessitates its falling from the dependent, i.e., the woman. And according to Abu Hanifa, she has committed actual zina, so she is stoned uniquely. (Mukhtasar, Ayni)
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a harbi (enemy non-Muslim) who enters Muslim territory with aman (safe conduct) and then commits zina with either a Muslim woman or a dhimmi woman. Abu Hanifa rules that the harbi man is not subject to hadd, but the woman (whether Muslim or dhimmi) is. Abu Yusuf holds the harbi must also be stoned because he has accepted our laws while here, except for drinking wine which he does not consider haram. Muhammad al-Shaybani holds neither is stoned because the hadd falls from the man (the primary) and thus also from the woman (the dependent). If the roles are reversed (a dhimmi or Muslim man with a musta'mana woman), the men are stoned but the woman is not according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad; Abu Yusuf stoned the woman as well. The underlying reasoning: Abu Yusuf emphasizes submission to jurisdiction; Muhammad sees the woman's share as dependent on the man's; Abu Hanifa sees the woman as independently guilty.

Key Terms
حربي مستأمن (harbi musta'man): An enemy non-Muslim who enters Muslim territory with a pledge of safe conduct (aman).
ذمية (dhimmi): A non-Muslim living permanently under Muslim rule with a covenant (dhimma).
مستأمنة (musta'mana): A female musta'man.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Neither is stoned
C) The woman is stoned, the man is not
D) The man is stoned, the woman is not

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the application of the hadd for zina to a harbi musta'man is disputed among the three Imams, reflecting differing views on the extent of the musta'man's submission to Islamic criminal law and the dependency of the woman's hadd on the man's.

Zina by a Minor or Insane Person: Hadd and Capacity
Ruling on hadd when a minor/insane commits zina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hadd when a minor or insane person commits zina with a sane adult, explain the school's proof, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute with Zufar.

Core Idea
No hadd on either party when a minor or insane person is the active participant in zina.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the chapter of hudud: the case where a minor boy or an insane man commits zina with a sane, adult woman. While there is consensus that hadd is not applied to the minor or insane person, a dispute arises regarding the woman. The Hanafi school, following Abu Hanifa, argues that she is also exempt, whereas Zufar (a Hanafi student) and the other three imams hold that she must receive the hadd. Understanding the reasoning behind this difference sharpens your ability to apply principles of legal capacity (ahliyyah) and the definition of zina in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two cases: (1) a minor/insane person commits zina with a sane adult woman, (2) the reverse: a sane adult man commits zina with a minor girl or insane woman. Note the ruling for each.
Focus on the first case as it is disputed.
2
State the consensus and the point of dispute
By consensus (ijma'), no hadd is applied to the minor or insane person. The dispute is solely about whether the sane adult woman receives hadd.
Zufar and the three imams (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) say she does; Abu Hanifa says she does not.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof (dalil aqli)
The Hanafi argument: zina is defined as an act by a person who is legally addressed (mukhatab) with the prohibition (kaf). The minor and insane lack such addressability, so their act is not legally considered zina. Therefore, the act cannot be a cause for hadd for either participant.
This is a rational (aqli) reasoning rooted in the concept of legal capacity (ahliyyat al-wujub/al-ada).
4
Understand the opposing proof
Zufar and others argue that each person is accountable for their own actions. The woman is an adult and willingly participated; her lack of hadd on the minor should not absolve her. They see the act as zina on her part.
They view the act as zina because she is a capable adult; her partner's incapacity does not change her own action.
5
Contrast with the reverse case
If a sane adult man commits zina with a minor girl or insane woman, he receives the hadd by consensus. This is because he is fully responsible and the act is considered zina from his side.
The ruling is consistent: the capable party bears the hadd when acting with an incapable party.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبزنا صبي إلخ: أي إذا زنا صبي أو مجنون بامرأة عاقلة بالغة فلا حد على الصبي والمجنون بالإجماع، ولا تحد المرأة أيضاً عندنا، وقال زفر والثلاثة: يجب عليها الحد؛ لأن امتناع الحد على المطاوع له لا يخل في حقها؛ لأن كلاً منهما مؤاخذ بفعله، ولنا: أن الزنا فعل من هو مخاطب بالكف، وفعل الصبي والمجنون ليس بهذه الصفة، فلا يكون موجباً للحد، وقوله: بخلاف عكسه" وهو ما إذا زنى العاقل البالغ بصبية أو مجنونة حيث يجب الحد على الرجل بالاتفاق. (مستخلص عيني بخلاف عكسه: أي لو زنى عاقل بالغ بمحبوبته أو صبية يجامع مثلها حد الرجل خاصة إجماعاً. (عيني)
And [the section on] zina of a minor or insane person, etc.: i.e., if a minor or an insane person commits zina with a sane, adult woman, there is no hadd on the minor and the insane by consensus, and the woman is also not stoned according to us. Zufar and the three [imams] said: the hadd is obligatory on her, because the prevention of the hadd on the one who submitted to him does not invalidate [it] in her right, because each of them is accountable for his action. Our proof: zina is the action of one who is addressed with prohibition, and the action of the minor and the insane does not have this description, so it does not become a cause for the hadd. And his statement: 'unlike the reverse', which is if a sane adult commits zina with a girl or a insane woman, the hadd is obligatory on the man by agreement. (Mukhtasar, Ayni: 'unlike the reverse': i.e., if a sane adult commits zina with his beloved or a girl who is like that in being able to be copulated with, the hadd is on the man alone by consensus.)
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling when a minor boy or an insane man commits zina with a sane adult woman. By consensus (ijma'), no hadd is applied to the minor or insane person. However, the Hanafi school also exempts the woman from hadd, whereas Zufar (a Hanafi student) and the three other imams (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) hold that the woman must receive the hadd because she is a legally responsible adult who committed zina with her consent. The Hanafi argument is that zina is defined as an act by a person who is obligated to refrain (mukhatab bi al-kaf), and since the minor/insane is not so obligated, the act does not legally constitute zina that would lead to hadd for either party. The woman's participation with such a person is not legally considered zina. Conversely, if a sane adult man commits zina with a minor girl or insane woman, he receives the hadd by consensus.

Key Terms
الصبي (al-sabi): A male minor who has not reached puberty.
المجنون (al-majnun): An insane person who lacks legal capacity.
مخاطب بالكف (mukhatab bi al-kaf): A person who is addressed by the Law to refrain from an act; i.e., someone with legal capacity (mukallaf).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a minor boy (pre-pubescent) commits zina with an adult woman, what is the ruling on the woman?
A) She must be stoned to death.
B) She must receive 100 lashes.
C) She does not receive any hadd punishment.
D) She receives ta'zir only.

Key Takeaway
Hadd for zina requires both parties to be legally responsible (mukhatab); when one lacks capacity, the act is not zina, and no hadd is imposed on either.

Hadd for Zina with a Hired Woman (Musta'jarah)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on hadd for hiring a woman for zina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on hadd for zina with a hired woman and explain why Abu Hanifa's view differs from the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Payment for zina creates a shubha that averts hadd; without condition, hadd applies.

This lesson examines a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute: if a man hires a woman for the explicit purpose of zina, does the hadd punishment apply? Abu Hanifa holds that the payment creates a shubha (doubt) that blocks the hadd, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) insist that the lack of any lawful connection makes it pure zina. We will follow the proofs and the practical distinction that settles the matter.

Guided Path
1
State Abu Hanifa's position
Identify the ruling: no hadd for the man when he hires a woman for zina. Note the key factor: payment creates a shubha.
Shubha is any semblance of legal connection.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's objection
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad argue that hadd must apply because there is no ownership or semblance of ownership between the parties, making it pure zina.
The Sahibayn are joined by the three other imams (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali).
3
Analyse Abu Hanifa's evidence
Examine the Quranic verse (al-Ma'idah 5:5) where mahr is called 'ujrah' (wage) and the narration about Umar treating such payment as mahr. This creates an analogy that the payment, though for zina, resembles a dower.
The dalil is the verse's use of 'ujoorunna' (their wages) for mahr.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, the man avoids hadd; under the Sahibayn, he receives the full hadd punishment.
This difference is critical in a hudud case.
5
Note the agreed-upon scenario
If the woman is hired for lawful service and then zina occurs without explicit condition, hadd applies by consensus. Also if payment is given without stipulating access, hadd applies.
The dispute is only when payment is explicitly conditioned on sexual access.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبالزنا بمستأجرة: أي إذا استأجر امرأة ليزني بها فوطئها لا يجب الحد عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما: يجب الحد؛ لأن ليس بينهما ملك ولا شبهة ملك، فكان زناً محضاً ، وبه قالت الثلاثة، وله ما روي أن امرأة طلبت من رجل مالا فأبى أن يعطيها . تمكنه حتى ه الحد عنهما، وقال: "هذا مهرها ، ولأنه تعالى سمى المهر أجرة نفسها، فدراً عمر من بقوله تعالى: إِذَا آتَيْتُمُوهُنَّ أُجُورَهُنَّ (المائدة:٥)، فصارت شبهة، ولهذا لو قال: أمهرتك كذا لأزني بك لم يجب الحد فكذا إذا قال: استأجرتك أو خذي هذا لأطأك أو مكنيني نفسك بكذا. رمز الحقائق: ٣٨٤/١] ولو استأجرها للخدمة فزنى بها يجب الحد بلا خلاف، والحاصل أن الخلاف فيما إذا أعطاها مالاً واشترط التمكين، أما إذا أعطاها مالاً ولم يشترط ثم جامعها يحد إجماعاً. (مستخلص، فتح)
And [the section on] zina with a hired woman: i.e., if someone hires a woman to commit zina with her then has intercourse, the hadd is not obligatory according to Abu Hanifa. According to the two companions: the hadd is obligatory because there is no ownership nor semblance of ownership between them, so it is pure zina, and the three [others] said the same. And for him [Abu Hanifa] is what was narrated: that a woman asked a man for money and he refused to give it to her until she let him take [؟] and he said 'this is her mahr'. And because the Exalted called the mahr 'ujrah' (wage) in His saying: 'When you give them their wages [ujoorahunna]' (al-Ma'idah:5), so it becomes a doubt (shubha). Therefore, if he said: 'I pay you mahr such and such for zina with you,' the hadd is not obligatory. Similarly if he said: 'I hire you' or 'take this so I may have intercourse with you' or 'let me have you for such.' (Rumuz al-Haqa'iq: 384/1) And if he hired her for service and then committed zina, the hadd is obligatory without dispute. The conclusion: the dispute is when he gave money and stipulated access; if he gave money without stipulation and then had intercourse, he is stoned by consensus. (Mukhtasar, Fath)
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage deals with the situation of hiring a woman for the purpose of zina (i.e., prostitution arrangement). Abu Hanifa holds that there is no hadd punishment for the man, because the payment (whether called mahr or ujrah) creates a doubt (shubha) that prevents the application of hadd. This is supported by a narration about Umar (?) who treated such payment as mahr, and by the Quranic verse (5:5) which uses the word 'ujoor' for mahr, drawing an analogy. Thus, if the transaction is explicitly for zina, the hadd is lifted. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) along with the three other imams say the hadd applies because there is no ownership or semblance of ownership. If the woman is hired for lawful service and then zina occurs without additional stipulation, the hadd is applied by consensus. The key distinction is whether the payment was specifically conditioned upon sexual access.

Key Terms
المستأجرة (al-musta'jarah): A woman hired, in this context, for the purpose of sexual intercourse.
الشبهة (al-shubha): A legal doubt that prevents the application of hadd punishments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (mufta bihi), if a man explicitly hires a woman for the act of zina, is the hadd punishment applied?
A) Yes, because it is pure zina
B) No, because the payment creates a doubt (shubha)
C) Only if the woman is also punished
D) Yes, because hiring for zina is invalid

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, any semblance of lawful connection (shubha) created by payment can avert the hadd punishment for zina, but only when the payment is explicitly conditioned on sexual access.
